\hline Quadrant & Signs of ratios & Remember \\
\hline I & All are +ve & All \\
\hline II & $\operatorname{Sin} \theta$ and $\operatorname{cosec} \theta=\frac{1}{\sin \theta}$ are +ve; Other ratios are -ve . & Silver \\
\hline III & $\tan \theta$ and $\cot \theta$ are +ve ; other ratios are - ve. & Tea \\
\hline IV & $\cos \theta$ and $\sec \theta=\frac{1}{\cos \theta}$ are +ve ; other ratios are -ve . & Cups \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

Table 3.11

\section*{Trigonometrical ratios of related or allied Angles:}

The basic angle is $\theta$ and angles associated with $\theta$ by a right angle (or) its multiples are called related angle or allied angles. Thus $90 \pm \theta, 180 \pm \theta, 270 \pm \theta, 360 \pm \theta$ are known as related or allied angles.

\section*{Trigonometrical ratios of any Angle}

Working Rule for $180 \pm \theta$ and $360 \pm \theta$
1. Determine the sign.
2. Change of ratio-Do not change

Refer Fig.3.12
\begin{tabular}{|l|l|l|l|}
\hline Ratio $180^{\circ}$ (or) $360^{\circ}$ & Falls in Quadrant Refer Fig.3.12 & Sign Refer Table 3.11 & Change of ratio (Do not change) \\
\hline 1) $\sin (180-\theta)$ & II (Silver) & $\sin \theta$ is +ve & $+\sin \theta$ \\
\hline 2) $\tan (180+\theta)$ & III (Tea) & $\tan \theta$ is +ve & $+\tan \theta$ \\
\hline 3) $\sec (360-\theta)$ & IV (Cups) & $\sec \theta$ is +ve & $+\sec \theta$ \\
\hline 4) $\tan (180-\theta)$ & II (Silver) & $\tan \theta$ is - ve & $-\tan \theta$ \\
\hline 5) $\cos (180+\theta)$ & III (Tea) & $\cos \theta$ is - ve & $-\cos \theta$ \\
\hline 6) $\operatorname{cosec}(360-\theta)$ & IV (Cups) & $\operatorname{cosec} \theta$ is - ve & $-\operatorname{cosec} \theta$ \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

\section*{Working Rule for $90 \pm \boldsymbol{\theta}$ and $270 \pm \boldsymbol{\theta}$}
1. Determine the sign
2. Change of ratio as follows:
$\sin \theta$ will change as $\cos \theta$ and $\cos \theta$ will change as $\sin \theta$
$\tan \theta$ will change as $\cot \theta$ and $\cot \theta$ will change as $\tan \theta$
$\sec \theta$ will change as $\operatorname{cosec} \theta$ and $\operatorname{cosec} \theta$ will change as $\sec \theta$
\begin{tabular}{|l|l|l|l|}
\hline Ratio $\mathbf{9 0}^{\circ}$ (or) $\mathbf{2 7 0}{ }^{\circ}$ & Refer Fig. 3.12 Quadrant & Referable 3.11 Sign & Change of ratio \\
\hline 1) $\sin (90-\theta)$ & I (All) & $\sin \theta$ is +ve & $+\cos \theta$ \\
\hline 2) $\operatorname{cosec}(90+\theta)$ & II (Silver) & $\operatorname{cosec} \theta$ is +ve & $+\sec \theta$ \\
\hline 3) $\cot (270-\theta)$ & III (Tea) & $\cot \theta$ is +ve & $+\tan \theta$ \\
\hline 4) $\sin (270+\theta)$ & IV (Cups) & $\sin \theta$ is - ve & $-\cos \theta$ \\
\hline 5) $\tan (270+\theta)$ & IV (Cups) & $\tan \theta$ is - ve & $-\cot \theta$ \\
\hline 6) $\cos (270-\theta)$ & III (Tea) & $\cos \theta$ is - ve & $-\sin \theta$ \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

\section*{Examples:}
1) $\sin 180^{\circ}=\sin \left(180^{\text {III }}+0\right)=-\sin 0^{\circ}=0$
2) $\cos 180^{\circ}=\cos \left(180^{\text {III }}+0\right)=-\cos 0^{\circ}=-1$
3) $\tan 225^{\circ}=\tan (180+45)=+\tan 45^{\circ}=1$
4) $\sin 120^{\circ}=\sin \left(180^{\text {II }}-60\right)=+\sin 60^{\circ}=\frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}$
5) $\cos 120^{\circ}=\cos (180-60)=-\cos 60^{\circ}=-\frac{1}{2}$
6) $\cot 210=\cot (180+30)=+\cot 30^{\circ}=\frac{1}{\left(\frac{1}{\sqrt{3}}\right)}=\sqrt{3}$
7) $\left.\begin{array}{rl}\sin 270^{\circ} & =\sin \left(180^{\text {III }}+90\right)=-\sin 90^{\circ}=-1 \\ & =\sin \left(270^{\text {IV }}+0\right)=-\cos 0=-1\end{array}\right\}$
8) $\left.\begin{array}{rl}\cos 240 & =\cos (180+60)=-\cos 60=-\frac{1}{2} \\ & =\cos (270-30)=-\sin 30=-\frac{1}{2}\end{array}\right\}$
9) $\underset{\text { (Remove multiangles of } 360^{\circ} \text { ) }}{\sin 600}=\sin 240=\sin (180+60)=-\sin 60=-\frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}$
10) $\underset{\text { (Remove multiangles of } 360^{\circ} \text { ) }}{\cos 720}=\cos 0=1$

\section*{Note:}
$-\theta$ falls in Quadrant IV where $\cos \theta$ and $\sec \theta$ are + ve. Therefore $\cos (-\theta)=\cos \theta$ and $\sec (-\theta)=$ $\sec \theta ; \sin (-\theta)=-\sin \theta ; \tan (-\theta)=-\tan \theta ; \cot (-\theta)=-\cot \theta ; \operatorname{cosec}(-\theta)=-\operatorname{cosec} \theta$.

\section*{Compound Angles:}

If an angle is expressed as the algebraic sum or difference of two or more angles, then it is called compound angle.

\section*{Formulae:}
1) $\sin (A+B)=\sin A \cos B+\cos A \sin B$
2) $\sin (A-B)=\sin A \cos B-\cos A \sin B$
3) $\cos (A+B)=\cos A \cos B-\sin A \sin B$
4) $\cos (\mathrm{A}-\mathrm{B})=\cos \mathrm{A} \cos \mathrm{B}+\sin \mathrm{A} \sin \mathrm{B}$
5) $\tan (\mathrm{A}+\mathrm{B})=\frac{\tan \mathrm{A}+\tan \mathrm{B}}{1-\tan \mathrm{A} \tan \mathrm{B}}$
6) $\tan (\mathrm{A}-\mathrm{B})=\frac{\tan \mathrm{A}-\tan \mathrm{B}}{1+\tan \mathrm{A} \tan \mathrm{B}}$

\section*{Results:}
1. Prove that $\sin (\mathrm{A}+\mathrm{B}) \sin (\mathrm{A}-\mathrm{B})=\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~B}$
$$\begin{aligned}
& \sin (A+B)=\underbrace{\sin A \cos B}_{x}+\underbrace{\cos A \sin B}_{y}=x+y \text { (say) } \\
& \sin (A-B)=\underbrace{\sin A \cos B}_{x}-\underbrace{\cos A \sin B}_{y}=x-y
\end{aligned}$$
$$\begin{array}{rlr}
\mathrm{LHS} & =\sin (\mathrm{A}+\mathrm{B}) \sin (\mathrm{A}-\mathrm{B})=(\mathrm{x}+\mathrm{y})(\mathrm{x}-\mathrm{y})=\mathrm{x}^{2}-\mathrm{y}^{2} & \\
& =(\sin \mathrm{A} \cos \mathrm{~B})^{2}-(\cos \mathrm{A} \sin \mathrm{~B})^{2} & \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~B}+\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~B}=1 \\
& =\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A} \cos ^{2} \mathrm{~B}-\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A} \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~B} & \cos ^{2} \mathrm{~B}=1-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~B} \\
& =\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}\left(1-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~B}\right)-\left(1-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}\right) \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~B} & \\
& =\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A} \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~B}-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~B}+\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A} \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~B} & \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}=\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}=1 \\
\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}=1-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}
\end{array}$$
$$=\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~B}=\text { RHS }$$
2. Prove that $\cos (\mathrm{A}+\mathrm{B}) \cos (\mathrm{A}-\mathrm{B})=\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~B}-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}=\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~B}$.
$$\begin{aligned}
& \cos (A+B)=\underbrace{\cos A \cos B}_{x}-\underbrace{\sin A \sin B}_{y}=x-y \\
& \cos (A-B)=\underbrace{\cos A \cos B}_{x}+\underbrace{\sin A \sin B}_{y}=x+y \\
& \text { LHS }=\cos (\mathrm{A}+\mathrm{B}) \cos (\mathrm{A}-\mathrm{B}) \\
& =(x-y)(x+y)=x^{2}-y^{2} \\
& =(\cos A \cos B)^{2}-(\sin A \sin B)^{2} \\
& =\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A} \cos ^{2} \mathrm{~B}-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A} \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~B} \\
& =\left(1-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}\right) \cos ^{2} \mathrm{~B}-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}\left(1-\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~B}\right) \\
& =\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~B}-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A} \cos ^{2} \mathrm{~B}-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}+\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A} \cos ^{2} \mathrm{~B} \\
& =\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~B}-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}=\text { RHS } \\
& =\left(1-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~B}\right)-\left(1-\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}\right) \\
& =1-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~B}-1+\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A} \\
& =\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~B}
\end{aligned}$$
$$\begin{array}{|r|}
\hline \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}+\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}
\end{array}=1 . \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}, ~ \begin{aligned}
\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A} & =1-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~B}=\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~B}
\end{aligned} \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~B}=1-\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~B} .$$
$$\begin{array}{|c|}
\hline \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~B}+\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~B}=1 \\
\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~B}=1-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~B} \\
\hline \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}=\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}=1 \\
\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}=1-\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A} \\
\hline
\end{array}$$

\subsection*{3.1 WORKED EXAMPLES PART - A}
1. Find the value of $\sin 65^{\circ} \cos 25^{\circ}+\cos 65^{\circ} \sin 25^{\circ}$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
& \sin 65^{\circ} \cos 25^{\circ}+\cos 65^{\circ} \sin 25^{\circ} \\
& =\sin \left(65^{\circ}+25^{\circ}\right)=\sin 90^{\circ}=1
\end{aligned}$$
2. Find the value of $\sin 40^{\circ} \cos 10^{\circ}-\cos 40^{\circ} \sin 10^{\circ}$.

\section*{Solution:}
$\sin 40^{\circ} \cos 10^{\circ}-\cos 40^{\circ} \sin 10^{\circ}$
$=\sin \left(40^{\circ}-10^{\circ}\right)=\sin 30^{\circ}=\frac{1}{2}$.
3. Find the value of $\cos 50^{\circ} \cos 40^{\circ}-\sin 50^{\circ} \sin 40^{\circ}$.

\section*{Solution:}
$\cos 50^{\circ} \cos 40^{\circ}-\sin 50^{\circ} \sin 40^{\circ}$
$=\cos \left(50^{\circ}+40^{\circ}\right)=\cos 90^{\circ}=0$
4. What is the value of $\cos 70^{\circ} \cos 10^{\circ}+\sin 70^{\circ} \sin 10^{\circ}$ ?

\section*{Solution:}
$\cos 70^{\circ} \cos 10^{\circ}+\sin 70^{\circ} \sin 10^{\circ}$
$=\cos \left(70^{\circ}-10^{\circ}\right)=\cos 60^{\circ}=\frac{1}{2}$
5. Find the value of $\frac{\tan 20^{\circ}+\tan 25^{\circ}}{1-\tan 20^{\circ} \tan 25^{\circ}}$.

\section*{Solution:}
$\frac{\tan 20^{\circ}+\tan 25^{\circ}}{1-\tan 20^{\circ} \tan 25^{\circ}}$
$=\tan \left(20^{\circ}+25^{\circ}\right)=\tan 45^{\circ}=1$
6. Find the value of $\frac{\tan 135^{\circ}-\tan 75^{\circ}}{1+\tan 135^{\circ} \tan 75^{\circ}}$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\frac{\tan 135^{\circ}-\tan 75^{\circ}}{1+\tan 135^{\circ} \tan 75^{\circ}}$$
$$\tan (\mathrm{A}-\mathrm{B}) \text { formula }$$
$=\tan \left(135^{\circ}-75^{\circ}\right)=\tan 60^{\circ}=\sqrt{3}$

\section*{PART - B}
1. Find the value of $\cos \left(60^{\circ}-\mathrm{A}\right) \cos \left(30^{\circ}+\mathrm{A}\right)-\sin \left(60^{\circ}-\mathrm{A}\right) \sin \left(30^{\circ}+\mathrm{A}\right)$.

\section*{Solution:}
$\cos \left(60^{\circ}-\mathrm{A}\right) \cos \left(30^{\circ}+\mathrm{A}\right)-\sin \left(60^{\circ}-\mathrm{A}\right) \sin \left(30^{\circ}+\mathrm{A}\right)$
$=\cos x \cos y-\sin x \sin y$
$=\cos (\mathrm{x}+\mathrm{y})=\cos 90^{\circ}=0$
\begin{tabular}{|l|}
\hline$x=60^{\circ}-A$ \\
$y=30^{\circ}+A$ \\
\hline$x+y=90^{\circ}$ \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
2. Find the value of $\sin 15^{\circ}$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
& \sin 15^{\circ}=\sin \left(45^{\circ}-30^{\circ}\right) \\
& \quad=\sin 45^{\circ} \cos 30^{\circ}-\cos 45^{\circ} \sin 30^{\circ} \\
& =\frac{1}{\sqrt{2}} \times \frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}-\frac{1}{\sqrt{2}} \times \frac{1}{2} \\
& =\frac{\sqrt{3}}{2 \sqrt{2}}-\frac{1}{2 \sqrt{2}}=\frac{\sqrt{3}-1}{2 \sqrt{2}}
\end{aligned}$$
3. Find hte value of $\cos 75^{\circ}$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
& \cos 75^{\circ}=\cos \left(45^{\circ}+30^{\circ}\right) \\
& \quad=\cos 45^{\circ} \cos 30^{\circ}-\sin 45^{\circ} \sin 30^{\circ} \\
& =\frac{1}{\sqrt{2}} \times \frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}-\frac{1}{\sqrt{2}} \times \frac{1}{2} \\
& =\frac{\sqrt{3}}{2 \sqrt{2}}-\frac{1}{2 \sqrt{2}}=\frac{\sqrt{3}-1}{2 \sqrt{2}}
\end{aligned}$$
4. Prove that $\frac{\sin (\mathrm{A}+\mathrm{B})+\sin (\mathrm{A}-\mathrm{B})}{\cos (\mathrm{A}+\mathrm{B})+\cos (\mathrm{A}-\mathrm{B})}=\tan \mathrm{A}$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
\mathrm{LHS} & =\frac{\sin A \cos B+\cos A \sin B+\sin A \cos B-\cos A \sin B}{\cos A \cos B-\sin A \sin B+\cos A \cos B+\sin A \sin B} \\
& =\frac{2 \sin A \cos B}{2 \cos A \cos B} \\
& =\frac{\sin A}{\cos A}=\tan A=R H S
\end{aligned}$$
5. Prove that $\sin (A+B) \sin (A-B)+\sin (B+C) \sin (B-C)+\sin (C+A) \sin (C-A)=0$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
\mathrm{LHS} & =\sin (\mathrm{A}+\mathrm{B}) \sin (\mathrm{A}-\mathrm{B})+\sin (\mathrm{B}+\mathrm{C}) \sin (\mathrm{B}-\mathrm{C})+\sin (\mathrm{C}+\mathrm{A}) \sin (\mathrm{C}-\mathrm{A}) \\
& =\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~B}+\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~B}-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{C}+\sin ^{2} \mathrm{C}-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}=0=\mathrm{RHS}
\end{aligned}$$
6. If $\tan \mathrm{A}=\frac{1}{2}$ and $\tan \mathrm{B}=\frac{1}{3}$ find the value of $\tan (\mathrm{A}+\mathrm{B})$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
\tan (\mathrm{A}+\mathrm{B}) & =\frac{\tan \mathrm{A}+\tan \mathrm{B}}{1-\tan \mathrm{A} \tan \mathrm{~B}} \\
& =\frac{\frac{1}{2}+\frac{1}{3}}{1-\frac{1}{2} \times \frac{1}{3}} \\
& =\frac{\frac{3+2}{6}}{1-\frac{1}{6}}=\frac{\frac{5}{6}}{\frac{6-1}{6}}=\frac{\frac{5}{6}}{\frac{5}{6}}=1
\end{aligned}$$
7. Find the value of $\tan 105^{\circ}$, with out using tables.

\section*{Solution:}
$\tan 105^{\circ}=\tan \left(60^{\circ}+45^{\circ}\right)$
$=\frac{\tan 60^{\circ}+\tan 45^{\circ}}{1-\tan 60^{\circ} \tan 45^{\circ}}$
$=\frac{\sqrt{3}+1}{1-\sqrt{3} \times 1}=\frac{\sqrt{3}+1}{1-\sqrt{3}}$
8. Prove that $\tan 20^{\circ}+\tan 25^{\circ}+\tan 20^{\circ} \tan 25^{\circ}=1$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
& 20^{\circ}+25^{\circ}=45^{\circ} \\
& \tan \left(20^{\circ}+25^{\circ}\right)=\tan 45^{\circ} \\
& \frac{\tan 20^{\circ}+\tan 25^{\circ}}{1-\tan 20^{\circ} \tan 25^{\circ}}=1
\end{aligned}$$

Cross multiplying, $\tan 20^{\circ}+\tan 25^{\circ}=1-\tan 20^{\circ} \tan 25^{\circ}$ $\tan 20^{\circ}+\tan 25^{\circ}+\tan 20^{\circ} \tan 25^{\circ}=1$

\section*{PART - C}
1. If A and B are acute and if $\sin \mathrm{A}=\frac{1}{\sqrt{10}}$ and $\sin \mathrm{B}=\frac{1}{\sqrt{5}}$ prove that $\mathrm{A}+\mathrm{B}=\frac{\pi}{4}$.

\section*{Solution:}

Given: $\quad \sin \mathrm{A}=\frac{1}{\sqrt{10}}$ and $\sin \mathrm{B}=\frac{1}{\sqrt{5}}$
$\cos \mathrm{A}=\sqrt{1-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}} \mid \cos \mathrm{B}=\sqrt{1-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~B}}$
$=\sqrt{1-\left(\frac{1}{\sqrt{10}}\right)^{2}}=\sqrt{1-\left(\frac{1}{\sqrt{5}}\right)^{2}}$
$=\sqrt{1-\frac{1}{10}}$
$=\sqrt{1-\frac{1}{5}}$
$=\sqrt{\frac{10-1}{10}}$
$=\sqrt{\frac{5-1}{5}}$
$=\sqrt{\frac{9}{10}}=\frac{3}{\sqrt{10}}$
$=\sqrt{\frac{4}{5}}=\frac{2}{\sqrt{5}}$
$$\begin{array}{|l|l|}
\hline \sin \mathrm{A}=\frac{1}{\sqrt{10}} & \sin \mathrm{~B}=\frac{1}{\sqrt{5}} \\
\cos \mathrm{~A}=\frac{3}{\sqrt{10}} & \cos \mathrm{~B}=\frac{2}{\sqrt{5}} \\
\hline
\end{array}$$
$\sin (A+B)=\sin A \cos B+\cos A \sin B$
$$\begin{aligned}
& =\frac{1}{\sqrt{10}} \times \frac{2}{\sqrt{5}}+\frac{3}{\sqrt{10}} \times \frac{1}{\sqrt{5}} \\
& =\frac{2}{\sqrt{50}}+\frac{3}{\sqrt{50}} \\
& =\frac{5}{\sqrt{50}}=\frac{5}{\sqrt{25 \times 2}}=\frac{5}{5 \sqrt{2}} \\
\sin (\mathrm{~A}+\mathrm{B}) & =\frac{1}{\sqrt{2}}=\sin 45^{\circ} \\
\mathrm{A}+\mathrm{B} & =45^{\circ}=\frac{180^{\circ}}{4}=\frac{\pi}{4}
\end{aligned}$$
2. If A and B are acute and if $\cos \mathrm{A}=\frac{1}{7}$ and $\cos \mathrm{B}=\frac{13}{14}$, prove that $\mathrm{A}-\mathrm{B}=60^{\circ}=\frac{\pi}{3}$.

\section*{Solution:}

Given:
$$\left.\begin{aligned}
& \cos \mathrm{A}=\frac{1}{7} \quad \text { and } \quad \cos \mathrm{B}=\frac{13}{14} \\
\sin \mathrm{~A}=\sqrt{1-\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}} & \sin \mathrm{~B}=\sqrt{1-\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~B}} \\
= & \sqrt{1-\left(\frac{1}{7}\right)^{2}} \\
= & \sqrt{1-\frac{1}{49}} \\
= & \sqrt{\frac{49-1}{49}} \\
= & \sqrt{\frac{48}{49}}=\sqrt{\frac{13}{\left.\frac{13}{14}\right)^{2}}} \\
= & \frac{4 \sqrt{3}}{7}
\end{aligned} \right\rvert\,=\sqrt{1-\frac{169}{196}}{ }^{\frac{196-169}{196}} . \sqrt{\frac{27}{196}}=\sqrt{\frac{9 \times 3}{14 \times 14}}$$
$$\begin{array}{|c|c|}
\hline \sin \mathrm{A}=\frac{4 \sqrt{3}}{7} & \sin \mathrm{~B}=\frac{3 \sqrt{3}}{14} \\
\cos \mathrm{~A}=\frac{1}{7} & \cos \mathrm{~B}=\frac{13}{14} \\
\hline
\end{array}$$
$\cos (\mathrm{A}-\mathrm{B})=\cos \mathrm{A} \cos \mathrm{B}+\sin \mathrm{A} \sin \mathrm{B}$
$$\begin{aligned}
& =\frac{1}{7} \times \frac{13}{14}+\frac{4 \sqrt{3}}{7} \times \frac{3 \sqrt{3}}{14} \\
& =\frac{13}{98}+\frac{12 \times 3}{98} \\
& =\frac{13+36}{98}=\frac{49}{98}=\frac{1}{2} \\
\cos (\mathrm{~A}-\mathrm{B}) & =\frac{1}{2}=\cos 60^{\circ} \\
\mathrm{A}-\mathrm{B} & =60^{\circ}=\frac{180^{\circ}}{3}=\frac{\pi}{3}
\end{aligned}$$
3. If $\mathrm{A}+\mathrm{B}=45^{\circ}$, prove that $(1+\tan \mathrm{A})(1+\tan \mathrm{B})=2$ and hence deduce the value of $\tan 22 \frac{1}{1^{\circ}}$.

\section*{Solution:}

Given: $\mathrm{A}+\mathrm{B}=45^{\circ}$
Taking tan on both sides
$$\begin{aligned}
& \tan (A+B)=\tan 45^{\circ} \\
& \frac{\tan A+\tan B}{1-\tan A \tan B}=1 \\
& \tan A+\tan B=1-\tan A \tan B \\
& \tan A+\tan B+\tan A \tan B=1 \\
& \begin{array}{l}
\text { LHS }=(1+\tan A)(1+\tan B) \\
\quad=1+\tan B+\tan A+\tan A \tan B \\
\quad=1+1 \text { using }(1) \\
\quad=2=\text { RHS }
\end{array}
\end{aligned}$$

Put $\mathrm{A}=221_{1} 2^{\circ}, \mathrm{B}=221_{2}{ }^{\circ}$. Then $\mathrm{A}+\mathrm{B}=221 /^{\circ}+221_{2}^{\circ}=45^{\circ}$.
$\left(1+\tan 22 \frac{1}{2} 2^{\circ}\right)\left(1+\tan 22 \frac{1}{2} 2^{\circ}\right)=2$
(say) $x \quad x$
$x^{2}=2$
$x=\sqrt{2}$
$1+\tan 221 / 2=\sqrt{2}$
$\tan 221 / 2=\sqrt{2}-1$
4. If A and B are acute angle and if $\tan \mathrm{A}=\frac{\mathrm{n}}{\mathrm{n}+1}$ and $\tan \mathrm{B}=\frac{1}{2 \mathrm{n}+1}$, show that $\mathrm{A}+\mathrm{B}=\frac{\pi}{4}$.

\section*{Solution:}

Given: $\tan \mathrm{A}=\frac{\mathrm{n}}{\mathrm{n}+1}$ and $\tan \mathrm{B}=\frac{1}{2 \mathrm{n}+1}$
$$\begin{aligned}
\tan (A+B) & =\frac{\tan A+\tan B}{1-\tan A \tan B} \\
& =\frac{\frac{n}{(n+1)}+\frac{1}{(2 n+1)}}{1-\frac{n}{(n+1)} \times \frac{1}{(2 n+1)}} \\
& =\frac{\frac{\mathrm{n}(2 \mathrm{n}+1)+1(\mathrm{n}+1)}{(\mathrm{n}+1)(2 \mathrm{n}+1)}}{\frac{(\mathrm{n}+1)(2 \mathrm{n}+1)-\mathrm{n} \times 1}{(\mathrm{n}+1)(2 \mathrm{n}+1)}} \\
& =\frac{2 \mathrm{n}^{2}+\mathrm{n}+\mathrm{n}+1}{2 \mathrm{n}^{2}+\mathrm{n}+2 \mathrm{n}+1-\mathrm{n}} \\
& =\frac{2 \mathrm{n}^{2}+2 \mathrm{n}+1}{2 \mathrm{n}^{2}+2 \mathrm{n}+1}=1 \\
\tan (\mathrm{~A}+\mathrm{B}) & =1=\tan 45^{\circ} \\
\mathrm{A}+\mathrm{B} & =45^{\circ}=\frac{180^{\circ}}{4}=\frac{\pi}{4}
\end{aligned}$$
5. If $\tan \mathrm{A}-\tan \mathrm{B}=\mathrm{p}$ and $\cot \mathrm{B}-\cot \mathrm{A}=\mathrm{q}$, show that $\cot (\mathrm{A}-\mathrm{B})=\frac{1}{\mathrm{p}}+\frac{1}{\mathrm{q}}$.

\section*{Solution:}

RHS $=\frac{1}{\mathrm{p}}+\frac{1}{\mathrm{q}}$
$$\begin{aligned}
& =\frac{1}{\tan \mathrm{~A}-\tan \mathrm{B}}+\frac{1}{\cot \mathrm{~B}-\cot \mathrm{A}} \\
& =\frac{1}{\tan \mathrm{~A}-\tan \mathrm{B}}+\frac{1}{\frac{1}{\tan \mathrm{~B}}-\frac{1}{\tan \mathrm{~A}}} \\
& =\frac{1}{\tan \mathrm{~A}-\tan \mathrm{B}}+\frac{1}{\frac{\tan \mathrm{~A}-\tan \mathrm{B}}{\tan \mathrm{~A} \tan \mathrm{~B}}} \\
& =\frac{1+\tan \mathrm{A} \tan \mathrm{~B}}{\tan \mathrm{~A}-\tan \mathrm{B}} \\
& =\cot (\mathrm{A}-\mathrm{B}) \\
& =\text { RHS }
\end{aligned}$$
$$\begin{aligned}
& \tan (\mathrm{A}-\mathrm{B})=\frac{\tan \mathrm{A}-\tan \mathrm{B}}{1+\tan \mathrm{A} \tan \mathrm{~B}} \\
& \cot (\mathrm{~A}-\mathrm{B})=\frac{1+\tan \mathrm{A} \tan \mathrm{~B}}{\tan \mathrm{~A}-\tan \mathrm{B}}
\end{aligned}$$

\subsection*{3.2 MULTIPLE AND SUB-MULTIPLE ANGLES}

Trigonometric ratios of multiple angles of 2A in terms to that of A.
1. Prove that $\sin 2 \mathrm{~A}=2 \sin \mathrm{~A} \cos \mathrm{~A}$

We know that
$\sin (A+B)=\sin A \cos B+\cos A \sin B$
Put $\mathrm{B}=\mathrm{A}$
$\sin (A+A)=\sin A \cos A+\cos A \sin A$
$\sin 2 \mathrm{~A}=\sin \mathrm{A} \cos \mathrm{A}+\sin \mathrm{A} \cos \mathrm{A}$
$\sin 2 \mathrm{~A}=2 \sin \mathrm{~A} \cos \mathrm{~A}$
Formula for $\sin 2 \mathrm{~A}$
2. Prove that $\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}=\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}=2 \cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}-1=1-2 \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}$.

We know that
$\cos (\mathrm{A}+\mathrm{B})=\cos \mathrm{A} \cos \mathrm{B}-\sin \mathrm{A} \sin \mathrm{B}$
Put B $=\mathrm{A}$
$\cos (\mathrm{A}+\mathrm{A})=\cos \mathrm{A} \cos (\mathrm{A})-\sin \mathrm{A} \sin (\mathrm{A})$
$\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}=\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}$
Formula for $\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}$
$=\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}-\left(1-\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}\right)$
$=\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}-1+\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}$
$\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}=2 \cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}-1$
Formula for $\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}$
$=2\left(1-\sin ^{2} A\right)-1$
$=2-2 \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}-1$
$\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}=1-2 \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}$
Formula for $\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}$
(iii)
3. Prove that $\tan 2 \mathrm{~A}=\frac{2 \tan \mathrm{~A}}{1-\tan ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}$.

\section*{Solution:}

We know that
$\tan (\mathrm{A}+\mathrm{B})=\frac{\tan \mathrm{A}+\tan \mathrm{B}}{1-\tan \mathrm{A} \tan \mathrm{B}}$
Put $\mathrm{B}=\mathrm{A}$
$\tan (\mathrm{A}+\mathrm{A})=\frac{\tan \mathrm{A}+\tan \mathrm{A}}{1-\tan \mathrm{A} \tan \mathrm{A}}$
$\tan 2 \mathrm{~A}=\frac{2 \tan \mathrm{~A}}{1-\tan ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}$
4. Prove that
a) $\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}=\frac{1-\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}}{2}$
b) $\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}=\frac{1+\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}}{2}$
c) $\tan ^{2} A=\frac{1-\cos 2 A}{1+\cos 2 A}$

\section*{Solution:}
(a) $\mathrm{RHS}=\frac{1-\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}}{2}=\frac{1-\left(1-2 \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}\right.}{2}$ using formula for $\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}-$ (iii)
$$\begin{aligned}
& =\frac{\not \perp-\nsupseteq+2 \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}{2}=\frac{\not 2 \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}{\not 2} \\
& =\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}=\mathrm{LHS}
\end{aligned}$$
(b) $\mathrm{RHS}=\frac{1+\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}}{2}=\frac{1+\left(2 \cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}-1\right)}{2}$ using formula for $\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}-$ (ii)
$$=\frac{2 \cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}{2}=\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}=\mathrm{LHS}$$
(c) Formula for $\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}$ - (iii)
$$\begin{aligned}
\mathrm{RHS}=\frac{1-\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}}{1+\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}} & =\frac{1-\left(1-2 \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}\right)}{1+2 \cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}-1} \\
& =\frac{\not 1-\nmid+2 \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}{2 \cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}=\frac{\not 2 \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}{\not 2 \cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}} \\
& =\frac{\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}{\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}=\tan ^{2} \mathrm{~A}=\mathrm{LHS}
\end{aligned}$$

To express $\sin 2 \mathrm{~A}$ and $\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}$ in terms of $\tan \mathrm{A}$
Prove that
(a) $\sin 2 \mathrm{~A}=\frac{2 \tan \mathrm{~A}}{1+\tan ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}$
(b) $\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}=\frac{1-\tan ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}{1+\tan ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}$

\section*{Solution:}
(a) RHS $=\frac{2 \tan \mathrm{~A}}{1+\tan ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}=\frac{\frac{2 \sin \mathrm{~A}}{\cos \mathrm{~A}}}{1+\frac{\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}{\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}}$
$$=\frac{\frac{2 \sin \mathrm{~A}}{\cos \mathrm{~A}}}{\frac{\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}+\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}{\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}}=\frac{\frac{2 \sin \mathrm{~A}}{\cos \mathrm{~A}}}{\frac{1}{\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}}$$
$$\begin{array}{ll}
=\frac{2 \sin \mathrm{~A}}{\cos \mathrm{~A}} \times \frac{\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}{1} & \text { cancelling } \cos \mathrm{A} \\
=2 \sin \mathrm{~A} \cos \mathrm{~A} & \text { Formula } \\
=\sin 2 \mathrm{~A}=\text { LHS } & \sin 2 \mathrm{~A}=2 \sin \mathrm{~A} \cos \mathrm{~A}
\end{array}$$

\section*{SUB-MULTIPLE ANGLES}

If $\mathbf{A}$ is any angle, then $\mathbf{A} / \mathbf{2}$ is called sub-multiple angle.
Prove that
a) $\sin \mathrm{A}=2 \sin (\mathrm{~A} / 2) \cos (\mathrm{A} / 2)$
b) $\cos \mathrm{A}=\cos ^{2}(\mathrm{~A} / 2)-\sin ^{2}(\mathrm{~A} / 2)$
$$\begin{aligned}
& =2 \cos ^{2}(\mathrm{~A} / 2)-1 \\
& =1-2 \sin ^{2}(\mathrm{~A} / 2)
\end{aligned}$$
a) We know that
$$\sin 2 \mathrm{~A}=2 \sin \mathrm{~A} \cos \mathrm{~A}$$

Divide the angles on both sides by 2
$$\begin{aligned}
\sin \left(\frac{2 \mathrm{~A}}{2}\right) & =2 \sin (\mathrm{~A} / 2) \cos (\mathrm{A} / 2) \\
\sin \mathrm{A} & =2 \sin (\mathrm{~A} / 2) \cos (\mathrm{A} / 2)
\end{aligned}$$
(b) We know that
$$\begin{aligned}
\cos 2 \mathrm{~A} & =\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A} \\
& =2 \cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}-1 \\
& =1-2 \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}
\end{aligned}$$

Divide the angles on both sides by 2
$$\begin{aligned}
\cos \mathrm{A} & =\cos ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)-\sin ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right) \\
& =2 \cos ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)-1 \\
& =1-2 \sin ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)
\end{aligned}$$

Prove that
(a) $\sin ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)=\frac{1-\cos \mathrm{A}}{2}$
(b) $\cos ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)=\frac{1+\cos \mathrm{A}}{2}$
(c) $\tan ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)=\frac{1-\cos \mathrm{A}}{1+\cos \mathrm{A}}$
(a) RHS $=\frac{1-\cos \mathrm{A}}{2}=\frac{1-\left[1-2 \sin ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)\right]}{2}$
$$\begin{aligned}
& =\frac{1-1+2 \sin ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)}{2}=\frac{2 \sin ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)}{2} \quad \text { using Formula (iii) } \\
& =\sin ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)=\text { LHS }
\end{aligned}$$
(b) RHS $=\frac{1+\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}}{2}=\frac{1+2 \cos ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)-1}{2} \quad$ using Formula (ii)
$$=\frac{2 \cos ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)}{2}=\cos ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)=\text { LHS }$$
$$\begin{array}{rlr}
\text { RHS } & =\frac{1-\cos \mathrm{A}}{1+\cos \mathrm{A}}=\frac{1-\left[1-2 \sin ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)\right]}{1+2 \cos ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)-1} & \text { using Formula (iii) } \\
& =\frac{1-1+2 \sin ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)}{2 \cos ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)}=\frac{2 \sin ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)}{2 \cos ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)} & \text { using Formula (ii) } \\
& =\tan ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)=\text { LHS } &
\end{array}$$

To express $\sin A, \cos A, \tan A$ in terms of $\tan \left(\frac{A}{2}\right)$.
Prove that
a) $\sin A=\frac{2 \tan \left(\frac{A}{2}\right)}{1+\tan ^{2}\left(\frac{A}{2}\right)}$
b) $\cos \mathrm{A}=\frac{1-\tan ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)}{1+\tan ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)}$
c) $\tan A=\frac{2 \tan \left(\frac{A}{2}\right)}{1-\tan ^{2}\left(\frac{A}{2}\right)}$

We have already proved that
$$\begin{aligned}
& \sin (2 \mathrm{~A})=\frac{2 \tan \mathrm{~A}}{1+\tan ^{2} \mathrm{~A}} \\
& \cos (2 \mathrm{~A})=\frac{1-\tan ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}{1+\tan ^{2} \mathrm{~A}} \\
& \tan (2 \mathrm{~A})=\frac{2 \tan \mathrm{~A}}{1-\tan ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}
\end{aligned}$$

Divide the angles on both sides by 2 on the above three results.
Then we get,
a) $\sin \mathrm{A}=\frac{2 \tan \left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)}{1+\tan ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)}$
b) $\cos \mathrm{A}=\frac{1-\tan ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)}{1+\tan ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)}$
c) $\tan \mathrm{A}=\frac{2 \tan \left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)}{1-\tan ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)}$

\section*{Multiple angles of 3A}

Prove that
$$\sin 3 A=3 \sin A-4 \sin ^{3} A$$

Formula
We know that
$$\begin{aligned}
& \sin (A+B)= \\
& \text { Put } B=2 A \\
& \begin{aligned}
\sin (A+2 A) & =\sin A \cos (2 A)+\cos A \sin B \\
\sin 3 A & =\sin A\left(1-2 \sin ^{2} A\right)+\cos A(2 \operatorname{Ain} A \cos A) \\
& =\sin A-2 \sin ^{3} A+2 \sin A \cos ^{2} A \\
& =\sin A-2 \sin ^{3} \mathrm{~A}+2 \sin \mathrm{~A}\left(1-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}\right) \\
& =\sin \mathrm{A}-2 \sin ^{3} \mathrm{~A}+2 \sin \mathrm{~A}-2 \sin ^{3} \mathrm{~A} \\
\sin 3 \mathrm{~A} & =3 \sin \mathrm{~A}-4 \sin ^{3} \mathrm{~A}
\end{aligned}
\end{aligned}$$

Prove that
$$\cos 3 \mathrm{~A}=4 \cos ^{3} \mathrm{~A}-3 \cos \mathrm{~A}$$

Formula
We know that
$$\begin{aligned}
& \cos (A+B)=\cos A \cos B-\sin A \sin B \\
& \text { Put } B=2 A \\
& \begin{aligned}
\cos (A+2 A) & =\cos A \cos 2 A-\sin A \sin 2 A \\
\cos 3 A & =\cos A\left(2 \cos ^{2} A-1\right)-\sin A(2 \sin A \cos A) \\
& =2 \cos ^{3} A-\cos A-2 \cos A \sin ^{2} A \\
& =2 \cos ^{3} A-\cos A-2 \cos A\left(1-\cos ^{2} A\right) \\
& =2 \cos ^{3} A-\cos A-2 \cos A+2 \cos ^{3} A \\
& =4 \cos ^{3} A-3 \cos A
\end{aligned}
\end{aligned}$$

Prove that $\tan 3 \mathrm{~A}=\frac{3 \tan \mathrm{~A}-\tan ^{3} \mathrm{~A}}{1-3 \tan ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\tan 3 \mathrm{~A}=\frac{3 \tan \mathrm{~A}-\tan ^{3} \mathrm{~A}}{1-3 \tan ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}$$

We know that
$$\begin{aligned}
\tan (\mathrm{A}+\mathrm{B}) & =\frac{\tan \mathrm{A}+\tan \mathrm{B}}{1-\tan \mathrm{A} \tan \mathrm{~B}} \\
\text { Put } \mathrm{B} & =2 \mathrm{~A} \\
\tan (\mathrm{~A}+2 \mathrm{~A}) & =\frac{\tan \mathrm{A}+\tan 2 \mathrm{~A}}{1-\tan \mathrm{A} \cdot \tan 2 \mathrm{~A}} \\
& =\frac{\tan \mathrm{A}+\frac{2 \tan \mathrm{~A}}{1-\tan 2} \mathrm{~A}}{1-\tan \mathrm{A} \times \frac{2 \tan \mathrm{~A}}{1-\tan ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}} \\
& =\frac{\frac{\tan \mathrm{A}\left(1-\tan ^{2} \mathrm{~A}\right)+2 \tan \mathrm{~A}}{1-\tan ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}}{\frac{1-\tan ^{2} \mathrm{~A}-2 \tan ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}{1-\tan ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}} \\
& =\frac{\tan \mathrm{A}-\tan ^{3} \mathrm{~A}+2 \tan \mathrm{~A}}{1-3 \tan ^{2} \mathrm{~A}} \\
& =\frac{3 \tan \mathrm{~A}-\tan ^{3} \mathrm{~A}}{1-3 \tan ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}
\end{aligned}$$

\subsection*{3.2 WORKED EXAMPLES PART - A}
1. Find the value of $2 \sin 15^{\circ} \cos 15^{\circ}$.

\section*{Solution:}

We know that $\sin 2 \mathrm{~A}=2 \sin \mathrm{~A} \cos \mathrm{~A}$
$$\begin{aligned}
& \text { Put } \mathrm{A}=15^{\circ} \\
& \sin \left(2 \times 15^{\circ}\right)=2 \text { in } 15^{\circ} \cos 15^{\circ} \\
& \sin 30^{\circ}=2 \sin 15^{\circ} \cos 15^{\circ} \\
& 2 \sin 15^{\circ} \cos 15^{\circ}=\sin 30^{\circ}=\frac{1}{2}
\end{aligned}$$
2. Find the value of $2 \sin 75^{\circ} \cos 75^{\circ}$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
2 \sin 75^{\circ} \cos 75^{\circ} & =\sin (2 \times \mathrm{A}) \\
& =\sin \left(2 \times 75^{\circ}\right) \\
& =\sin 150^{\circ}=\sin (180-30) \\
& =+\sin 30^{\circ}=\frac{1}{2}
\end{aligned}$$
3. Find the value of $\cos ^{2} 15^{\circ}-\sin ^{2} 15^{\circ}$.

\section*{Solution:}

We know that
$$\begin{aligned}
& \cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}=\cos 2 \mathrm{~A} \\
& \text { Put } \mathrm{A}=15^{\circ} \\
& \cos ^{2} 15^{\circ}-\sin ^{2} 15^{\circ}=\cos \left(2 \times 15^{\circ}\right) \\
&=\cos 30^{\circ}=\frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}
\end{aligned}$$
4. Find the value of $1-2 \sin ^{2} 221 / 2^{\circ}$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
& 1-2 \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}=\cos 2 \mathrm{~A} \\
& 1-2 \sin ^{2} 221 /^{\circ}=\cos \left(2 \times 221 / 2^{\circ}\right)=\cos 45^{\circ}=\frac{1}{\sqrt{2}}
\end{aligned}$$
5. Prove that $\frac{2 \tan 15^{\circ}}{1+\tan ^{2} 15^{\circ}}=\frac{1}{2}$

\section*{Solution:}

We know that
$$\begin{aligned}
\frac{2 \tan \mathrm{~A}}{1+\tan ^{2} \mathrm{~A}} & =\sin 2 \mathrm{~A} \\
\text { Put } \mathrm{A} & =15^{\circ} \\
\frac{2 \tan 15^{\circ}}{1+\tan ^{2} 15^{\circ}} & =\sin 2\left(15^{\circ}\right) \\
& =\sin 30^{\circ}=\frac{1}{2}
\end{aligned}$$
6. Find the value of $\frac{1-\tan ^{2} 15^{\circ}}{1+\tan ^{2} 15^{\circ}}$.

\section*{Solution:}

We know that
$$\begin{aligned}
& \frac{1-\tan ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}{1+\tan ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}=\cos 2 \mathrm{~A} \\
& \frac{1-\tan ^{2} 15^{\circ}}{1+\tan ^{2} 15^{\circ}}=\cos (2 \times 15)=\cos 30=\frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}
\end{aligned}$$
7. Prove that $\frac{\sin 2 A}{1+\cos 2 A}=\tan A$.

Solution:
$$\begin{array}{rlr}
\mathrm{LHS} & =\frac{\sin 2 \mathrm{~A}}{1+\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}} \\
& =\frac{2 \sin \mathrm{~A} \cos \mathrm{~A}}{1+2 \cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}-1} \quad & \begin{array}{l}
\text { Formula } \\
\sin 2 \mathrm{~A}=2 \sin \mathrm{~A} \cos \mathrm{~A} \\
\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}=2 \cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}-1
\end{array}
\end{array}$$
$$\begin{aligned}
& =\frac{\not 2 \sin \mathrm{~A} \cos \mathrm{~A}}{\not \not 2 \cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}} \\
& =\frac{\sin \mathrm{A}}{\cos \mathrm{~A}} \quad \text { cancelling } \cos \mathrm{A} \\
& =\tan \mathrm{A}=\text { LHS }
\end{aligned}$$
8. Prove that $\frac{\sin \mathrm{A}}{1-\cos \mathrm{A}}=\cot \left(\frac{\mathrm{A}}{2}\right)$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\text { LHS }=\frac{\sin A}{1-\cos A} \quad \begin{aligned}
& \text { Formulae } \\
& \sin 2 A=2 \sin A \cos A \\
& \cos 2 A=1-2 \sin ^{2} A
\end{aligned}$$

Dividing angles by 2
$$\begin{aligned}
& =\frac{2 \sin \left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right) \cos \left(\frac{\mathrm{A}}{2}\right)}{1-\left(1-2 \sin ^{2} \frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)} \quad \begin{array}{l}
\sin \mathrm{A}=2 \sin \mathrm{~A} / 2 \cos \mathrm{~A} / 2 \\
\cos \mathrm{~A}=1-2 \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A} / 2
\end{array} \\
& =\frac{2 \sin \left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right) \cos \left(\frac{\mathrm{A}}{2}\right)}{1-1+2 \sin ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)} \\
& =\frac{2 \sin \left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right) \cos \left(\frac{\mathrm{A}}{2}\right)}{2 \sin ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)} \\
& =\frac{\cos \left(\frac{\mathrm{A}}{2}\right)}{\sin \left(\frac{\mathrm{A}}{2}\right)}=\cot \left(\frac{\mathrm{A}}{2}\right)
\end{aligned}$$
9. Prove that $\left(\sin \frac{\mathrm{A}}{2}-\cos \frac{\mathrm{A}}{2}\right)^{2}=1-\sin \mathrm{A}$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{array}{rlr}
\text { LHS } & =\left(\sin \frac{\mathrm{A}}{2}-\cos \frac{\mathrm{A}}{2}\right)^{2} & (\mathrm{a}-\mathrm{b})^{2}=\mathrm{a}^{2}+\mathrm{b}^{2}-2 \mathrm{ab} \\
& =\sin ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)+\cos ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)-2 \sin \left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right) \cos \left(\frac{\mathrm{A}}{2}\right) \\
& =1-\sin \mathrm{A} & \begin{aligned}
& \sin ^{2} \theta+\cos ^{2} \theta=1 \\
& 2 \sin \mathrm{~A} / 2 \cos \mathrm{~A} / 2=\sin 2(\mathrm{~A} / 2) \\
&=\sin \mathrm{A}
\end{aligned} \\
& =\text { RHS } & \begin{aligned}
\end{aligned}
\end{array}$$
10. Find the value of $3 \sin 20^{\circ}-4 \sin ^{3} 20^{\circ}$.

We know that
$$\begin{aligned}
& \sin 3 \mathrm{~A}=3 \sin \mathrm{~A}-4 \sin ^{3} \mathrm{~A} \\
& \mathrm{Put} \mathrm{~A}=20 \\
& \begin{aligned}
\sin \left(3 \times 20^{\circ}\right) & =3 \sin 20^{\circ}-4 \sin ^{3} 20^{\circ} \\
3 \sin 20^{\circ}-4 \sin ^{3} 20^{\circ} & =\sin \left(3 \times 20^{\circ}\right) \\
& =\sin 60^{\circ}=\frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}
\end{aligned}
\end{aligned}$$
11. Find that value of $4 \cos ^{3} 10^{\circ}-3 \cos 10^{\circ}$.

We know that
$$\begin{aligned}
4 \cos 3 \mathrm{~A}-3 \cos \mathrm{~A} & =\cos 3 \mathrm{~A} \\
4 \cos ^{3} 10^{\circ}-3 \cos 10^{\circ} & =\cos \left(3 \times 10^{\circ}\right) \\
& =\cos 30^{\circ}=\frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}
\end{aligned}$$
12. Find the value of $3 \sin 40^{\circ}-4 \sin ^{3} 40^{\circ}$.

\section*{Solution:}

We know that
$$\begin{aligned}
3 \sin \mathrm{~A}-4 \sin 3 \mathrm{~A} & =\sin 3 \mathrm{~A} \\
3 \sin 40^{\circ}-4 \sin ^{3} 40^{\circ} & =\sin \left(3 \times 40^{\circ}\right) \\
& =\sin 120^{\circ} \\
& =\sin \left(180^{\circ}-60^{\circ}\right) \\
& =\sin 60^{\circ}=\frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}
\end{aligned}$$

\section*{PART - B}
1. Prove that $\tan \mathrm{A}+\cot \mathrm{A}=2 \operatorname{cosec} 2 \mathrm{~A}$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
\text { LHS }=\tan \mathrm{A}+\cot \mathrm{A} \\
\begin{aligned}
\frac{\sin \mathrm{A}}{\cos \mathrm{~A}}+\frac{\cos \mathrm{A}}{\sin \mathrm{~A}} & =\frac{\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}+\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}{\sin \mathrm{~A} \cos \mathrm{~A}} \\
& =\frac{1}{\sin \mathrm{~A} \cos \mathrm{~A}}=\frac{2}{2 \sin \mathrm{~A} \cos \mathrm{~A}} \quad \text { Multiply and Divide by } 2 \\
& =\frac{2}{\sin 2 \mathrm{~A}} \quad \because \sin 2 \mathrm{~A}=2 \sin \mathrm{~A} \cos \mathrm{~A} \\
& =2 \operatorname{cosec} 2 \mathrm{~A} \quad \because \frac{1}{\sin \mathrm{~A}}=\operatorname{cosec} \mathrm{A} \\
& =\text { RHS }
\end{aligned}
\end{aligned}$$
2. Prove that $\frac{\sin \mathrm{A}+\sin 2 \mathrm{~A}}{1+\cos \mathrm{A}+\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}}=\tan \mathrm{A}$.

Solution:
$$\text { LHS }=\frac{\sin \mathrm{A}+\sin 2 \mathrm{~A}}{1+\cos \mathrm{A}+\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}} \quad\left|\begin{array}{l}
\text { Formula } \\
\sin 2 \mathrm{~A}=2 \sin \mathrm{~A} \cos \mathrm{~A} \\
\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}=2 \cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}-1
\end{array}\right|$$
$$\begin{array}{ll}
=\frac{\sin A+2 \sin A \cos A}{\not x+\cos A+2 \cos ^{2} A \not-1} & \begin{array}{l}
\sin \mathrm{A} \text { is common in } \mathrm{Nr} . \\
\cos \mathrm{A} \text { is common in } \mathrm{Dr} .
\end{array} \\
=\frac{\sin \mathrm{A}[1+2 \cos \mathrm{~A}]}{\cos \mathrm{A}[1+2 \cos \mathrm{~A}]} & \\
=\frac{\sin \mathrm{A}}{\cos \mathrm{~A}} & \text { cancelling } 1+2 \cos \mathrm{~A} \\
=\tan A=\text { RHS } &
\end{array}$$
3. Prove that $\cos ^{4} \mathrm{~A}-\sin ^{4} \mathrm{~A}=\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
\mathrm{LHS} & =\left(\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}\right)^{2}-\left(\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}\right)^{2} \quad \mathrm{a}^{2}-\mathrm{b}^{2}=(\mathrm{a}+\mathrm{b})(\mathrm{a}-\mathrm{b}) \\
& =\left(\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}+\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}\right)\left(\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}\right) \\
& =1(\cos 2 \mathrm{~A})=\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}=\text { RHS }
\end{aligned}$$

\section*{PART - C}
1. Prove that $\frac{1-\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}+\sin 2 \mathrm{~A}}{1+\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}+\sin 2 \mathrm{~A}}=\tan \mathrm{A}$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
\text { LHS } & =\frac{1-\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}+\sin 2 \mathrm{~A}}{1+\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}+\sin 2 \mathrm{~A}} \quad \begin{array}{l}
\text { Formulae } \\
\sin 2 \mathrm{~A}=2 \sin \mathrm{~A} \cos \mathrm{~A} \\
\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}=1-2 \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}=2 \cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}-1
\end{array} \\
& =\frac{1-\left(1-2 \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}\right)+2 \sin \mathrm{~A} \cos \mathrm{~A}}{\not \lambda+2 \cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}-\not \subset+2 \sin \mathrm{~A} \cos \mathrm{~A}} \\
& =\frac{\not 1-\nexists+2 \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}+2 \sin \mathrm{~A} \cos \mathrm{~A}}{2 \cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}+2 \sin \mathrm{~A} \cos \mathrm{~A}} \\
& =\frac{2 \sin \mathrm{~A}(\sin \mathrm{~A}+\cos \mathrm{A})}{2 \cos \mathrm{~A}(\cos \mathrm{~A}+\sin \mathrm{A})} \quad \begin{array}{l}
2 \sin \mathrm{~A} \text { is common in } \mathrm{Nr} \\
2 \cos \mathrm{~A} \text { is common in } \mathrm{Dr}
\end{array} \\
& =\frac{\sin \mathrm{A}}{\cos \mathrm{~A}}=\tan \mathrm{A}=\mathrm{RHS}
\end{aligned}$$
2. Prove that $\frac{1-\cos A+\sin A}{1+\cos A+\sin A}=\tan \left(\frac{A}{2}\right)$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
\text { LHS } & =\frac{1-\cos \mathrm{A}+\sin \mathrm{A}}{1+\cos \mathrm{A}+\sin \mathrm{A}} \begin{array}{l}
\sin \mathrm{A}=2 \sin (\mathrm{~A} / 2) \cos (\mathrm{A} / 2) \\
\cos \mathrm{A}=1-2 \sin ^{2}(\mathrm{~A} / 2) \\
=2 \cos ^{2}(\mathrm{~A} / 2)-1
\end{array} \\
& =\frac{1-\left[1-2 \sin ^{2}(\mathrm{~A} / 2)\right]+2 \sin (\mathrm{~A} / 2) \cos (\mathrm{A} / 2)}{1+\left[2 \cos ^{2}(\mathrm{~A} / 2)-1\right]+2 \sin (\mathrm{~A} / 2) \cos (\mathrm{A} / 2)} \\
& =\frac{1-1+2 \sin ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)+2 \sin \left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right) \cos \left(\frac{\mathrm{A}}{2}\right)}{1+2 \cos ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)+2 \sin \left(\frac{\mathrm{~A}}{2}\right) \cos \left(\frac{\mathrm{A}}{2}\right)}
\end{aligned}$$
$$\left.\left.\begin{array}{rl}
\hline 2 \sin (\mathrm{~A} / 2) \text { is common in } \mathrm{Nr} \\
2 \cos (\mathrm{~A} / 2) \text { is common in } \mathrm{Dr}
\end{array}\right]+2 \sin (\mathrm{~A} / 2)[\sin (\mathrm{A} / 2)+\cos (\mathrm{A} / 2)]\right] \text { 2 } \cos (\mathrm{A} / 2)[\cos (\mathrm{A} / 2)+\sin (\mathrm{A} / 2)] .$$
3. If $\tan \mathrm{A}=\frac{1}{3}$ and $\tan \mathrm{B}=\frac{1}{7}$ show that $2 \mathrm{~A}+\mathrm{B}=\frac{\pi}{4}$.

\section*{Solution:}

Given $\tan \mathrm{A}=\frac{1}{3} \quad \tan \mathrm{~B}=\frac{1}{7}$
$$\text { Formula for } \begin{aligned}
\tan 2 \mathrm{~A} & =\frac{2 \tan \mathrm{~A}^{\prime}}{1-\tan ^{2} \mathrm{~A}} \\
& =\frac{2\left(\frac{1}{3}\right)}{1-\left(\frac{1}{3}\right)^{2}} \\
& =\frac{\frac{2}{3}}{1-\frac{1}{9}}=\frac{\frac{2}{3}}{\frac{9-1}{9}} \\
& =\frac{\frac{2}{3}}{\frac{8}{9}}=\frac{\not 2}{\not 2} \times \frac{\not 93}{\not 84} \\
\tan 2 \mathrm{~A} & =\frac{3}{4}
\end{aligned}$$
$$\begin{aligned}
\tan (\mathrm{A}+\mathrm{B}) & =\frac{\tan \mathrm{A}+\tan \mathrm{B}}{1-\tan \mathrm{A} \tan \mathrm{~B}} \\
\text { Put } \mathrm{A} & =2 \mathrm{~A} \text { on both sides } \\
\tan (2 \mathrm{~A}+\mathrm{B}) & =\frac{\tan 2 \mathrm{~A}+\tan \mathrm{B}}{1-\tan 2 \mathrm{~A} \tan \mathrm{~B}} \\
& =\frac{\frac{3}{4}+\frac{1}{7}}{1-\frac{3}{4} \times \frac{1}{7}} \quad \text { using }(1) \\
& =\frac{\frac{21+4}{28}}{\frac{28-3}{28}}=\frac{\frac{25}{28}}{\frac{25}{28}} \\
& =\frac{25}{28} \times \frac{28}{25}=1
\end{aligned}$$
$$\tan (2 \mathrm{~A}+\mathrm{B})=1=\tan 45^{\circ}$$
$2 \mathrm{~A}+\mathrm{B}=45^{\circ}=\frac{180^{\circ}}{4}=\frac{\pi}{4}$
4. If $\sin \theta=\frac{3}{5}$ find the value of $\sin 3 \theta$.

\section*{Solution:}

Given: $\sin \theta=\frac{3}{5}$
We know that
$$\begin{aligned}
\sin 3 \theta & =3 \sin \theta-4 \sin ^{3} \theta \\
& =3\left(\frac{3}{5}\right)-4\left(\frac{3}{5}\right)^{3} \\
& =\frac{9}{5}-4\left(\frac{27}{125}\right)=\frac{9}{5}-\frac{108}{125} \\
& =\frac{225-108}{125}=\frac{117}{125}
\end{aligned}$$
5. If $\cos \mathrm{A}=\frac{1}{3}$ find the value of $\cos 3 \mathrm{~A}$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
& \text { Given : } \begin{aligned}
\cos \mathrm{A}=\frac{1}{3} \\
\begin{aligned}
\cos 3 \mathrm{~A} & =4 \cos ^{3} \mathrm{~A}-3 \cos \mathrm{~A} \\
& =4\left(\frac{1}{3}\right)^{3}-3\left(\frac{1}{3}\right) \\
& =4\left(\frac{1}{27}\right)-1=\frac{4}{27}-1 \\
& =\frac{4-27}{27}=\frac{-23}{27}
\end{aligned}
\end{aligned} \begin{array}{l}
\text { ( }
\end{array} \\
&
\end{aligned}$$
6. Prove that $\frac{\sin 3 A}{1+2 \cos 2 A}=\sin A$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
\text { LHS } & =\frac{\sin 3 \mathrm{~A}}{1+2 \cos 2 \mathrm{~A}} \quad \begin{array}{l}
\text { Formulae } \\
\sin 3 \mathrm{~A}=3 \sin \mathrm{~A}-4 \sin ^{3} \mathrm{~A} \\
\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}=1-2 \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}
\end{array} \\
& =\frac{3 \sin \mathrm{~A}-4 \sin ^{3} \mathrm{~A}}{1+2\left(1-2 \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}\right)} \quad \text { sin } \mathrm{A} \text { is common in } \mathrm{Nr} \\
& =\frac{\sin \mathrm{A}\left(3-4 \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}\right)}{1+2-4 \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}} \\
& =\frac{\sin \mathrm{A}\left(3-4 \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}\right)}{\left(3-4 \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}\right)} \\
& =\sin \mathrm{A}=\text { RHS }
\end{aligned}$$
7. Prove that $4 \sin A \sin (60+A) \sin (60-A)=\sin 3 A$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
\mathrm{LHS} & =4 \sin \mathrm{~A} \sin (60+\mathrm{A}) \sin (60-\mathrm{A}) \\
& =4 \sin \mathrm{~A}\left[\sin ^{2} 60-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}\right]
\end{aligned}$$

Formula:
$$\sin (A+B) \sin (A-B)=\sin ^{2} A-\sin ^{2} B$$
$$\begin{aligned}
& =4 \sin \mathrm{~A}\left[\frac{3}{4}-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}\right] \begin{array}{l}
\sin 60=\frac{\sqrt{3}}{2} \\
\sin ^{2} 60=\frac{\sqrt{3}}{2} \times \frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}=\frac{3}{4}
\end{array} \\
& =4 \sin \mathrm{~A}\left[\frac{3-4 \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}}{4}\right] \\
& =\sin \mathrm{A}\left[3-4 \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}\right] \\
& =3 \sin \mathrm{~A}-4 \sin ^{3} \mathrm{~A}=\text { RHS }
\end{aligned}$$
8. Prove that $\frac{\sin 3 \mathrm{~A}}{\sin \mathrm{~A}}-\frac{\cos 3 \mathrm{~A}}{\cos \mathrm{~A}}=2$

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
\mathrm{LHS} & =\frac{\sin 3 \mathrm{~A}}{\sin \mathrm{~A}}-\frac{\cos 3 \mathrm{~A}}{\cos \mathrm{~A}} \\
& =\frac{\left(3 \sin \mathrm{~A}-4 \sin ^{3} \mathrm{~A}\right)}{\sin \mathrm{A}}-\frac{\left(4 \cos ^{3} \mathrm{~A}-3 \cos \mathrm{~A}\right)}{\cos \mathrm{A}} \\
& =\frac{\sin \mathrm{A}\left[3-4 \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}\right]}{\sin \mathrm{A}}-\frac{\cos \mathrm{A}\left[4 \cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}-3\right]}{\cos \mathrm{A}} \\
& =\left[3-4 \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}\right]-\left[4 \cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}-3\right] \\
& =3-4 \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}-4 \cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}+3 \\
& =6-4\left(\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}+\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}\right) \\
& =6-4(1) \quad \because \because \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}+\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}=1 \\
& =6-4=2=\mathrm{RHS}
\end{aligned}$$
9. Prove that $\frac{\cos ^{3} A-\cos 3 A}{\cos A}+\frac{\sin ^{3} A+\sin 3 A}{\sin A}=3$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\text { LHS }=\frac{\cos ^{3} A-\cos 3 A}{\cos A}+\frac{\sin ^{3} A+\sin 3 A}{\sin A}=3$$

Formulae
$$\begin{aligned}
& \begin{array}{l}
\sin 3 \mathrm{~A}=3 \sin \mathrm{~A}-4 \sin ^{3} \mathrm{~A} \\
\cos 3 \mathrm{~A}=4 \cos ^{3} \mathrm{~A}-3 \cos \mathrm{~A}
\end{array} \\
& =\frac{\cos ^{3} \mathrm{~A}-(4 \cos \mathrm{~A}+3 \cos \mathrm{~A})}{\cos \mathrm{A}}+\frac{\sin ^{3} \mathrm{~A}+3 \sin \mathrm{~A}-4 \sin ^{3} \mathrm{~A}}{\sin \mathrm{~A}} \\
& =\frac{\cos \mathrm{A}\left[\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}-4 \cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}+3\right]}{\cos \mathrm{A}}+\frac{\sin \mathrm{A}\left[\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}+3-4 \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}\right]}{\sin \mathrm{A}} \\
& =3-3 \cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}+3-3 \sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A} \\
& =6-3\left(\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~A}+\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}\right) \\
& =6-3(1)=6-3=3=\text { RHS }
\end{aligned}$$
10. Prove that $\cos 20^{\circ} \cos 40^{\circ} \cos 80^{\circ}=\frac{1}{8}$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
\mathrm{LHS} & =\cos 20^{\circ} \cos 40^{\circ} \cos 80^{\circ} \\
& =\cos 80^{\circ} \cos 40^{\circ} \cos 20^{\circ} \\
& =\cos \left(60^{\circ}+20^{\circ}\right) \cos \left(60^{\circ}+20^{\circ}\right) \cos 20^{\circ} \\
& =\left[\cos ^{2} 20-\sin ^{2} 60\right] \cos 20^{\circ} \\
& \begin{array}{l}
\text { Formula : } \\
\cos (\mathrm{A}+\mathrm{B}) \cos (\mathrm{A}-\mathrm{B}) \\
=\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~B}-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}
\end{array} \\
& =\left[\cos ^{2} 20-\frac{3}{4}\right] \cos 20^{\circ} \\
& =\frac{\left(4 \cos ^{2} 20-3\right)}{4} \cos 20^{\circ} \\
& =\frac{1}{4}\left(4 \cos ^{3} 20^{\circ}-3 \cos 20^{\circ}\right)=\frac{\sqrt{3}}{2} \sin ^{2} 60=\frac{\sqrt{3}}{2} \times \frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}=\frac{3}{4} \\
& =\frac{1}{4} \cos 3 \mathrm{~A}\left[\because \cos 3 \mathrm{~A}=4 \cos ^{3} \mathrm{~A}-3 \cos \mathrm{~A}\right] \\
& =\frac{1}{4} \cos (3 \times 20)=\frac{1}{4} \cos 60=\frac{1}{4} \times \frac{1}{2} \\
& =\frac{1}{8}=\mathrm{RHS}
\end{aligned}$$

\subsection*{3.3 SUM AND PRODUCT FORMULAE}

We know that
$$\begin{aligned}
& \sin (A+B)=\sin A \cos B+\cos A \sin B \\
& \sin (A-B)=\sin A \cos B-\cos A \sin B \\
& \cos (A+B)=\cos A \cos B-\sin A \sin B \\
& \cos (A-B)=\cos A \cos B+\sin A \sin B
\end{aligned}$$

Adding (1) and (2), we get
$$\sin (\mathrm{A}+\mathrm{B})+\sin (\mathrm{A}-\mathrm{B})=2 \sin \mathrm{~A} \cos \mathrm{~B}$$

Subtracting (2) from (1), we get
$$\sin (A+B)-\sin (A-B)=2 \cos A \sin B$$

Adding (3) and (4), we get
$$\cos (\mathrm{A}+\mathrm{B})+\cos (\mathrm{A}-\mathrm{B})=2 \cos \mathrm{~A} \cos \mathrm{~B}$$

Subtracting (4) from (3), we get
$$\cos (A+B)-\cos (A-B)=-2 \sin A \sin B$$

If we put,
$$\begin{aligned}
& \mathrm{A}+\mathrm{B}=\mathrm{C} \\
& \mathrm{~A}-\mathrm{B}=\mathrm{D}
\end{aligned}$$
then
(i) + (ii) $\Rightarrow 2 \mathrm{~A}=\mathrm{C}+\mathrm{D} \Rightarrow \mathrm{A}=\frac{\mathrm{C}+\mathrm{D}}{2}$
(i) - (ii) $\Rightarrow 2 \mathrm{~B}=\mathrm{C}-\mathrm{D} \Rightarrow \mathrm{B}=\frac{\mathrm{C}-\mathrm{D}}{2}$

Then the results (5), (6), (7) and (8) will become
$$\begin{aligned}
& \sin \mathrm{C}+\sin \mathrm{D}=2 \sin \left(\frac{\mathrm{C}+\mathrm{D}}{2}\right) \cos \left(\frac{\mathrm{C}-\mathrm{D}}{2}\right) \\
& \sin \mathrm{C}-\sin \mathrm{D}=2 \cos \left(\frac{\mathrm{C}+\mathrm{D}}{2}\right) \sin \left(\frac{\mathrm{C}-\mathrm{D}}{2}\right) \\
& \cos \mathrm{C}+\cos \mathrm{D}=2 \cos \left(\frac{\mathrm{C}+\mathrm{D}}{2}\right) \cos \left(\frac{\mathrm{C}-\mathrm{D}}{2}\right) \\
& \cos \mathrm{C}-\cos \mathrm{D}=-2 \sin \left(\frac{\mathrm{C}+\mathrm{D}}{2}\right) \sin \left(\frac{\mathrm{C}-\mathrm{D}}{2}\right)
\end{aligned}$$
$\qquad$
$\qquad$
$\qquad$
$\qquad$

The above results are known as sum and product formulae (because their LHS is sum \& difference and RHS is product). These formulae can be remembered by the short way
\begin{tabular}{l|l}
\hline $\mathrm{S}+\mathrm{S}=2 \mathrm{SC}$ & \\
$\mathrm{S}-\mathrm{S}=2 \mathrm{CS}$ & where \\
$\mathrm{C}+\mathrm{C}=2 \mathrm{CC}$ & $\mathrm{S}=\sin$ \\
$\mathrm{C}=\cos$
\end{tabular}

\subsection*{3.3 WORKED EXAMPLES \\ PART - A}
1. Express the following as sum or difference:
(i) $2 \sin 2 \mathrm{~A} \cos \mathrm{~A}$
(ii) $2 \cos 5 \mathrm{~A} \sin 3 \mathrm{~A}$
(iii) $2 \cos 3 \mathrm{~A} \cos 2 \mathrm{~A}$
(iv) $2 \sin 3 \mathrm{~A} \sin \mathrm{~A}$

\section*{Solution:}
(i) $2 \sin 2 \mathrm{~A} \cos \mathrm{~A} \quad 2 \mathrm{SC}=\mathrm{S}+\mathrm{S}$
$$\begin{aligned}
& =\sin (2 \mathrm{Add}+\mathrm{A})+\sin (2 \mathrm{~A}-\mathrm{A}) \\
& =\sin 3 \mathrm{~A}+\sin \mathrm{A}
\end{aligned}$$
(ii) $2 \cos 5 \mathrm{~A} \sin 3 \mathrm{~A} \quad 2 \mathrm{CS}=\mathrm{S}-\mathrm{S}$
$$\begin{aligned}
& =\sin \left(5 \mathrm{~A}^{\text {Add }}+3 \mathrm{~A}\right)-\sin \left(5 \mathrm{~A}^{\text {Subtract }}-3 \mathrm{~A}\right) \\
& =\sin 7 \mathrm{~A}+\sin 2 \mathrm{~A}
\end{aligned}$$
(iii) $2 \cos 3 \mathrm{~A} \cos 2 \mathrm{~A} \quad 2 \mathrm{CC}=\mathrm{C}+\mathrm{C}$
$$\begin{aligned}
& =\cos (3 \mathrm{~A}+2 \mathrm{~A})+\cos (3 \mathrm{~A}-2 \mathrm{~A}) \\
& =\cos 5 \mathrm{~A}+\cos \mathrm{A}
\end{aligned}$$
(iv) $2 \sin 3 \mathrm{~A} \sin \mathrm{~A} \quad \mathrm{C}-\mathrm{C}=-2 \mathrm{SS}$
$$\begin{aligned}
& =[2 \sin 3 \mathrm{~A} \sin \mathrm{~A}] \\
& =-[\cos (3 \mathrm{~A}+\mathrm{A})-\cos (3 \mathrm{~A}-\mathrm{A})] \\
& =-[\cos 4 \mathrm{~A}-\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}]=\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}-\cos 4 \mathrm{~A}
\end{aligned}$$
2. Express the following as product
i) $\sin 4 \mathrm{~A}+\sin 2 \mathrm{~A}$
(ii) $\sin 5 \mathrm{~A}-\sin 3 \mathrm{~A}$
iii) $\cos 7 \mathrm{~A}+\cos 3 \mathrm{~A}$
iv) $\cos 4 \mathrm{~A}-\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}$

\section*{Solution:}

\section*{Formula-(9)}
$$\begin{aligned}
& \text { i) } \begin{array}{l}
\sin 4 \mathrm{~A}+\sin 2 \mathrm{~A} \quad \mathrm{~S}+\mathrm{S}=2 \mathrm{SC} \\
= \\
=2 \sin \left(\frac{4 \mathrm{~A}+2 \mathrm{~A}}{2}\right) \cos \left(\frac{4 \mathrm{~A}-2 \mathrm{~A}}{2}\right) \\
=2 \sin \left(\frac{6 \mathrm{~A}}{2}\right) \cos \left(\frac{2 \mathrm{~A}}{2}\right) \\
=2 \sin 3 \mathrm{~A} \cos \mathrm{~A}
\end{array}
\end{aligned}$$
$$\begin{aligned}
& \text { ii) } \sin 5 \mathrm{~A}-\sin 3 \mathrm{~A} \quad \begin{array}{l}
\text { Formula }-(10) \\
=2 \cos \left(\frac{5 \mathrm{~A}+3 \mathrm{CS}}{2}\right) \sin \left(\frac{5 \mathrm{~A}-3 \mathrm{~A}}{2}\right) \\
=2 \sin \left(\frac{8 \mathrm{~A}}{2}\right) \cos \left(\frac{2 \mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)=2 \cos 4 \mathrm{~A} \sin \mathrm{~A}
\end{array}
\end{aligned}$$
iii) $\cos 7 \mathrm{~A}+\cos 3 \mathrm{~A} \quad \mathrm{C}+\mathrm{C}=2 \mathrm{CC}$
$$\begin{aligned}
& =2 \cos \left(\frac{7 \mathrm{~A}+3 \mathrm{~A}}{2}\right) \cos \left(\frac{7 \mathrm{~A}-3 \mathrm{~A}}{2}\right) \\
& =2 \cos \left(\frac{10 \mathrm{~A}}{2}\right) \cos \left(\frac{4 \mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)=2 \cos 5 \mathrm{~A} \cos 2 \mathrm{~A}
\end{aligned}$$
iv) $\cos 4 \mathrm{~A}-\cos 2 \mathrm{~A} \quad$\begin{tabular}{c} 
Formula-(12) \\
$\mathrm{C}-\mathrm{C}=-2 \mathrm{SS}$ \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
$=-2 \sin \left(\frac{4 \mathrm{~A}+2 \mathrm{~A}}{2}\right) \sin \left(\frac{4 \mathrm{~A}-2 \mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)$
$=-2 \sin \left(\frac{6 \mathrm{~A}}{2}\right) \sin \left(\frac{2 \mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)$
$=-2 \sin (3 \mathrm{~A}) \sin (\mathrm{A})$
3. Write $\sin 5 \mathrm{~A}-\sin 7 \mathrm{~A}$ in product form.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
& \sin 5 \mathrm{~A}-\sin 7 \mathrm{~A} \quad \mathrm{~S}-\mathrm{S}=2 \mathrm{CS} \\
& =2 \cos \left(\frac{5 \mathrm{~A}+7 \mathrm{~A}}{2}\right) \sin \left(\frac{5 \mathrm{~A}-7 \mathrm{~A}}{2}\right) \\
& =2 \cos \left(\frac{12 \mathrm{~A}}{2}\right) \sin \left(\frac{-2 \mathrm{~A}}{2}\right) \\
& =2 \cos (6 \mathrm{~A}) \sin (-\mathrm{A}) \\
& =2 \cos 6 \mathrm{~A}(-\sin \mathrm{A}) \\
& =-2 \cos 6 \mathrm{~A} \sin \mathrm{~A}
\end{aligned}$$
4. Write the product $2 \cos 4 \mathrm{~A} \cos 6 \mathrm{~A}$ as sum or difference of trigonometric function.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
& 2 \cos 4 A \cos 6 A \quad C+C=2 C C \\
& =\cos (4 A+6 A)+\cos (4 A-6 A) \\
& =\cos 10 A+\cos (-2 A) \quad \text { as }(-\theta) \text { is Quadrant-IV } \\
& =\cos 10 A+\cos 2 A
\end{aligned}$$

\section*{PART -B}
1. Prove that $\sin 50^{\circ}-\sin 70^{\circ}+\sin 10^{\circ}=0$

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{array}{rlr}
\mathrm{LHS} & =\sin 50^{\circ}+\sin 10^{\circ}-\sin 70^{\circ} \quad \mathrm{S}+\mathrm{S}=2 \mathrm{SC} \\
& =2 \sin \left(\frac{50^{\circ}+10^{\circ}}{2}\right) \cos \left(\frac{50^{\circ}-10^{\circ}}{2}\right)-\sin 70^{\circ} \\
& =2 \sin \left(\frac{60^{\circ}}{2}\right) \cos \left(\frac{40^{\circ}}{2}\right)-\sin 70^{\circ} \\
& =2 \sin \left(30^{\circ}\right) \cos \left(20^{\circ}\right)-\sin \left(90^{\circ}-20^{\circ}\right) \\
& =2 \times \frac{1}{2} \cos 20^{\circ}-\cos 20^{\circ} \quad \text { change of ratio for } 90^{\circ} \\
& =\cos 20^{\circ}-\cos 20^{\circ} \\
& =0=\mathrm{RHS}
\end{array}$$
2. Prove that $\cos 20^{\circ}+\cos 100^{\circ}+\cos 140^{\circ}=0$

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{array}{rlr}
\mathrm{LHS} & =\cos 140^{\circ}+\cos 100^{\circ}+\cos 20^{\circ} & \mathrm{C}+\mathrm{C}=2 \mathrm{CC} \\
& =2 \cos \left(\frac{140^{\circ}+100^{\circ}}{2}\right) \cos \left(\frac{140^{\circ}-100^{\circ}}{2}\right)+\cos 20^{\circ} \\
& =2 \cos \left(\frac{240^{\circ}}{2}\right) \cos \left(\frac{40^{\circ}}{2}\right)+\cos 20^{\circ} \\
& =2 \cos 120^{\circ} \cos 20^{\circ}+\cos 20^{\circ} & \\
& =2 \times-\frac{1}{2} \cos 20^{\circ}+\cos 20^{\circ} & \cos 120^{\circ}=\cos \left(180^{\circ}-60^{\circ}\right) \\
& =-\cos 20^{\circ}+\cos 20^{\circ} \\
& =0
\end{array}$$
3. Prove that $\cos \mathrm{A}+\cos \left(120^{\circ}+\mathrm{A}\right)+\cos \left(120^{\circ}-\mathrm{A}\right)=0$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
\mathrm{LHS} & =\cos \left(120^{\circ}+\mathrm{A}\right)+\cos \left(120^{\circ}-\mathrm{A}\right)+\cos \mathrm{A} \\
& =2 \cos \left[\frac{120^{\circ}+\mathrm{A}+120^{\circ}-\mathrm{A}}{2}\right] \cos \left[\frac{120^{\circ}+\mathrm{A}-\left(120^{\circ}-\mathrm{A}\right)}{2}\right]+\cos \mathrm{A} \\
& =2 \cos \left[\frac{240^{\circ}}{2}\right] \cos \left[\frac{120^{\circ}+\mathrm{A}-120+\mathrm{A}}{2}\right]+\cos \mathrm{A} \\
& =2 \cos \left(120^{\circ}\right) \cos \left(\frac{2 \mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)+\cos \mathrm{A} \\
& =2 \times-\frac{1}{2} \cos \mathrm{~A}+\cos \mathrm{A} \\
& =-\cos \mathrm{A}+\cos \mathrm{A} \\
& =0=\mathrm{RHS}
\end{aligned}$$
4. Prove that $\frac{\sin 2 \mathrm{~A}-\sin 2 \mathrm{~B}}{\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}+\cos 2 \mathrm{~B}}=\tan (\mathrm{A}+\mathrm{B})$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
\mathrm{LHS} & =\frac{\sin 2 \mathrm{~A}-\sin 2 \mathrm{~B}}{\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}+\cos 2 \mathrm{~B}} \quad \begin{array}{c}
\mathrm{S}-\mathrm{S}=2 \mathrm{CS} \\
\mathrm{C}+\mathrm{C}=2 \mathrm{CC}
\end{array} \\
& =\frac{2 \cos \left(\frac{2 \mathrm{~A}+2 \mathrm{~B}}{2}\right) \sin \left(\frac{2 \mathrm{~A}-2 \mathrm{~B}}{2}\right)}{2 \cos \left(\frac{2 \mathrm{~A}+2 \mathrm{~B}}{2}\right) \cos \left(\frac{2 \mathrm{~A}-2 \mathrm{~B}}{2}\right)} \\
& =\frac{2 \cos (\mathrm{~A}+\mathrm{B}) \sin (\mathrm{A}-\mathrm{B})}{2 \cos (\mathrm{~A}+\mathrm{B}) \cos (\mathrm{A}-\mathrm{B})} \\
& =\tan (\mathrm{A}-\mathrm{B})=\text { RHS }
\end{aligned}$$

\section*{PART - C}
1. Prove that $(\cos \alpha+\cos \beta)^{2}+(\sin \alpha+\sin \beta)^{2}=4 \cos ^{2}\left(\frac{\alpha-\beta}{2}\right)$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{gathered}
\text { LHS }=(\cos \alpha+\cos \beta)^{2}+(\sin \alpha+\sin \beta)^{2} \\
\mathrm{C}+\mathrm{C}=2 \mathrm{CC} \quad \mathrm{~S}+\mathrm{S}=2 \mathrm{SC}
\end{gathered}$$

Formulae
$=\left[2 \cos \left(\frac{\alpha+\beta}{2}\right) \cos \left(\frac{\alpha-\beta}{2}\right)\right]^{2}+\left[2 \sin \left(\frac{\alpha+\beta}{2}\right) \cos \left(\frac{\alpha-\beta}{2}\right)\right]^{2}$
$=4 \cos ^{2}\left(\frac{\alpha+\beta}{2}\right) \cos ^{2}\left(\frac{\alpha-\beta}{2}\right)+4 \sin ^{2}\left(\frac{\alpha+\beta}{2}\right) \cos ^{2}\left(\frac{\alpha-\beta}{2}\right)$
$4 \cos ^{2}\left(\frac{\alpha-\beta}{2}\right)$ is common for both the terms
$=4 \cos ^{2}\left(\frac{\alpha-\beta}{2}\right)\left[\cos ^{2}\left(\frac{\alpha+\beta}{2}\right)+\sin ^{2}\left(\frac{\alpha+\beta}{2}\right)\right]$
$=4 \cos ^{2}\left(\frac{\alpha-\beta}{2}\right) \times 1 \quad\left[\because \cos ^{2} \theta+\sin ^{2} \theta=1\right]$
$=4 \cos ^{2}\left(\frac{\alpha-\beta}{2}\right)=$ RHS
2. If $\sin \mathrm{x}+\sin \mathrm{y}=\mathrm{a}$ and $\cos \mathrm{x}+\cos \mathrm{y}=\mathrm{b}$. Prove that $\tan ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{x}-\mathrm{y}}{2}\right)=\frac{4-\mathrm{a}^{2}-\mathrm{b}^{2}}{\mathrm{a}^{2}+\mathrm{b}^{2}}$.

\section*{Solution:}

Given $\mathrm{a}=\sin \mathrm{x}+\sin \mathrm{y} \mathrm{b}=\cos \mathrm{x}+\cos \mathrm{y}$
$\therefore \mathrm{a}^{2}+\mathrm{b}^{2}$
$=[\sin x+\sin y]^{2}+[\cos x+\cos y]^{2}$
Formula $\mathrm{S}+\mathrm{S}=2 \mathrm{SC} \quad \mathrm{C}+\mathrm{C}=2 \mathrm{CC}$
$=\left[2 \sin \left(\frac{\mathrm{x}+\mathrm{y}}{2}\right) \cos \left(\frac{\mathrm{x}-\mathrm{y}}{2}\right)\right]^{2}+\left[2 \cos \left(\frac{\mathrm{x}+\mathrm{y}}{2}\right) \cos \left(\frac{\mathrm{x}-\mathrm{y}}{2}\right)\right]^{2}$
$=4 \sin ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{x}+\mathrm{y}}{2}\right) \cos ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{x}-\mathrm{y}}{2}\right)+4 \cos ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{x}+\mathrm{y}}{2}\right) \cos ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{x}-\mathrm{y}}{2}\right)$
$4 \cos ^{2}\left(\frac{x-y}{2}\right)$ is common to both are terms
$$\begin{aligned}
& =4 \cos ^{2}\left(\frac{x-y}{2}\right)\left[\sin ^{2}\left(\frac{x+y}{2}\right)+\cos ^{2}\left(\frac{x+y}{2}\right)\right] \\
& =4 \cos ^{2}\left(\frac{x-y}{2}\right) \times 1 \quad \because \sin ^{2} \theta+\cos ^{2} \theta=1 \\
a^{2}+b^{2} & =4 \cos ^{2}\left(\frac{x-y}{2}\right)
\end{aligned}$$
$$\begin{aligned}
\text { RHS } & =\frac{4-a^{2}-b^{2}}{\left(a^{2}+b^{2}\right)}=\frac{4-\left(a^{2}+b^{2}\right)}{\left(a^{2}+b^{2}\right)} \\
& =\frac{4-4 \cos ^{2}\left(\frac{x-y}{2}\right)}{4 \cos ^{2}\left(\frac{x-y}{2}\right)}=\frac{A\left[1-\cos ^{2}\left(\frac{x-y}{2}\right)\right]}{A \cos ^{2}\left(\frac{x-y}{2}\right)} \\
& =\frac{\sin ^{2}\left(\frac{x-y}{2}\right)}{\cos ^{2}\left(\frac{x-y}{2}\right)} \quad \because 1-\cos ^{2} \theta=\sin ^{2} \theta \\
& =\tan ^{2}\left(\frac{x-y}{2}\right)=\text { RHS }
\end{aligned}$$
3. If $\sin \mathrm{x}+\sin \mathrm{y}=\mathrm{a}$ and $\cos \mathrm{x}+\cos \mathrm{y}=\mathrm{b}$ prove that $\sin (\mathrm{x}+\mathrm{y})=\frac{2 \mathrm{ab}}{\mathrm{a}^{2}+\mathrm{b}^{2}}$

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
\mathrm{a}^{2}+\mathrm{b}^{2} & =4 \cos ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{x}-\mathrm{y}}{2}\right) \quad[\text { Refer Example 2] } \\
2 \mathrm{ab} & =2(\sin \mathrm{x}+\sin \mathrm{y})(\cos \mathrm{x}+\cos \mathrm{y}) \\
& \quad \mathrm{S}+\mathrm{S}=2 \mathrm{SC} \quad \mathrm{C}+\mathrm{C}=2 \mathrm{CC} \\
& =2\left[2 \sin \left(\frac{\mathrm{x}+\mathrm{y}}{2}\right) \cos \left(\frac{\mathrm{x}-\mathrm{y}}{2}\right)\right] \cdot 2 \cos \left(\frac{\mathrm{x}+\mathrm{y}}{2}\right) \cos \left(\frac{\mathrm{x}-\mathrm{y}}{2}\right) \\
& =8 \sin \left(\frac{\mathrm{x}+\mathrm{y}}{2}\right) \cos \left(\frac{\mathrm{x}+\mathrm{y}}{2}\right) \cos ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{x}-\mathrm{y}}{2}\right) \\
\text { RHS } & =\frac{2 \mathrm{ab}}{\mathrm{a}^{2}+\mathrm{b}^{2}}=\frac{2 \not 2 \sin \left(\frac{\mathrm{x}+\mathrm{y}}{2}\right) \cos \left(\frac{\mathrm{x}+\mathrm{y}}{2}\right) \cos ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{x}-\mathrm{y}}{2}\right)}{\not A \cos ^{2}\left(\frac{\mathrm{x}-\mathrm{y}}{2}\right)} \\
& =2 \sin \left(\frac{\mathrm{x}+\mathrm{y}}{2}\right) \cos \left(\frac{\mathrm{x}+\mathrm{y}}{2}\right) \\
& =2 \sin \theta \cos \theta=\sin 2 \theta \text { where } \theta=\frac{\mathrm{x}+\mathrm{y}}{2} \\
& =\sin \left[\not 2 \times \frac{(\mathrm{x}+\mathrm{y})}{\not 2}\right] \\
& =\sin (\mathrm{x}+\mathrm{y})=\mathrm{LHS}
\end{aligned}$$
4. Prove that $\frac{\sin \mathrm{A}+\sin 2 \mathrm{~A}+\sin 3 \mathrm{~A}}{\cos \mathrm{~A}+\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}+\cos 3 \mathrm{~A}}=\tan 2 \mathrm{~A}$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\text { LHS }=\frac{\frac{S+S=2 S C}{\sin 3 \mathrm{~A}+\sin \mathrm{A}}+\sin 2 \mathrm{~A}}{\mathrm{C}+=-2 \mathrm{CC}}, \frac{\cos 3 \mathrm{~A}+\cos \mathrm{A}}{\cos 2 \mathrm{c}}+\cos 2$$
$$\begin{aligned}
& =\frac{2 \sin \left(\frac{3 \mathrm{~A}+\mathrm{A}}{2}\right) \cos \left(\frac{3 \mathrm{~A}-\mathrm{A}}{2}\right)+\sin 2 \mathrm{~A}}{2 \cos \left(\frac{3 \mathrm{~A}+\mathrm{A}}{2}\right) \cos \left(\frac{3 \mathrm{~A}-\mathrm{A}}{2}\right)+\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}} \\
& =\frac{2 \sin \left(\frac{4 \mathrm{~A}}{2}\right) \cos \left(\frac{2 \mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)+\sin 2 \mathrm{~A}}{2 \cos \left(\frac{4 \mathrm{~A}}{2}\right) \cos \left(\frac{2 \mathrm{~A}}{2}\right)+\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}} \\
& =\frac{2 \sin (2 \mathrm{~A}) \cos \mathrm{A}+\sin 2 \mathrm{~A}}{2 \cos 2 \mathrm{~A} \cos \mathrm{~A}+\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}} \\
& = \\
& =\frac{\sin 2 \mathrm{~A}[2 \cos \mathrm{~A}+1]}{\cos 2 \mathrm{~A}[2 \cos \mathrm{~A}+1]} \\
& =\tan 2 \mathrm{~A}=\mathrm{RHS}
\end{aligned}$$

\section*{INVERSE TRIGONOMETRIC RATIOS AND DIFFERENTIAL CALCULUS-I}

Definition of inverse trigonometric ratios - Relation between inverse trigonometric ratios. Simple problems.
