Definition of Limits. Problems using the following results:
(i) $\lim _{x \rightarrow a} \frac{x^{n}-a^{n}}{x-a}=n a^{n-1}$
(ii) $\lim _{\theta \rightarrow 0} \frac{\sin \theta}{\theta}=1$ and
(iii) $\lim _{\theta \rightarrow 0} \frac{\tan \theta}{\theta}=1$ ( $\theta$ - in radians) (results only).

Simple Problems.

\subsection*{4.3 DIFFERENTIATION}

Definition - Differentiation of $x^{n}, \sin x, \cos x, \tan x, \operatorname{cosec} x, \sec x, \cot x, \log x, e x, u \pm v, u v, u v w, \frac{u}{v}(v$ $\neq 0$ ) (results only) Simple problems using the above results.

\subsection*{4.1 INVERSE TRIGONOMETRIC FUNCTIONS}

\section*{Definition:}

A function which is the reverse process of a trigonometric function is called the inverse trigonometric function.

The domain of a trigonometric function is the set angles and the range is the set of real numbers. In case of inverse trigonometric function, the domain is the set of real numbers and the range is the set of angles.

Inverse trigonometric function of $\sin \mathrm{x}$ is denoted as $\sin ^{-1} x$. Similarly $\cos ^{-1} x, \tan ^{-1} x, \sec ^{-1} x, \cot ^{-1} x$ and $\operatorname{cosec}^{-1} \mathrm{x}$ are the inverse trigonometric functions of $\cos x, \tan x, \sec x, \cot x$ and $\operatorname{cosec} x$ respectively.

\section*{Examples:}

We know that
$$\begin{array}{ll}
\sin 30^{\circ}=\frac{1}{2} & \therefore \sin ^{-1}\left(\frac{1}{2}\right)=30^{\circ} \\
\cos 0^{\circ}=1 & \therefore \cos ^{-1}(1)=0 \\
\tan 30^{\circ}=\frac{1}{\sqrt{3}} & \therefore \tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{1}{\sqrt{3}}\right)=30^{\circ} \\
\cot 45^{\circ}=1 & \therefore \cot ^{-1}(1)=45^{\circ}
\end{array}$$
$\sec 30^{\circ}=\frac{2}{\sqrt{3}} \quad \therefore \sec ^{-1}\left(\frac{2}{\sqrt{3}}\right)=30^{\circ}$
$\operatorname{cosec} 90^{\circ}=1 \quad \therefore \operatorname{cosec}^{-1}(1)=90^{\circ}$
If $x=\sin \theta \cdot \theta=\sin ^{-1} x$.
$\sin ^{-1} x$ is an angle.
There is a difference between $\sin ^{-1} \mathrm{x}$ and $(\sin \mathrm{x})^{-1} \cdot \sin ^{-1} \mathrm{x}$ is the inverse trigonometric function of $\sin \theta$ where as $(\sin x)^{-1}$ is the reciprocal of $\sin x$. i.e, $(\sin x)^{-1}=\frac{1}{\sin x}=\operatorname{cosec} x$.

\section*{Principal Value}

Among all the values, the numerically least value of the inverse trigonometric function is called principal value.

\section*{Examples:}
1) $\sin 30^{\circ}=\frac{1}{2}, \sin 150^{\circ}=\frac{1}{2}, \sin 390^{\circ}=\frac{1}{2}$
$\sin ^{-1}\left(\frac{1}{2}\right)=30^{\circ}, 150^{\circ}, 390^{\circ}$, $\qquad$
The least positive value is 30 ; which is called the principal value of $\sin ^{-1}\left(\frac{1}{2}\right)$.
2) $\cos 60^{\circ}=\frac{1}{2}, \cos 300^{\circ}=\frac{1}{2}, \cos \left(-60^{\circ}\right)=\frac{1}{2}, \cos 420^{\circ}=\frac{1}{2}$
$\cos ^{-1}\left(\frac{1}{2}\right)=60^{\circ}, 300^{\circ},-60^{\circ}, 4=0$
The principal value of $\cos ^{-1}\left(\frac{1}{2}\right)$ is $60^{\circ}$.
\begin{tabular}{lll} 
Function & Domain & Range of Principal value of $\theta$ \\
$\sin ^{-1} \mathrm{x}$ & $-1 \leq \mathrm{x} \leq 1$ & $-\pi / 2 \leq \theta \leq \pi / 2$ \\
$\cos ^{-1} \mathrm{x}$ & $-1 \leq \mathrm{x} \leq 1$ & $0 \leq \theta \leq \pi$ \\
$\tan ^{-1} \mathrm{x}$ & $(-\infty, \infty)$ & $-\pi / 2 \leq \theta \leq \pi / 2$ \\
$\cot ^{-1} \mathrm{x}$ & $(-\infty, \infty)$ & $-\pi / 2<\theta<\pi / 2$ \\
$\sec ^{-1} \mathrm{x}$ & $(-1,1)$ except 0 & $0<\theta<\pi, \theta \neq \pi / 2$ \\
$\operatorname{cosec}^{-1} \mathrm{x}$ & $(-1,1)$ except 0 & $-\pi / 2<\theta<\pi / 2, \theta \neq 0$
\end{tabular}

\section*{Properties}

\section*{Property (1) :}
(a) $\sin ^{-1}(\sin \mathrm{x})=\mathrm{x}$
(b) $\cos ^{-1}(\cos x)=x$
(c) $\tan ^{-1}(\tan \mathrm{x})=\mathrm{x}$
(d) $\cot ^{-1}(\cot x)=x$
(e) $\sec ^{-1}(\sec x)=x$
(f) $\operatorname{cosec}^{-1}(\operatorname{cosec} x)=x$

\section*{Proof:}
(a) Let $\sin x=y$
$$\begin{aligned}
& \therefore \quad \mathrm{x}=\sin ^{-1} \mathrm{y} \\
&=\sin ^{-1}(\sin \mathrm{x})[\text { from }(1) \\
& \therefore \quad \sin ^{-1}(\sin \mathrm{x})=\mathrm{x}
\end{aligned}$$

Similarly other results can be proved.

\section*{Property (2):}
(a) $\sin \left(\sin ^{-1} x\right)=x$
(b) $\cos \left(\cos ^{-1} x\right)=x$
(c) $\tan \left(\tan ^{-1} x\right)=x$
(d) $\cot \left(\cot ^{-1} x\right)=x$
(e) $\sec \left(\sec ^{-1} x\right)=x$
(f) $\operatorname{cosec}\left(\operatorname{cosec}^{-1} x\right)=x$

\section*{Proof:}
(b) Let $\cos ^{-1} \mathrm{x}=\mathrm{y}$

Then $\mathrm{x}=\cos \mathrm{y}$
$$=\cos \left(\cos ^{-1} x\right)[\text { From (1) }$$
$\therefore \cos \left(\cos ^{-1} \mathrm{x}\right)=\mathrm{x}$
Similarly other results can be proved.

\section*{Property (3):}
(a) $\sin ^{-1}\left(\frac{1}{x}\right)=\operatorname{cosec}^{-1}(x)$
(b) $\cos ^{-1}\left(\frac{1}{x}\right)=\sec ^{-1}(x)$
(c) $\tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{1}{x}\right)=\cot ^{-1}(x)$
(d) $\cot ^{-1}\left(\frac{1}{x}\right)=\tan ^{-1}(x)$
(e) $\sec ^{-1}\left(\frac{1}{x}\right)=\cos ^{-1}(x)$
(f) $\operatorname{cosec}^{-1}\left(\frac{1}{x}\right)=\sin ^{-1}(x)$

\section*{Proof:}
(c) Let $\tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{1}{x}\right)=y$
$\therefore \frac{1}{\mathrm{x}}=\tan \mathrm{y}$
$\therefore x=\frac{1}{\tan y}=\cot y$
$\therefore \mathrm{y}=\cot ^{-1}(\mathrm{x})$
From (1) \& (2), $\tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{1}{x}\right)=\cot ^{-1}(x)$
Similarly other results can be proved.

\section*{Property (4):}
(a) $\sin ^{-1}(-x)=-\sin ^{-1} x$
(b) $\cos ^{-1}(-x)=\pi-\cos ^{-1} x$
(c) $\tan ^{-1}(-x)=-\tan ^{-1} x$
(d) $\cot ^{-1}(-x)=-\cot ^{-1} x$
(e) $\sec ^{-1}(-x)=\pi-\sec ^{-1} x$
(f) $\operatorname{cosec}^{-1}(-x)=-\operatorname{cosec}^{-1} x$

\section*{Proof:}
(f) Let $\mathrm{y}=\operatorname{cosec}^{-1}(-\mathrm{x})$
$\therefore \operatorname{cosec} \mathrm{y}=-\mathrm{x}$
i.e., $\quad x=-\operatorname{cosec} y$
$$=\operatorname{cosec}(-y) \quad[\because \operatorname{cosec}(-y)=\operatorname{cosec}(2 \pi-y)=-\operatorname{cosec} y]$$
i.e., $\operatorname{cosec}^{-1}(\mathrm{x})=-\mathrm{y}$
$$=-\operatorname{cosec}^{-1}(-\mathrm{x}) \quad[\text { From }(1)$$
$\therefore \operatorname{cosec}^{-1}(-\mathrm{x})=-\operatorname{cosec}^{-1}(\mathrm{x})$
(e) Let $\mathrm{y}=\sec ^{-1}(-\mathrm{x})$
$$\begin{aligned}
\therefore & \sec y & =-x \\
\text { i.e., } & x & =-\sec y \\
& & =\sec (\pi-y) \quad[\sec (\pi-y)=-\sec y
\end{aligned}$$
i.e., $\quad \sec ^{-1} x=\pi-y$
$$\therefore \mathrm{y} \quad=\pi-\sec ^{-1} \mathrm{x}$$

From (1) \& (2), $\sec ^{-1}(-x)=\pi-\sec ^{-1} x$
Similarly other results can be proved.

\section*{Property (5):}
$$\begin{aligned}
& \sin ^{-1} \mathrm{X}+\cos ^{-1} \mathrm{X}=\frac{\pi}{2} \\
& \tan ^{-1} \mathrm{X}+\cot ^{-1} \mathrm{X}=\frac{\pi}{2} \\
& \sec ^{-1} \mathrm{X}+\operatorname{cosec}^{-1} \mathrm{X}=\frac{\pi}{2}
\end{aligned}$$

\section*{Proof:}

Let $\theta=\tan ^{-1} \mathrm{x}$
$$\therefore \mathrm{x}=\tan \theta$$
$$\begin{aligned}
& =\cot \left(\frac{\pi}{2}-\theta\right) \quad\left[\because \cot \left(90^{\circ}-\theta\right)=\tan \theta\right] \\
& =\cot ^{-1} x=\frac{\pi}{2}-\theta
\end{aligned}$$
$$=\frac{\pi}{2}-\tan ^{-1} \mathrm{x}$$
$$\therefore \tan ^{-1} \mathrm{x}+\cot ^{-1} \mathrm{x}=\frac{\pi}{2}$$

Similarly other results can be proved.

\section*{Property (6):}

If $x y<1, \tan ^{-1} x+\tan ^{-1} y=\tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{x+y}{1-x y}\right)$
Let $\mathrm{A}=\tan ^{-1} \mathrm{x} \quad \therefore \mathrm{x}=\tan \mathrm{A}$
Let $\mathrm{B}=\tan ^{-1} \mathrm{y} \quad \therefore \mathrm{y}=\tan \mathrm{B}$
Now,
$\tan (\mathrm{A}+\mathrm{B})=\frac{\tan \mathrm{A}+\tan \mathrm{B}}{1-\tan \mathrm{A} \tan \mathrm{B}}$
$=\frac{x+y}{1-x y}$
$\therefore(A+B)=\tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{\mathrm{x}+\mathrm{y}}{1-\mathrm{xy}}\right)$
i.e, $\tan ^{-1} x+\tan ^{-1} y=\tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{x+y}{1-x y}\right)$
[From (1) \& (2)

\section*{Property (7):}
$$\sin ^{-1} x+\sin ^{-1} y=\sin ^{-1}\left[x \sqrt{1-y^{2}}+y \sqrt{1-x^{2}}\right]$$

\section*{Proof:}
$$\begin{array}{ll}
\text { Let } \mathrm{A}=\sin ^{-1} \mathrm{x} & \therefore \mathrm{x}=\sin \mathrm{A} \\
\text { Let } \mathrm{B}=\sin ^{-1} \mathrm{y} & \therefore \mathrm{y}=\sin \mathrm{B}
\end{array}$$
$$\begin{aligned}
\sin (\mathrm{A}+\mathrm{B}) & =\sin \mathrm{A} \cos \mathrm{~B}+\cos \mathrm{A} \sin \mathrm{~B} \\
& =\sin \mathrm{A} \sqrt{1-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~B}}+\sqrt{1-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{~A}} \\
& =\mathrm{x} \sqrt{1-\mathrm{y}^{2}}+\sqrt{1-\mathrm{x}^{2}} \mathrm{y} \\
\mathrm{~A}+\mathrm{B} & =\sin ^{-1}\left[\mathrm{x} \sqrt{1-\mathrm{y}^{2}}+\mathrm{y} \sqrt{1-\mathrm{x}^{2}}\right]
\end{aligned}$$
i.e, $\sin ^{-1} x+\sin ^{-1} y=\sin ^{-1}\left[x \sqrt{1-y^{2}}+y \sqrt{1-x^{2}}\right]$
[From (1) \& (2)

\section*{Property (8):}
$$\cos ^{-1} x+\cos ^{-1} y=\cos ^{-1}\left[x y-\sqrt{1-x^{2}} \sqrt{1-y^{2}}\right]$$

\section*{Proof:}
$$\begin{array}{ll}
\text { Let } \mathrm{A}=\cos ^{-1} \mathrm{x} & \therefore \mathrm{x}=\cos \mathrm{A} \\
\text { Let } \mathrm{B}=\cos ^{-1} \mathrm{y} & \therefore \mathrm{y}=\cos \mathrm{B}
\end{array}$$
$$\text { Now, } \cos (\mathrm{A}+\mathrm{B})=\cos \mathrm{A} \cos \mathrm{~B}-\sin \mathrm{A} \sin \mathrm{~B}$$
$$\begin{aligned}
& =\cos A \cos B-\sqrt{1-\cos ^{2} A} \sqrt{1-\cos ^{2} \mathrm{~B}} \\
& =x y-\sqrt{1-x^{2}} \sqrt{1-y^{2}}
\end{aligned}$$
i.e., $A+B=\cos ^{-1}\left[x y-\sqrt{1-x^{2}} \sqrt{1-y^{2}}\right]$

\section*{From (1) \& (2)}
$$\cos ^{-1} x+\cos ^{-1} y=\cos ^{-1}\left[x y-\sqrt{1-x^{2}} \sqrt{1-y^{2}}\right]$$

\section*{WORKED EXAMPLES}

\section*{PART - A}
1. Find the principal value of
(i) $\sin ^{-1}\left(\frac{1}{\sqrt{2}}\right)$
(ii) $\cos ^{-1}\left(\frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}\right)$
(iii) $\tan ^{-1}\left(-\frac{1}{\sqrt{3}}\right)$
(iv) $\cot ^{-1}(-1)$
(v) $\sec ^{-1}(-2)$
(vi) $\operatorname{cosec}^{-1}\left(\frac{2}{\sqrt{3}}\right)$

\section*{Solution:}
(i) Let $\mathrm{x}=\sin ^{-1}\left(\frac{1}{\sqrt{2}}\right)$
$\therefore \sin \mathrm{x}=\frac{1}{\sqrt{2}}$
i.e, $\sin x=\sin 45^{\circ} \quad\left[\because \sin 45^{\circ}=\frac{1}{\sqrt{2}}\right]$
$\therefore \mathrm{x}=45^{\circ}$
$\therefore \sin ^{-1}\left(\frac{1}{\sqrt{2}}\right)=45^{\circ}$
(ii) Let $x=\cos ^{-1}\left(\frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}\right)$
$\therefore \cos x=\frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}$
$\cos x=\cos 30^{\circ} \quad\left[\because \cos 30=\frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}\right]$
$\therefore \mathrm{x}=30^{\circ}$
$\therefore \cos ^{-1}\left(\frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}\right)=30^{\circ}$
(iii) Let $\mathrm{x}=\tan ^{-1}\left(-\frac{1}{\sqrt{3}}\right)$
$\therefore \tan x=-\frac{1}{\sqrt{3}}$
$$=-\tan 30^{\circ} \quad\left[\because \tan 30=\frac{1}{\sqrt{3}}\right]$$
i.e., $\tan x=\tan ^{\circ}\left(-30^{\circ}\right) \quad[\because \tan (-\theta)=-\tan \theta]$
$\therefore \mathrm{x}=-30^{\circ}$
$\therefore \tan ^{-1}\left(-\frac{1}{\sqrt{3}}\right)=-30^{\circ}$
(iv) Let $x=\cot ^{-1}(-1)$
$$\begin{aligned}
\therefore \cot \mathrm{x} & =-1 \\
& =-\cot 45^{\circ}
\end{aligned}$$
i.e., $\cot x=\cot \left(-45^{\circ}\right)$
$\therefore \mathrm{x}=-45^{\circ}$
$\therefore \cot ^{-1}(-1)=-45^{\circ}$
(v) Let $\mathrm{x}=\sec ^{-1}(-2)$
$$\begin{aligned}
\therefore \sec x & =-2 \\
& =-\sec 60^{\circ} \\
\text { i.e., } \sec x & =\sec \left(120^{\circ}\right) \quad[\because \sec (120)=\sec (180-60)=-\sec 60
\end{aligned}$$
$\therefore \mathrm{x}=-120^{\circ}$
$\therefore \sec ^{-1}(-2)=120^{\circ}$
(v) Let $x=\operatorname{cosec}^{-1}\left(\frac{2}{\sqrt{3}}\right)$
$\therefore \operatorname{cosec} \mathrm{x}=\frac{2}{\sqrt{3}}$
$$=\operatorname{cosec} 60^{\circ} \quad\left[\because \operatorname{cosec} 60=\frac{1}{\sin 60}=\frac{1}{(\sqrt{3} / 2)}=\frac{2}{\sqrt{3}}\right.$$
$\therefore \mathrm{x}=60^{\circ}$
$\therefore \operatorname{cosec}^{-1}\left(\frac{2}{\sqrt{3}}\right)=60^{\circ}$
2. Prove that $\tan ^{-1} x+\tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{1}{x}\right)=\frac{\pi}{2}$

Solution:
$$\begin{aligned}
& \text { LHS }=\tan ^{-1} x+\tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{1}{x}\right) \\
& =\tan ^{-1} x+\cot ^{-1}(x) \quad[\text { By property } 3 \\
& =\frac{\pi}{2} \quad \quad \text { By property } 5
\end{aligned}$$

\section*{PART - B}
1. Prove that $\sin ^{-1}\left(\sqrt{1-x^{2}}\right)=\cos ^{-1} x$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
& \text { Put } x=\cos \theta \quad \therefore \theta=\cos ^{-1} \mathrm{x} \\
& \text { Now, LHS }
\end{aligned} \begin{aligned}
& \sin ^{-1}\left(\sqrt{1-\mathrm{x}^{2}}\right) \\
& =\sin ^{-1}\left(\sqrt{1-\cos ^{2} \theta}\right) \\
& =\sin ^{-1}\left(\sqrt{1-\sin ^{2} \theta}\right) \\
& =\sin ^{-1}(\sin \theta) \\
& =\theta \quad[\text { By Property } 1 \\
& =\cos ^{-1} \mathrm{x} \quad[\text { By }(1)
\end{aligned}$$
2. Prove that $\tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{1}{3}\right)+\tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{2}{5}\right)=\tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{11}{13}\right)$.

\section*{Solution:}

We know, $\tan ^{-1} x+\tan ^{-1} y=\tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{x+y}{1-x y}\right)$
$$\begin{aligned}
\therefore \tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{1}{3}\right)+\tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{2}{5}\right) & =\tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{\frac{1}{3}+\frac{2}{5}}{1-\frac{1}{3} \cdot \frac{2}{5}}\right) \\
& =\tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{\frac{5+6}{15}}{\frac{15-2}{15}}\right) \\
& =\tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{11}{13}\right)
\end{aligned}$$

\section*{PART - C}
1. Show that $2 \tan ^{-1} \mathrm{x}=\cos ^{-1}\left(\frac{1-\mathrm{x}^{2}}{1+\mathrm{x}^{2}}\right)$

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
& \text { Let } \mathrm{x}=\tan \theta \quad \therefore \theta=\tan ^{-1} \mathrm{x} \\
& \begin{aligned}
\text { R.H.S } & =\cos ^{-1}\left(\frac{1-\mathrm{x}^{2}}{1+\mathrm{x}^{2}}\right) \\
& =\cos ^{-1}\left(\frac{1-\tan ^{2} \theta}{1+\tan ^{2} \theta}\right) \\
& =\cos ^{-1}(\cos 2 \theta) \\
& =2 \theta \\
& =2 \tan ^{-1} \mathrm{x}=\text { L.H.S }
\end{aligned}
\end{aligned}$$
2. Show that $\tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{3 x-x^{2}}{1-3 x^{2}}\right)=3 \tan ^{-1} x$.

\section*{Solution:}

Let $\mathrm{x}=\tan \theta \quad \therefore \theta=\tan ^{-1} \mathrm{x}$
$$\begin{aligned}
\text { LHS } & =\tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{3 x-x^{2}}{1-3 x^{2}}\right) \\
& =\tan ^{-1}\left[\frac{3 \tan \theta-\tan ^{2} \theta}{1-3 \tan ^{2} \theta}\right] \\
& =\tan ^{-1}(\tan 3 \theta) \\
& =3 \theta \\
& =3 \tan ^{-1} x \\
& =\text { RHS }
\end{aligned} \quad \text { [From (1) }$$
3. Show that $2 \tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{2}{3}\right)=\tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{12}{15}\right)$

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
\text { LHS } & =2 \tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{2}{3}\right) \\
& =\tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{2}{3}\right)+\tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{2}{3}\right) \\
& =\tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{\frac{2}{3}+\frac{2}{3}}{1-\frac{2}{3} \cdot \frac{2}{3}}\right) \\
& =\tan ^{-1}\left[\frac{\frac{4}{3}}{\frac{9-4}{9}}\right] \\
& =\tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{4}{3} \times \frac{9}{5}\right) \\
& =\tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{12}{5}\right)=\text { RHS }
\end{aligned}$$
4. Evaluate $\tan \left[\cos ^{-1}\left(\frac{8}{17}\right)\right]$.

\section*{Solution:}

Let $\cos ^{-1}\left(\frac{8}{17}\right)=\theta$
$\therefore \cos \theta=\frac{8}{17}$
$\mathrm{AB}^{2}=\mathrm{AC}^{2}-\mathrm{BC}^{2}=17^{2}-8^{2}$
$=289-64=225$
$\therefore \mathrm{AB}=\sqrt{225}=15$
![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/2025_05_07_b62b456faa89cfbc166dg-116.jpg?height=268&width=445&top_left_y=1447&top_left_x=1192)
$\therefore \tan \theta=\frac{\mathrm{AB}}{\mathrm{BC}}=\frac{15}{8}$
$\therefore \theta=\tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{15}{8}\right)$
From (1) \& (2), $\cos ^{-1}\left(\frac{8}{17}\right)=\tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{15}{8}\right)$
$\therefore \tan \left[\cos ^{-1}\left(\frac{8}{17}\right)\right]=\tan \left[\tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{15}{8}\right)\right]$
$=\frac{15}{8}$

\subsection*{4.2 LIMITS}

Mlathematical quantities can be divided into two (i) constants and (ii) Variables
The quantitity which does not change in its value is called constant.
Constants can be divided (i) Absolute constants and (ii) Arbitrary constants
Absolute constants are those which retain in values at any time and at any place.

\section*{Examples:}

Numbers $5,-7,3, \frac{-11}{27}, \pi$, e, $\sqrt{2}, \sqrt{3}$, $\qquad$ etc. are absolute constants.
Arbitrary constants are those which are constants in a particular problem but changes from problem to problem. They are represented as $\mathrm{a}, \mathrm{b}, \mathrm{c}, \mathrm{f}, \mathrm{g}, \mathrm{h}$, $\qquad$ etc.

\section*{Examples:}
(i) $\mathrm{ax}+\mathrm{by}+\mathrm{c}=0-\mathrm{a}, \mathrm{b}, \mathrm{c}$
(ii) $x^{2}+y^{2}+2 g x+2 f y+c=0-f, g$, h. $\qquad$ .ex.
Variables are those which vary in their values. They are represented as $u, v, w, x, y, \theta$, $\qquad$
Variables can be divided into two (i) Independent variable and (ii) Dependent varaible.
In the equation $\mathrm{y}=\mathrm{x}^{2}, \mathrm{x}$ is the independent variable and y is the dependent variable depending on x
For example, if x takes the value 2 , y takes the value 4 . If x takes -3 , y takes 9 $\qquad$ etc.
The relation or equation or connection between two variables is called a function and is denoted as $\mathrm{f}(\mathrm{x})$.

Example: $\mathrm{y}=\mathrm{f}(\mathrm{x})=\mathrm{x}^{2}$ or $\sin \mathrm{x}$.
The value of $f(x)$ at $x=a$ is $f(a)$ and is called the functional value of $f(x)$ at $x=a$.
If for every function, if the functional value at every point of its domain exists, there is no need to study Limit chapter and from that the famous CALCULS.

For example, $f(x)=\frac{x^{2}-4}{x-2}$ at $x=2$ i.e, $f(2)$ does not exist, since $f(2)=\frac{0}{0}$, the indeterminant quantity. Similarly there are two more indeterminant quantities $\frac{\infty}{\infty}$ and $\infty-\infty$.

But, as x approaches $2, \mathrm{f}(\mathrm{x})=\frac{\mathrm{x}^{2}-4}{\mathrm{x}-2}$ will approach 4 .
\begin{tabular}{|c|c|c|c|c|c|c|c|}
\hline x & 1 & 1.5 & 1.9 & 1.99 & 1.999 & 1.9999 & $\ldots \ldots$ \\
\hline$y=\frac{x^{2}-4}{\mathrm{x}-2}$ & 3 & 3.5 & 3.9 & 3.99 & 3.999 & 3.9999 & $\ldots \ldots$
\end{tabular}$\rightarrow 4$

Hence the approachment value 4 of the function $\frac{x^{2}-4}{x-2}$ as $x$ approaches 2 is called the limit value of the function.

\section*{Definition of Limit:}

When the variable x approaches a constant a and if the function $\mathrm{f}(\mathrm{x})$ approaches a constant $l$, then $l$ is called the limit value of $\mathrm{f}(\mathrm{x})$ as x approaches a and is denotd as
$$\operatorname{Ltf}_{x \rightarrow \mathrm{a}} \mathrm{f}(\mathrm{x})=1$$

\section*{Results:}
1) $\underset{x \rightarrow a}{\operatorname{Lt}}[f(x)+g(x)]=\underset{x \rightarrow a}{\operatorname{Lt}} f(x) \pm \underset{x \rightarrow a}{\operatorname{Lt}} g(x)$
![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/2025_05_07_b62b456faa89cfbc166dg-118.jpg?height=66&width=751&top_left_y=273&top_left_x=206)
3) $\underset{x \rightarrow a}{\operatorname{Lt}}[f(x) \cdot g(x)]=\underset{x \rightarrow a}{\operatorname{Lt} f(x)} \underset{x \rightarrow a}{\operatorname{Lt} g(x)}$
4) $\underset{x \rightarrow a}{\operatorname{Lt}}\left[\frac{f(x)}{g(x)}\right]=\frac{\underset{x \rightarrow a}{\operatorname{Lt} f(x)}}{\underset{x \rightarrow a}{\operatorname{Lt}} g(x)}$, provided $\underset{x \rightarrow a}{\operatorname{Lt} g(x) \neq 0}$

\section*{Formulae:}
1) $\underset{x \rightarrow a}{ } \operatorname{Lt} \frac{x^{n}-a^{n}}{x-a}=n a^{n-1}$, for all values of $x$.
2) $\underset{x \rightarrow a}{ } \frac{\sin \theta}{\theta}=1$
3) $\underset{x \rightarrow a}{\operatorname{Lt}} \frac{\tan \theta}{\theta}=1, \theta$ in radians

Now,
$$\begin{array}{rlrl}
\underset{\theta \rightarrow 0}{\mathrm{Lt}} \frac{\sin \mathrm{n} \theta}{\theta} & =\underset{\theta \rightarrow 0}{\mathrm{Lt}}\left[\frac{\sin \mathrm{n} \theta}{\mathrm{n} \theta} \cdot \mathrm{n}\right] & & \\
& =\mathrm{n} \operatorname{Lt}_{\theta \rightarrow 0}\left(\frac{\sin \mathrm{n} \theta}{\mathrm{n} \theta}\right) & & {\left[\mathrm{By} \mathrm{R}_{2}\right.} \\
& =\mathrm{n} .1 & & {\left[\mathrm{By} \mathrm{~F}_{2}\right.} \\
& =\mathrm{n} &
\end{array}$$

Similarly, $\underset{\theta \rightarrow 0}{\mathrm{Lt}} \frac{\tan \mathrm{n} \theta}{\theta}=\mathrm{n}$

\section*{WORKED EXAMPLES \\ PART - A}
1. Evaluate $\underset{\theta \rightarrow 0}{\operatorname{Lt}} \frac{3 \mathrm{x}^{2}+2 \mathrm{x}+1}{5 \mathrm{x}^{2}+6 \mathrm{x}+7}$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
\underset{\theta \rightarrow 0}{\operatorname{Lt}} \frac{3 x^{2}+2 x+1}{5 x^{2}+6 x+7} & =\frac{3(0)^{2}+2(0)+1}{5(0)^{2}+6(0)+7} \\
& =\frac{1}{7}
\end{aligned}$$
2. Evaluate $\underset{x \rightarrow 0}{\operatorname{Lt}} \frac{3 x^{2}+4 x}{5 x-7 x^{2}}$

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
\operatorname{Lt}_{x \rightarrow 0} \frac{3 x^{2}+4 x}{5 x-7 x^{2}} & =\underset{x \rightarrow 0}{\operatorname{Lt}} \frac{x(3 x-4)}{x(5-7 x)} \\
& =\frac{3.0-4}{5-7.0} \\
& =\frac{-4}{5}=-\frac{4}{5}
\end{aligned}$$
3. Evaluate: $\underset{\theta \rightarrow 0}{\mathrm{Lt}} \frac{\sin 7 \theta}{0}$

Solution:
$$\begin{aligned}
& \underset{\theta \rightarrow 0}{\mathrm{Lt}} \frac{\sin 7 \theta}{\theta}=\underset{\theta \rightarrow 0}{\mathrm{Lt}}\left[\frac{\sin 7 \theta}{7 \theta} .7\right] \\
& =7 \mathrm{Lt} \frac{\sin 7 \theta}{7 \theta}
\end{aligned}$$
7.1

7

\section*{PART - B}
1. Evaluate: $\operatorname{Lt}_{x \rightarrow 1} \frac{x^{2}+x-2}{x^{2}-4 x+3}$

Solution:
$\operatorname{Lt}_{x \rightarrow 1} \frac{x^{2}+x-2}{x^{2}-4 x+3}=\frac{1+1-2}{1-4(1)+3}=\frac{2-2}{4-4}=\frac{0}{0}$ Indeterminent
$$\begin{aligned}
\operatorname{Lt}_{x \rightarrow 1} \frac{x^{2}+x-2}{x^{2}-4 x+3} & =\underset{x \rightarrow 1}{\operatorname{Lt}} \frac{(x+2)(x-1)}{(x-1)(x-3)} \\
& =\underset{x \rightarrow 1}{\operatorname{Lt}} \frac{x+2}{x-3} \\
& =\frac{1+2}{1-3}=\frac{3}{-2}=-\frac{3}{2}
\end{aligned}$$
2. Evaluate $\underset{x \rightarrow 2}{\operatorname{Lt}} \frac{x^{10}-2^{10}}{x-2}$.

Solution:
$$\begin{aligned}
\operatorname{Lt}_{x \rightarrow 2} \frac{\mathrm{x}^{10}-2^{10}}{\mathrm{x}-2} & =10.2^{10-1} \quad\left[\text { By F1 } \underset{\mathrm{x} \rightarrow \mathrm{a}}{\mathrm{Lt}} \frac{\mathrm{x}^{\mathrm{n}}-\mathrm{a}^{\mathrm{n}}}{\mathrm{x}-\mathrm{a}}=\mathrm{na}{ }^{\mathrm{n}-1}\right] \\
& =10.2^{9} \\
& =10 \times 512 \\
& =5120
\end{aligned}$$
3. Evaluate $\operatorname{Lt}_{x \rightarrow a} \frac{\sqrt{x}-\sqrt{a}}{x-a}$.

Solution:
$$\begin{aligned}
\operatorname{Lt}_{x \rightarrow a} \frac{\sqrt{x}-\sqrt{a}}{x-a} & =\underset{x \rightarrow a}{\operatorname{Lt}} \frac{x^{1 / 2}-a^{1 / 2}}{x-a} \\
& =\frac{1}{2} \cdot a^{1 / 2^{-1}} \\
& =\frac{1}{2} a^{-1 / 2} \\
& =\frac{1}{2} \cdot \frac{1}{a^{1 / 2}}=\frac{1}{2 \sqrt{a}}
\end{aligned}$$
4. Evaluate $\underset{x \rightarrow 0}{\operatorname{Lt}} \frac{\sin 5 x}{4 x}$

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{array}{ll}
\operatorname{Lt}_{x \rightarrow 0} \frac{\sin 5 x}{4 x}=\frac{1}{4} \underset{x \rightarrow 0}{\operatorname{Lt}} \frac{\sin 5 x}{x}=\frac{1}{4} \underset{x \rightarrow 0}{\operatorname{Lt}}\left[\frac{\sin 5 x}{5 x} \times 5\right] \\
=\frac{1}{4} \times 5 \underset{x \rightarrow 0}{\mathrm{Lt}} \frac{\sin 5 x}{5 x} & {\left[\begin{array}{l}
\operatorname{By~F}_{2} \\
\operatorname{Lt}_{x \rightarrow 0} \frac{\sin \theta}{\theta}=1
\end{array}\right.} \\
=\frac{5}{4} \cdot 1=\frac{5}{4} &
\end{array}$$
5. Evaluate $\underset{x \rightarrow 0}{\operatorname{Lt}} \frac{\tan ^{2} 5 x}{x^{2}}$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
\underset{x \rightarrow 0}{\mathrm{Lt}} \frac{\tan ^{2} 5 \mathrm{x}}{\mathrm{x}^{2}} & =\underset{\mathrm{x} \rightarrow \mathrm{a}}{\mathrm{Lt}}\left(\frac{\tan 5 \mathrm{x}}{\mathrm{x}}\right)^{2} \\
& =\underset{\mathrm{x} \rightarrow 0}{\mathrm{Lt}}\left[\frac{\tan 5 \mathrm{x}}{5 \mathrm{x}} \cdot 5\right]^{2} \\
& =\underset{\mathrm{xt} \rightarrow 0}{\mathrm{Lt}}\left(\frac{\tan 5 \mathrm{x}}{5 \mathrm{x}}\right)^{2} \times 25 \quad\left[\begin{array}{l}
\operatorname{By~F}_{3} \\
\operatorname{Lt}_{\theta \rightarrow 0}^{\tan \theta} \\
\theta
\end{array}=1\right. \\
& =25 \underset{\mathrm{x} \rightarrow \mathrm{a}}{\mathrm{Lt}}\left(\frac{\tan 5 \mathrm{x}}{5 \mathrm{x}}\right)^{2} \\
& =25.1^{2}=25
\end{aligned}$$

\section*{PART - C}
1. Evaluate $\underset{x \rightarrow 3}{\operatorname{Lt}} \frac{x^{5}-243}{x^{2}-9}$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
\operatorname{Lt}_{x \rightarrow 3} \frac{x^{5}-243}{x^{2}-9} & =\underset{x \rightarrow 3}{\operatorname{Lt}} \frac{x^{5}-3^{5}}{x^{2}-9} \\
& =\underset{x \rightarrow 3}{\operatorname{Lt}}\left[\frac{x^{5}-3^{5}}{x-3} \times \frac{x-3}{x^{2}-3^{2}}\right] \\
& =\operatorname{Lt}_{x \rightarrow 3}\left[\frac{x^{5}-3^{5}}{x-3} / \frac{x^{2}-3^{2}}{x-3}\right] \\
& =\frac{\operatorname{Lt} \frac{x^{5}-3^{5}}{x-3}}{\operatorname{Lt} \frac{x^{2}-3^{2}}{x-3}} \quad \quad[\text { By } \\
& =\frac{5.3^{5-1}}{2.3^{2-1}}=\frac{5.3^{4}}{2.3^{1}} \\
& =\frac{5}{2} \times 3^{3}=\frac{5}{2} \times 27=\frac{135}{2}
\end{aligned}$$
2. Evaluate : $\underset{x \rightarrow 4}{\operatorname{Lt}} \frac{x^{7 / 3}-4^{7 / 3}}{x^{2 / 3}-4^{2 / 3}}$

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
\operatorname{Lt}_{x \rightarrow 4} \frac{x^{7 / 3}-4^{7 / 3}}{x^{2 / 3}}-4^{2 / 3} & =\underset{x \rightarrow 4}{\operatorname{Lt}}\left[\frac{x^{7 / 3}-4^{7 / 3}}{x-4} \times \frac{x-4}{x^{2 / 3}-4^{2 / 3}}\right] \\
& =\underset{x \rightarrow 4}{\operatorname{Lt}}\left[\frac{x^{7 / 3}-4^{7 / 3}}{x-4} / \frac{x^{2 / 3}-4^{2 / 3}}{x-4}\right]
\end{aligned}$$
$=\frac{\operatorname{Lt}_{x \rightarrow 4} \frac{x^{7 / 3}-4^{7 / 3}}{x-4}}{\underset{x \rightarrow 4}{\operatorname{Lt}^{2 / 3}-4^{2 / 3}}}$
$=\frac{\frac{7}{3} \cdot 4^{\frac{7}{3}-1}}{\frac{2}{3} \cdot 4^{\frac{2}{3}-1}}=\frac{\frac{7}{3} \cdot 4^{4 / 3}}{\frac{2}{3} \cdot 4^{-1 / 3}}$
$=\frac{7}{3} \times \frac{3}{2} \times 4^{4 / 3+1 / 3}=\frac{7}{2} 4^{5 / 3}$
3. Evaluate $\underset{\theta \rightarrow 0}{\mathrm{Lt} \frac{\sin 8 \theta}{\tan 3 \theta}}$.

Solution:
$$\begin{aligned}
\underset{\theta \rightarrow 0}{\mathrm{Lt}} \frac{\sin 8 \theta}{\tan 3 \theta} & =\underset{\theta \rightarrow 0}{\mathrm{Lt}}\left[\frac{\sin 8 \theta}{8 \theta} \times \frac{3 \theta}{\tan 3 \theta}\right] \times \frac{8}{3} \\
& =\underset{\theta \rightarrow 0}{\mathrm{Lt}}\left[\frac{\sin 8 \theta}{8 \theta} / \frac{\tan 3 \theta}{3 \theta}\right] \times \frac{8}{3} \\
& =\frac{8}{3} \frac{\mathrm{Lt} \rightarrow 0}{\mathrm{Lt} \frac{\sin 8 \theta}{8 \theta}} \\
& =\frac{8}{3} \cdot \frac{1}{1}=\frac{8}{3} 3
\end{aligned}$$

\subsection*{4.3 DIFFERENTIATION}

Let $y=f(x)$ (1) be a function of $x$.
Let $\Delta x$ be a small increment in $x$ and let $\Delta y$ be the corresponding increment in $y$.
$\therefore y+\Delta y=f(x+\Delta x)$
(2) - (1) $\quad \Delta y=f(x+\Delta x)-f(x)$
$\therefore \frac{\Delta \mathrm{y}}{\Delta \mathrm{x}}=\frac{\mathrm{f}(\mathrm{x}+\Delta \mathrm{x})-\mathrm{f}(\mathrm{x})}{\Delta \mathrm{x}}$
Taking the limit as $\Delta \mathrm{x} \rightarrow 0$,
$\underset{\Delta \mathrm{x} \rightarrow 0}{\mathrm{Lt}} \frac{\Delta \mathrm{y}}{\Delta \mathrm{x}}=\underset{\Delta \mathrm{x} \rightarrow 0}{\mathrm{Lt}} \frac{\mathrm{f}(\mathrm{x}+\Delta \mathrm{x})-\mathrm{f}(\mathrm{x})}{\Delta \mathrm{x}}$
$\underset{\Delta \mathrm{x} \rightarrow 0}{\mathrm{Lt}} \frac{\Delta \mathrm{y}}{\Delta \mathrm{x}}$ is called the differential coefficient of y with respect to x and is denoted as $\frac{\mathrm{dy}}{\mathrm{dx}}$.
$\therefore \frac{d y}{d x}=\operatorname{Lt}_{\Delta x \rightarrow 0} \frac{f(x+\Delta x)-f(x)}{\Delta x}$

\section*{List of formulae:}
(1) $\frac{d}{d x}\left(x^{n}\right)=n x^{n-1}, n$ a real number
(2) $\frac{d}{d x}(\sqrt{x})=\frac{1}{2 \sqrt{x}}$
(3) $\frac{d}{d x}\left(e^{x}\right)=e^{x}$
(4) $\frac{d}{d x}(\log x)=\frac{1}{x}$
(5) $\frac{d}{d x}(\sin x)=\cos x$
(6) $\frac{d}{d x}(\cos x)=-\sin x$
(7) $\frac{d}{d x}(\tan x)=\sec ^{2} x$
(8) $\frac{d}{d x}(\cot x)=-\operatorname{cosec}^{2} x$
(9) $\frac{d}{d x}(\sec x)=\sec x \tan x$
(10) $\frac{d}{d x}(\operatorname{cosec} x)=-\operatorname{cosec} x \cot x$

\section*{Results:}
1) If $u$ and $v$ are functions of $x$,
$$\frac{d}{d x}(u \pm v)=\frac{d u}{d x} \pm \frac{d v}{d x}$$
2) $\frac{d}{d x}(k u)=k \frac{d u}{d x}$, where $k$ is a constant.
3) $\frac{d}{d x}($ any constant $)=0$
4) Product Rule of Differentiation

If $u \& v$ are two functions of $x$,
$$\frac{d}{d x}(u v)=u \frac{d v}{d x}+v \frac{d u}{d x}$$
5) $\frac{d}{d x}(u \vee v)=u v \frac{d w}{d x}+v w \frac{d u}{d x}+w u \frac{d v}{d x}$, where $u$, $v$ and $w$ are function of $x$.
6) Quotient Rule of Differentiation

If $u \& v$ are functions of $x$,
$\frac{d}{d x}\left(\frac{u}{v}\right)=\frac{v \frac{d u}{d x}-u \frac{d v}{d x}}{v^{2}}$

\section*{WORKED EXAMPLES}

\section*{PART - A}
1. Find $\frac{d y}{d x}$ if
(i) $y=\frac{1}{x^{2}}$
(ii) $\mathrm{y}=\mathrm{x}^{3}+2$
(iii) $y=\frac{1}{\sqrt{x}}$
(iv) $y=\sqrt{x}$
(v) $y=\frac{1}{\sin x}$
(vi) $y=9 \sqrt{x}+x^{2}$

\section*{Solution:}
(i) $y=\frac{1}{x^{2}}=x^{-2}$
$\therefore \frac{\mathrm{dy}}{\mathrm{dx}}=\frac{\mathrm{d}}{\mathrm{dx}}\left(\mathrm{x}^{-2}\right)=-2 \mathrm{x}^{-3}=-\frac{2}{\mathrm{x}^{3}}$
(ii) $y=x^{3}+2$
$\therefore \frac{\mathrm{dy}}{\mathrm{dx}}=\frac{\mathrm{d}}{\mathrm{dx}}\left(\mathrm{x}^{3}+2\right)=\frac{\mathrm{d}}{\mathrm{dx}}\left(\mathrm{x}^{3}\right)+\frac{\mathrm{d}}{\mathrm{dx}}(2)=3 \mathrm{x}^{2}+0=3 \mathrm{x}^{2}$
(iii) $\mathrm{y}=\frac{1}{\sqrt{\mathrm{x}}}=\frac{1}{\mathrm{x}^{1 / 2}}=\mathrm{x}^{-1 / 2}$
$\therefore \frac{d y}{d x}=\frac{d}{d x}\left(x^{-1 / 2}\right)=-\frac{1}{2} \mathrm{x}^{-\frac{1}{2}-1}=-\frac{1}{2} \mathrm{x}^{-3 / 2}=-\frac{1}{2 \mathrm{x}^{3 / 2}}$
(iv) $y=\sqrt{x}=x^{1 / 2}$
$\frac{d y}{d x}=\frac{d}{d x}\left(x^{1 / 2}\right)=\frac{1}{2} x^{-\frac{1}{2}-1}=\frac{1}{2} x^{-1 / 2}=\frac{1}{2} \cdot \frac{1}{x^{1 / 2}}=\frac{1}{2 \sqrt{x}}$
(v) $y=\frac{1}{\sin x}=\operatorname{cosec} x$
$\therefore \frac{\mathrm{dy}}{\mathrm{dx}}=\frac{\mathrm{d}}{\mathrm{dx}}(\operatorname{cosec} \mathrm{x})=-\operatorname{cosec} \mathrm{x} \cot \mathrm{x}$
(vi) $y=9 \sqrt{x}+x^{2}$
$$\begin{aligned}
& \therefore \frac{\mathrm{dy}}{\mathrm{dx}}=\frac{\mathrm{d}}{\mathrm{dx}}\left(9 \sqrt{\mathrm{x}}+\mathrm{x}^{2}\right)=9 \frac{\mathrm{~d}}{\mathrm{dx}}(\sqrt{\mathrm{x}})+\frac{\mathrm{d}}{\mathrm{dx}}\left(\mathrm{x}^{2}\right) \\
& =9 \cdot \frac{1}{2 \sqrt{\mathrm{x}}}+2 \mathrm{x} \\
& =\frac{9}{2 \sqrt{\mathrm{x}}}+2 x
\end{aligned}$$

\section*{PART -B}
1. Find $\frac{d y}{d x}$ if $\mathrm{y}=\frac{3}{\mathrm{x}^{2}}+\frac{2}{\mathrm{x}}+\frac{1}{4}$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
y & =\frac{3}{x^{2}}+\frac{2}{x}+\frac{1}{4}=3 x^{-2}+2 x^{-1}+\frac{1}{4} \\
\frac{d y}{d x} & =\frac{d}{d x}\left(3 x^{-2}+2 x^{-1}+\frac{1}{4}\right)=3(-2) x^{-3}+2(-1) x^{-2}+0 \\
& =\frac{-6}{x^{3}}-\frac{2}{x^{2}}
\end{aligned}$$
2. Find $\frac{d y}{d x}$ if $\mathrm{y}=\mathrm{e}^{\mathrm{x}} \sin \mathrm{x}$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
y & =e^{x} \sin x \\
\frac{d y}{d x} & =\frac{d}{d x}\left(e^{x} \sin x\right)=" u \frac{d v}{d x}+v \frac{d u}{d x} " \\
& =e^{x} \frac{d}{d x}(\sin x)+\sin x \frac{d}{d x}\left(e^{x}\right) \\
& =e^{x} \cos x+\sin x . e^{x}
\end{aligned}$$
3. Find $\frac{d y}{d x}$ if $y=x^{2} e^{x} \sin x$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
y & =x^{2} e^{x} \sin x \\
\frac{d y}{d x} & =\frac{d}{d x}\left(x^{2} e^{x} \sin x\right)=" u v \frac{d w}{d x}+v w \frac{d u}{d x}+w u \frac{d v}{d x} " \\
& =x^{2} e^{x} \frac{d}{d x}(\sin x)+e^{x} \sin x \frac{d}{d x}\left(x^{2}\right)+\sin x \cdot x^{2} \frac{d}{d x}\left(e^{x}\right) \\
& =x^{2} e^{x} \cos x+e^{x} \sin x \cdot 2 x+\sin x \cdot x^{2} e^{x}
\end{aligned}$$
4. Find $\frac{d y}{d x}$ if $y=\frac{\cos x}{\sqrt{x}}$.

Solution:
$$\begin{aligned}
y & =\frac{\cos x}{\sqrt{x}} \\
\frac{d y}{d x} & =\frac{v \frac{d u}{d x}-u \frac{d v}{d x}}{v^{2}} \\
& =\frac{\sqrt{x} \frac{d}{d x}(\cos x)-\cos x \frac{d}{d x}(\sqrt{x})}{(\sqrt{x})^{2}} \\
& =\frac{\sqrt{x}(-\sin x)-\cos x \cdot \frac{1}{2 \sqrt{x}}}{x}
\end{aligned}$$

\section*{PART - C}
1. Find $\frac{d y}{d x}$ if $y=\left(x^{2}+3\right) \cos x \log x$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
y & =\left(x^{2}+3\right) \cos x \log x \\
\frac{d y}{d x} & =\frac{d}{d x}\left[\left(x^{2}+3\right) \cos x \log x\right]=" u v \frac{d w}{d x}+v w \frac{d u}{d x}+w u \frac{d v}{d x} " \\
& =\left(x^{2}+3\right) \cos x \frac{d}{d x}(\log x)+\cos x \log x \frac{d}{d x}\left(x^{2}+3\right)+\log x\left(x^{2}+3\right) \frac{d}{d x}(\cos x) \\
& =\left(x^{2}+3\right) \cos x \cdot \frac{1}{x}+\cos x \log x \cdot 2 x+\log x \cdot\left(x^{2}+3\right)(-\sin x) \\
& =\frac{\left(x^{2}+3\right) \cos x}{x}+2 x \cos x \log x-\left(x^{2}+3\right) \sin x \log x
\end{aligned}$$
2. If $y=\frac{x^{3} \tan x}{e^{x}+1}$, find $\frac{d y}{d x}$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
y & =\frac{x^{3} \tan x}{e^{x}+1} \\
\frac{d y}{d x} & =\frac{v \frac{d u}{d x}-u \frac{d v}{d x}}{v^{2}} \\
& =\frac{\left(e^{x}+1\right) \frac{d}{d x}\left(x^{3} \tan x\right)-\left(x^{3} \tan x\right) \frac{d}{d x}\left(e^{x}+1\right)}{\left(e^{x}+1\right)^{2}} \\
& =\frac{\left(e^{x}+1\right)\left[x^{3} \frac{d}{d x}(\tan x)+\tan x \frac{d}{d x}\left(x^{3}\right)\right]-x^{3} \tan x \cdot e^{x}}{\left(e^{x}+1\right)^{2}} \\
& =\frac{\left(e^{x}+1\right)\left[x^{3} \sec ^{2} x+\tan x \cdot 3 x^{2}\right]-x^{3} \tan x \cdot e^{x}}{\left(e^{x}+1\right)^{2}}
\end{aligned}$$
3. Find $\frac{d y}{d x}$ if $y=\frac{1+x+x^{2}}{1-x+x^{2}}$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
y & =\frac{1+x+x^{2}}{1-x+x^{2}} \\
\frac{d y}{d x} & =\frac{v \frac{d u}{d x}-u \frac{d v}{d x}}{v^{2}} \\
& =\frac{\left(1-x+x^{2}\right) \frac{d}{d x}\left(1+x+x^{2}\right)-\left(1+x+x^{2}\right) \frac{d}{d x}\left(1-x+x^{2}\right)}{\left(1-x+x^{2}\right)^{2}} \\
& =\frac{\left(1-x+x^{2}\right)(1+2 x)-\left(1+x+x^{2}\right)(-1+2 x)}{\left(1-x+x^{2}\right)^{2}} \\
& =\frac{1+2 x-x-2 x^{2}+x^{2}+2 x^{3}+1-2 x+x-2 x^{2}+x^{2}-2 x^{3}}{\left(1-x+x^{2}\right)^{2}} \\
& =\frac{2-2 x^{2}}{\left(1-x+x^{2}\right)^{2}}=\frac{2\left(1-x^{2}\right)}{\left(1-x+x^{2}\right)^{2}}
\end{aligned}$$

\section*{DIFFERENTIAL CALCULUS-II}

\subsection*{5.1 DIFFERENTIATION METHODS}

Differentiation of function functions (chain rule), Inverse Trigonometric functions and Implict functions. Simple Problems.

\subsection*{5.2 SUCCESSIVE DIFFERENTIATION}

Successive differentiation up to second order (parametric form not included). Definition of differential equation, order and degree, formation of differential equation. Simple problems.

\subsection*{5.3 PARTIAL DIFFERENTIATION}

Definition - Partial differentiation of two variables up to second order only. Simple Problems.

\subsection*{5.1 DIFFERENTIATION METHODS}

\section*{Function of Funtions Rule:}

If ' $y$ ' is a function of ' $u$ ' and ' $u$ ' is a function of ' $x$ ' then the derivative of ' $y$ ' w.r.t ' $x$ ' is equal to the product of the derivative of 'y' w.r.t ' $u$ ' and the derivative of 'u' w.r.t ' $x$ '.
i.e. $\frac{d y}{d x}=\frac{d y}{d u} \cdot \frac{d u}{d x}$

It is called function of function rule. This rule can be extended which is known as 'Chain rule'.

\section*{Chain rule:}

If ' $y$ ' is a function of ' $u$ ' and ' $u$ ' is a function of ' $v$ ' and ' $v$ ' is a function of ' $x$ ' then.
$$\frac{d y}{d x}=\frac{d y}{d u} \cdot \frac{d u}{d v} \frac{d v}{d x}$$

\section*{PART -A}

Find $\frac{d y}{d x}$ if
1) $y=(2 x+5)^{3}$
2) $y=\sqrt{\sin x}$
3) $y=\cos ^{4} x$
4) $y=e^{\tan x}$
5) $y=\log (\sec x)$
6) $y=\sin m x$
7) $y=\sec \sqrt{x}$
8) $y=\cos (2-3 x)$

\section*{Solution:}
1) $y=(2 x+5)^{3}$
$y=u^{3}$ where $u=2 x+5$
$$\begin{aligned}
\frac{d y}{d u} & =3 u^{2} \left\lvert\, \frac{d u}{d x}=2\right. \\
\frac{d y}{d x} & =\frac{d y}{d u} \cdot \frac{d u}{d x} \\
& =\left(3 u^{2}\right)(2) \\
& =6(2 x+5)^{2}
\end{aligned}$$
2) $y=\sqrt{\sin x}$
$$\begin{aligned}
& y=\sqrt{\mathrm{u}} \text { where } \mathrm{u}=\sin \mathrm{x} \\
& \left.\frac{\mathrm{dy}}{\mathrm{du}}=\frac{1}{2 \sqrt{\mathrm{u}}} \right\rvert\, \frac{\mathrm{du}}{\mathrm{dx}}=\cos \mathrm{x} \\
& \frac{\mathrm{dy}}{\mathrm{dx}}=\left(\frac{1}{2 \sqrt{\mathrm{u}}}\right)(\cos \mathrm{x}) \\
& \quad=\frac{\cos \mathrm{x}}{2 \sqrt{\sin \mathrm{x}}}
\end{aligned}$$
3) $y=\cos ^{4} x$
$y=u^{4}$ where $u=\cos x$
$$\begin{aligned}
& \frac{d y}{d u}=4 u^{3} \left\lvert\, \frac{d u}{d x}=-\sin x\right. \\
& \frac{d y}{d x}=4 u^{3}(-\sin x) \\
& =-4 \sin x \cos ^{3} x
\end{aligned}$$
4) $y=e^{\tan x}$
$y=e^{u}$ where $u=\tan x$
$$\begin{aligned}
& \frac{d y}{d u}=e^{u} \left\lvert\, \frac{d u}{d x}=\sec ^{2} x\right. \\
& \frac{d y}{d x}=\left(e^{u}\right)\left(\sec ^{2} x\right) \\
& =e^{\tan x} \sec ^{2} x
\end{aligned}$$
5) $y=\log (\sec x)$
$y=\log u$ where $u=\sec x$
$$\begin{aligned}
& \frac{d y}{d u}=\frac{1}{u} \left\lvert\, \frac{d u}{d x}=\sec x \tan x\right. \\
& \frac{d y}{d x}=\left(\frac{1}{u}\right)(\sec x \tan x) \\
&=\frac{1}{\sec x}(\sec x \tan x) \\
&=\tan x
\end{aligned}$$
6) $y=\sin m x$
$y=\sin u$ where $u=m x$
$$\begin{aligned}
& \left.\frac{d y}{d u}=\cos u \right\rvert\, \frac{d u}{d x}=m \\
& \begin{array}{c}
\frac{d y}{d x} \\
=(\cos u)(m) \\
\\
=m \cos m x
\end{array}
\end{aligned}$$
7) $y=\cos (2-3 x)$
$y=\cos u$ where $u=2-3 x$
$$\begin{aligned}
& \frac{d y}{d u}=-\left.\sin u\right|^{\frac{d u}{d x}=0-3(1)}=-3 \\
& \frac{d y}{d x}=(-\sin u)(-3) \\
& =3 \sin (2-3 x)
\end{aligned}$$
8) $y=\sec \sqrt{x}$
$y=\sec u$ where $u=\sqrt{x}$
$$\begin{aligned}
& \left.\frac{d y}{d u}=\sec u \cdot \tan u \right\rvert\, \frac{d u}{d x}=\frac{1}{2 \sqrt{x}} \\
& \frac{d y}{d x}
\end{aligned}=(\sec u \tan u)\left(\frac{1}{2 \sqrt{x}}\right) \quad \begin{aligned}
& \text { } \\
& =\frac{1}{2 \sqrt{x}} \cdot \sec \sqrt{x} \cdot \tan \sqrt{x}
\end{aligned}$$

\section*{Note:}
1. $\frac{d}{d x}\left(e^{m x}\right)=m e^{m x}$
2. $\frac{d}{d x}(\sin m x)=m \cos m x$
3. $\frac{d}{d x}(\cos m x)=-m \sin m x$
4. $\frac{d}{d x}(\tan m x)=m \sec ^{2} m x$
5. $\frac{d}{d x}(\cot m x)=-m \operatorname{cosec}^{2} m x$
6. $\frac{d}{d x}(\sec m x)=m \sec m x \tan m x$
7. $\frac{\mathrm{d}}{\mathrm{dx}}(\operatorname{cosec} \mathrm{mx})=-\mathrm{m} \operatorname{cosec} \mathrm{mx} \cot \mathrm{mx}$

\section*{PART - B}

\section*{Differentiate the following w.r.t ' $x$ '.}
1) $\left(2 x^{2}-3 x+1\right)^{3}$
2) $\cos \left(e^{5 x}\right)$
3) $e^{\sin ^{2} x}$
4) $\log (\sec x+\tan x)$
5) $y=\operatorname{cosec}^{3}(5 x+1)$

\section*{Solution:}
1) $y=\left(2 x^{2}-3 x+1\right)^{3}$
$y=u^{3}$ where $u=2 x^{2}-3 x+1$
$$\begin{aligned}
& \left.\frac{d y}{d u}=3 u^{2} \right\rvert\, \frac{d u}{d x}=4 x-3 \\
& \frac{d y}{d x}=\left(3 u^{2}\right)(4 x-3) \\
& \quad=3\left(2 x^{2}-3 x+1\right)^{2}(4 x-3)
\end{aligned}$$
2) Let $y=\cos \left(e^{5 x}\right)$
$y=\cos u$ where $u=e^{5 x}$
$$\begin{aligned}
& \left.\frac{d y}{d u}=-\sin u \right\rvert\, \frac{d u}{d x}=5 e^{5 x} \\
& \frac{d y}{d x}=(-\sin u)\left(5 e^{5 x}\right) \\
& =-5 e^{5 x} \sin \left(e^{5 x}\right)
\end{aligned}$$
3) Let $y=e^{\sin ^{2} x}$
$y=e^{u}$ where $u=\sin ^{2} x$
$$\begin{aligned}
& \left.\frac{d y}{d u}=e^{u} \right\rvert\, u=v^{2} \text { where } v=\sin x \\
& \quad \frac{d u}{d v}=2 v \left\lvert\, \frac{d v}{d x}=\cos x\right. \\
& \frac{d y}{d x}=\frac{d y}{d u} \cdot \frac{d u}{d v} \cdot \frac{d v}{d x} \\
& =\left(e^{u}\right)(2 v)(\cos x) \\
& =
\end{aligned}$$
4) Let $y=\log (\sec x+\tan x)$
$y=\log u$ where $u=\sec x+\tan x$
$$\begin{aligned}
& \frac{d y}{d u}=\left.\frac{1}{u}\right|^{\frac{d u}{d x}}=\sec x \cdot \tan x+\sec ^{2} x \\
& =\sec x(\tan x+\sec x) \\
& \frac{d y}{d x}=\left(\frac{1}{u}\right)[\sec x(\tan x+\sec x)] \\
& = \\
& =\frac{1}{(\sec x+\tan x)} \cdot \sec x(\tan x+\sec x) \\
& \\
& =\sec x
\end{aligned}$$
5) Let $y=\operatorname{cosec}^{3}(5 x+1)$
$y=u^{3}$ where $u=\operatorname{cosec}(5 x+1)$
$$\begin{aligned}
& \left.\frac{d y}{d u}=3 u^{2} \right\rvert\, u=\operatorname{cosec} v \text { where } v=5 x+1 \\
& \left.\frac{d u}{d v}=-\operatorname{cosec} v \cot v \right\rvert\, \frac{d v}{d x}=5 \\
& \frac{d y}{d x}=\left(3 u^{2}\right)(-\operatorname{cosec} v \cot v)(5) \\
& =-15 \operatorname{cosec}^{2}(5 x+1) \cdot \operatorname{cosec}(5 x+1) \cot (5 x+1) \\
& =-15 \operatorname{cosec}^{3}(5 x+1) \cot (5 x+1)
\end{aligned}$$

\section*{PART - C}

\section*{Differentitate the following w.r.t $x$.}
1) $y=\sin \left(e^{x} \log x\right)$
2) $\left(x^{2}+5\right) e^{-2 x} \sin x$
3) $y=(x \cos x)^{3}$
4) $y=\log \left(\frac{1-\cos x}{1+\cos x}\right)$
5) $y=\sqrt{\frac{1+x^{3}}{1+x^{3}}}$
6) $y=e^{4 x}+\sin \left(x^{2}+5\right)$
7) $y=x^{3} e^{-5 x} \log (\sec x)$

\section*{Solution:}
1) $y=\sin \left(e^{x} \log x\right)$
$\mathrm{y}=\sin \mathrm{u}$ where $\mathrm{u}=\mathrm{e}^{\mathrm{x}} \log \mathrm{x}$
$$\begin{gathered}
\begin{array}{c}
\frac{d y}{d u}=\cos u \left\lvert\, \begin{array}{c}
\frac{d u}{d x}=e^{x} \frac{1}{x}+\log x \times e^{x} \\
\text { (using product rule) }
\end{array}\right. \\
=e^{x}\left(\frac{1}{x}+\log x\right)
\end{array} \\
\frac{d y}{d x}=(\cos u)\left[\mathrm{e}^{x}\left(\frac{1}{x}+\log x\right)\right] \\
=\cos \left(e^{x} \log x\right)\left[e^{x}\left(\frac{1}{x}+\log x\right)\right]
\end{gathered}$$
2) $y=\left(x^{2}+5\right) e^{-2 x} \sin x$
$$\begin{array}{c|l|l}
u=x^{2}+5 & \begin{array}{l}
v=e^{-2 x} \\
\frac{d u}{d x}=2 x
\end{array} & \begin{array}{l}
\frac{d v}{d x}=e^{-2 x}(-2) \\
=-2 e^{-2 x}
\end{array}
\end{array}$$
$$\begin{aligned}
& \frac{d y}{d x}=u v \frac{d w}{d x}+v w \frac{d u}{d x}+u w \frac{d v}{d x} \\
& =\left(x^{2}+5\right) e^{-2 x} \cos x+e^{-2 x} \sin x(2 x)+\left(x^{2}-5\right) \sin x\left(-2 e^{-2 x}\right)
\end{aligned}$$
3) $y=(x \cos x)^{3}$
$y=u^{3}$ where $u=x \cos x$
$$\begin{array}{l|l}
\frac{d y}{d u}=3 u^{2} & \begin{array}{l}
\frac{d u}{d x}=x(-\sin x)+\cos x(1) \\
(\text { using product rule) } \\
=-x \sin x+\cos x
\end{array}
\end{array}$$
$$\begin{aligned}
\frac{d y}{d x} & =\left(3 u^{2}\right)(-x \sin x+\cos x) \\
& =3(x \cos x)^{2}(-x \sin x+\cos x)
\end{aligned}$$
4) $y=\log \left(\frac{1-\cos x}{1+\cos x}\right)$
$$\begin{aligned}
y & =\log u \text { where } u=\frac{1-\cos x}{1+\cos x} \\
& \frac{d y}{d u}=\frac{1}{u} \left\lvert\, \frac{d u}{d x}=\frac{(1+\cos x)(+\sin x)-(1-\cos x)(-\sin x)}{(1+\cos x)^{2}}\right. \\
\frac{d y}{d x} & =\left(\frac{1}{u}\right)\left[\frac{\sin x(1+\cos x)+\sin x(1-\cos x)}{(1+\cos x)^{2}}\right] \\
& =\left(\frac{1+\cos x}{1-\cos x}\right)\left[\frac{2 \sin x}{(1+\cos x)^{2}}\right] \\
& =\frac{2 \sin x}{(1+\cos x)(1-\cos x)}=\frac{2 \sin x}{1-\cos ^{2} x} \\
& =\frac{2 \sin x}{\sin ^{2} x} \\
& =\frac{2}{\sin ^{2} x}
\end{aligned}$$
5) $y=\sqrt{\frac{1+\mathrm{x}^{3}}{1+\mathrm{x}^{3}}}$
$$\begin{array}{l|l}
y=\sqrt{u} \\
\frac{d y}{d u}=\frac{1}{2 \sqrt{u}} & \begin{array}{l}
\text { where } u=\frac{1-x^{3}}{1+x^{3}} \\
\frac{d u}{d x}=\frac{\left(1+x^{3}\right)\left(-3 x^{2}\right)-\left(1-x^{3}\right)\left(3 x^{2}\right)}{\left(1+x^{3}\right)^{2}} \\
=3 x^{2}\left[\frac{-\left(1+x^{3}\right)-\left(1-x^{3}\right)}{\left(1+x^{3}\right)^{2}}\right] \\
=\frac{-6 x^{2}}{\left(1+x^{3}\right)^{2}}
\end{array}
\end{array}$$
$$\begin{aligned}
\frac{d y}{d x} & =\left(\frac{1}{2 \sqrt{u}}\right) \frac{-6 x^{2}}{\left(1+x^{3}\right)^{2}} \\
& =\frac{1}{2 \sqrt{\frac{1-x^{3}}{1+x^{3}}}}\left[\frac{-6 x^{2}}{\left(1+x^{3}\right)^{2}}\right] \\
& =\frac{-3 x^{2}}{\left(1+x^{3}\right)^{2}} \sqrt{\frac{1+x^{3}}{1-x^{3}}}
\end{aligned}$$
6) $y=e^{4 x}+\sin \left(x^{2}+5\right)$
$$\begin{aligned}
\frac{d y}{d x} & =e^{4 x} \times 4+\cos \left(x^{2}+5\right) \times(2 x+0) \\
& =4 e^{4 x}+2 x \cos \left(x^{2}+5\right)
\end{aligned}$$
7) $y=x^{3} e^{-5 x} \log (\sec x)$
$$\begin{aligned}
& \begin{array}{rl|rl}
u & =x^{3} & v & =e^{-5 x} \\
\frac{d u}{d x} & =3 x^{2} & \begin{aligned}
w & =\log (\sec x) \\
d x & =e^{-5 x}(-5) \\
& =-5 e^{-5 x}
\end{aligned} & \begin{aligned}
\frac{d w}{d x} & =\frac{1}{\sec x} \sec x \cdot \tan x \\
& =\tan x
\end{aligned}
\end{array} \\
& \frac{d y}{d x}=u v \frac{d w}{d x}+\operatorname{vw} \frac{d u}{d x}+u w \frac{d v}{d x} \\
& =\mathrm{x}^{3} \mathrm{e}^{-5 \mathrm{x}} \tan \mathrm{x}+\mathrm{e}^{-5 \mathrm{x}} \log (\sec \mathrm{x})\left(3 \mathrm{x}^{2}\right)+\mathrm{x}^{3} \log (\sec \mathrm{x})\left(-5 \mathrm{e}^{-5 \mathrm{x}}\right)
\end{aligned}$$

\subsection*{5.1.2 DIFFERENTIATION OF INVERSE TRIGONOMETRIC FUNCTIONS}

If $x=\sin y$ then we get a unique real value of $x$ to the given angle $y$. But if $x$ is given $y$ has many values.

We can express $y$ interms of $x$ as $y=\sin ^{-1} x$ "Inverse sine of $x$ ". The Quantities $\sin ^{-1} x, \cos ^{-1} x$, $\tan ^{-1} x, \cot ^{-1} x, \sec ^{-1} x, \operatorname{cosec}^{-1} x$ are called Inverse Trigonometric Functions.
Differential co-efficient of $\sin ^{-1} x$ :
Let $y=\sin ^{-1} x$
$\Rightarrow \sin y=x$
Differentiating w.r.t x
$$\begin{aligned}
\cos y \cdot \frac{d y}{d x} & =1 \\
\frac{d y}{d x} & =\frac{1}{\cos y} \\
& =\frac{1}{\sqrt{1-\sin ^{2} y}}
\end{aligned}$$
i.e., $\frac{d}{d x}\left(\sin ^{-1} x\right)=\frac{1}{\sqrt{1-x^{2}}}$

Similarly we get
(i) $\frac{d}{d x}\left(\cos ^{-1} x\right)=\frac{-1}{\sqrt{1-x^{2}}}$
(ii) $\frac{d}{d x}\left(\tan ^{-1} x\right)=\frac{1}{1+x^{2}}$
(iii) $\frac{d}{d x}\left(\cot ^{-1} x\right)=\frac{-1}{1+x^{2}}$
(iv) $\frac{d}{d x}\left(\sec ^{-1} x\right)=\frac{-1}{x \sqrt{x^{2}-1}}$
(v) $\frac{d}{d x}\left(\operatorname{cosec}^{-1} x\right)=\frac{-1}{x \sqrt{x^{2}-1}}$

\section*{WORKED EXAMPLES \\ PART - A}

Find $\frac{d y}{d x}$ if
(i) $y=\sin ^{-1} \sqrt{x}$
(ii) $y=\cos ^{-1}(2 x)$
(iii) $y=\tan ^{-1}(\log x)$

\section*{Solution:}
(i) $y=\sin ^{-1} \sqrt{x}$
$$\begin{aligned}
\frac{d y}{d x} & =\sin ^{-1} u \text { where } u=\sqrt{x} \\
& \left.\frac{d y}{d u}=\frac{1}{\sqrt{1-u^{2}}} \right\rvert\, \frac{d u}{d x}=\frac{1}{2 \sqrt{x}} \\
\frac{d y}{d x} & =\left(\frac{1}{\sqrt{1-u^{2}}}\right)\left(\frac{1}{2 \sqrt{x}}\right) \\
& =\frac{1}{\sqrt{1-(\sqrt{x})^{2}}} \frac{1}{2 \sqrt{x}} \\
& =\frac{1}{\sqrt{1-x} \cdot \frac{1}{2 \sqrt{x}}} \\
& =\frac{1}{2 \sqrt{x(1-x)}}
\end{aligned}$$
(ii) $y=\cos ^{-1}(2 x)$
$y=\cos ^{-1} u$ where $u=2 x$
$$\begin{aligned}
& \left.\frac{\mathrm{dy}}{\mathrm{du}}=\frac{-1}{\sqrt{1-\mathrm{u}^{2}}} \right\rvert\, \frac{\mathrm{du}}{\mathrm{dx}}=2 \\
& \begin{aligned}
\frac{\mathrm{dy}}{\mathrm{dx}} & =\frac{-1}{\sqrt{1-\mathrm{u}^{2}}} \cdot 2 \\
& =\frac{-1}{\sqrt{1-(2 \mathrm{x})^{2}}} \cdot 2
\end{aligned} \\
& \frac{\mathrm{dy}}{\mathrm{dx}}=\frac{-2}{\sqrt{1-4 \mathrm{x}^{2}}}
\end{aligned}$$
(iii) $y=\tan ^{-1}(\log x)$
$\mathrm{y}=\tan ^{-1} \mathrm{u}$ where $\mathrm{u}=\log \mathrm{x}$
$$\begin{aligned}
& \left.\frac{d y}{d u}=\frac{1}{1+u^{2}} \right\rvert\, \frac{d u}{d x}=\frac{1}{x} \\
& \frac{d y}{d x}=\left(\frac{1}{1+u^{2}}\right)\left(\frac{1}{x}\right) \\
& =\frac{1}{x\left[1+(\log x)^{2}\right]}
\end{aligned}$$

\section*{PART - B}

Find $\frac{d y}{d x}$ if
(i) $y=\sin ^{-1}(\cos x)$
(ii) $y=\cos ^{-1}(2 x+3)$
(iii) $y=\cos ^{-1}\left(2 x^{2}-1\right)$
(iv) $y=\sin ^{-1}\left(3 x-4 x^{3}\right)$

\section*{Solution:}
(i) $y=\sin ^{-1}(\cos x)$
$$\begin{aligned}
& \begin{aligned}
y & = \\
& \sin ^{-1} u \text { where } u=\cos x \\
\frac{d y}{d u} & =\frac{1}{\sqrt{1-u^{2}}} \left\lvert\, \frac{d u}{d x}=-\sin x\right. \\
\frac{d y}{d x} & =\left(\frac{1}{\sqrt{1-u^{2}}}\right)(-\sin x) \\
& =\frac{1}{\sqrt{1-\cos ^{2} x}}(-\sin x) \\
& =\frac{-\sin x}{\sqrt{\sin ^{2} x}}=-1
\end{aligned}
\end{aligned}$$
(ii) $y=\cos ^{-1}(2 x+3)$
$$\begin{aligned}
\frac{d y}{d x} & =\frac{-1}{\sqrt{1-(2 x+3)^{2}}} \cdot \frac{d}{d x}(2 x+3) \\
& =\frac{-1}{\sqrt{1-(2 x+3)^{2}}} \times 2 \\
& =\frac{-2}{\sqrt{1-(2 x+3)^{2}}}
\end{aligned}$$
(iii) $y=\cos ^{-1}\left(2 x^{2}-1\right)$
$$\begin{aligned}
\frac{d y}{d x} & =\frac{-1}{\sqrt{1-\left(2 x^{2}-1\right)^{2}}} \cdot \frac{d}{d x}\left(2 x^{2}\right) \\
& =\frac{-1}{\sqrt{1-\left(2 x^{2}-1\right)^{2}}} \cdot 4 x \\
& =\frac{-4 x}{\sqrt{1-\left(2 x^{2}-1\right)^{2}}}=\frac{-4 x}{\sqrt{1-4 x^{4}+4 x^{2}-1}}=\frac{-4 x}{\sqrt{4 x^{2}-4 x^{4}}}=\frac{-4 x}{2 x \sqrt{1-x^{2}}}=\frac{-2}{\sqrt{1-x^{2}}}
\end{aligned}$$

\section*{ALITER}
$y=\cos ^{-1}\left(2 x^{2}-1\right)$
Put $x=\cos \theta$
$$\begin{aligned}
y & =\cos ^{-1}\left(2 \cos ^{2} \theta-1\right) \\
& =\cos -1(\cos 2 \theta) \\
y & =2 \theta \\
y & =2 \cos ^{-1} x \quad x=\cos \theta \Rightarrow \theta=\cos ^{-1} x \\
\frac{d y}{d x} & =2 \times \frac{-1}{\sqrt{1-x^{2}}}=\frac{-2}{\sqrt{1-x^{2}}}
\end{aligned}$$
(iv) $y=\sin ^{-1}\left(3 x-4 x^{3}\right)$
$$\frac{d y}{d x}=\frac{1}{\sqrt{1-\left(3 x-4 x^{3}\right)^{2}}} \cdot\left(3-12 x^{2}\right)$$

\section*{ALITER}

Put $\mathrm{x}=\sin \theta$
$$\begin{aligned}
y & =\sin ^{-1}\left(3 \sin \theta-4 \sin ^{3} \theta\right) \\
& =\sin ^{-1}(\sin 3 \theta) \\
y & =3 \theta \\
y & =3 \sin ^{-1} x \quad x=\sin \theta \Rightarrow \theta=\sin ^{-1} x \\
\frac{d y}{d x} & =\frac{3}{\sqrt{1-x^{2}}}
\end{aligned}$$

\section*{PART - C}
(i) $y=\cos ^{-1}\left(\frac{1-x^{2}}{1+x^{2}}\right)$
(ii) $y=\sin ^{-1}\left(\frac{2 x}{1+x^{2}}\right)$
(iii) $y=\tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{2 x}{1-x^{2}}\right)$
(iv) $y=\left(1+x^{2}\right) \tan ^{-1} x$

\section*{Solution:}
(i) $y=\cos ^{-1}\left(\frac{1-x^{2}}{1+x^{2}}\right)$

Let $x=\tan \theta \Rightarrow \theta=\tan ^{-1} \mathrm{x}$
$$\begin{aligned}
y & =\cos ^{-1}\left(\frac{1-\tan ^{2} \theta}{1+\tan ^{2} \theta}\right) \\
& =\cos ^{-1}(\cos 2 \theta) \\
& =2 \theta \\
y & =2 \tan ^{-1} x \\
\frac{d y}{d x} & =2 \frac{1}{1+x^{2}}
\end{aligned}$$
(ii) $y=\sin ^{-1}\left(\frac{2 x}{1+x^{2}}\right)$

Let $\mathrm{x}=\tan \theta \Rightarrow \theta=\tan ^{-1} \mathrm{x}$
$$\begin{aligned}
y & =\sin ^{-1}\left(\frac{2 \tan \theta}{1+\tan ^{2} \theta}\right) \\
& =\sin ^{-1}(\sin 2 \theta) \\
& =2 \theta \\
y & =2 \tan ^{-1} x \\
\frac{d y}{d x} & =2 \cdot \frac{1}{1+x^{2}}
\end{aligned}$$
(iii) $y=\tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{2 x}{1-x^{2}}\right)$

Let $\mathrm{x}=\tan \theta \Rightarrow \theta=\tan ^{-1} \mathrm{x}$
$$\begin{aligned}
y & =\tan ^{-1}\left(\frac{2 \tan \theta}{1-\tan ^{2} \theta}\right) \\
& =\tan ^{-1}(\tan 2 \theta) \\
y & =2 \theta \\
y & =2 \tan ^{-1} x \\
\frac{d y}{d x} & =2 \cdot \frac{1}{1+x^{2}}
\end{aligned}$$
(iv) $y=\left(1+x^{2}\right) \tan ^{-1} x$
$$\begin{aligned}
\frac{d y}{d x} & =\left(1+x^{2}\right) \frac{1}{1+x^{2}}+\tan ^{-1} x(0+2 x) \quad \text { (using product rule) } \\
& =1+2 x \tan ^{-1} x
\end{aligned}$$

\subsection*{5.1.3 IMPLICIT FUNCTION}

If the variables x and y are connected by a relation $\mathrm{f}(\mathrm{x}, \mathrm{y})=0$ then it is called an implicit function. i.e If the dependent variable (y) cannot be expressed explicitly in terms of the independent variable x.

Example: (i) $\mathrm{x}^{2}+\mathrm{y}^{2}-4 \mathrm{x}+\mathrm{y}+12=0$
(ii) $\frac{\mathrm{x}^{2}}{\mathrm{a}^{2}}+\frac{\mathrm{y}^{2}}{\mathrm{~b}^{2}}=1 \quad$ are implicit function

\section*{PART -B}
1. Find $\frac{d y}{d x}$ if
(i) $x^{2}+y^{2}+2 y=0$
(ii) $\mathrm{x}^{2}+\mathrm{y}^{2}=\mathrm{a}^{2}$
(iii) $x y=c^{2}$
(iv) $\sqrt{y}+\sqrt{x}=\sqrt{a}$

\section*{Solution:}
(i) $x^{2}+y^{2}+2 y=0$

Differentiate w.r.t x
$$\begin{aligned}
2 x+2 y \frac{d y}{d x}+2 \frac{d y}{d x} & =0 \\
x+y \frac{d y}{d x}+\frac{d y}{d x} & =0 \\
(y+1) \frac{d y}{d x} & =-x \\
\frac{d y}{d x} & =\frac{-x}{1+y}
\end{aligned}$$
(ii) $\mathrm{x}^{2}+\mathrm{y}^{2}=\mathrm{a}^{2}$

Differentiate w.r.t x
$$\begin{aligned}
2 x+2 y \frac{d y}{d x} & =0 \\
x+y \frac{d y}{d x} & =0 \\
y \frac{d y}{d x} & =-x \\
\frac{d y}{d x} & =\frac{-x}{y}
\end{aligned}$$
(iii) $x y=c^{2}$

Differentiate w.r.t x
$\mathrm{x} \cdot \frac{\mathrm{dy}}{\mathrm{dx}}+\mathrm{y}(1)=0$ (using product rule)
$x \frac{d y}{d x}=-y$
$\frac{d y}{d x}=\frac{-y}{x}$
(iv) $\sqrt{\mathrm{y}}+\sqrt{\mathrm{x}}=\sqrt{\mathrm{a}}$

Differentiate w.r.t x
$\frac{1}{2 \sqrt{x}}+\frac{1}{2 \sqrt{y}} \cdot \frac{d y}{d x}=0$
Multiply by 2
$$\begin{aligned}
& \frac{1}{\sqrt{x}}+\frac{1}{\sqrt{y}} \cdot \frac{d y}{d x}=0 \\
& \frac{1}{\sqrt{y}} \frac{d y}{d x}=\frac{-1}{\sqrt{x}} \\
& \frac{d y}{d x}=\frac{-\sqrt{y}}{\sqrt{x}}
\end{aligned}$$

\section*{PART - C}
1. Find $\frac{d y}{d x}$ if
(i) $\cos \mathrm{x}+\sin \mathrm{y}=\mathrm{c}$
(ii) $\mathrm{x}^{2} \sin \mathrm{y}=\mathrm{c}$
(iii) $y=a+x e^{y}$

\section*{Solution:}
(i) $\cos \mathrm{x}+\sin \mathrm{y}=\mathrm{c}$

Differentiate w.r.t x
$$\begin{aligned}
-\sin x+\cos y \cdot \frac{d y}{d x} & =0 \\
\cos y \cdot \frac{d y}{d x} & =\sin x \\
\frac{d y}{d x} & =\frac{\sin x}{\cos y}
\end{aligned}$$
(ii) $x^{2} \sin y=c$

Differentiate w.r.t x
$$\begin{aligned}
x^{2} \cos y \cdot \frac{d y}{d x}+\sin y(2 x) & =0 \quad(\text { using product rule }) \\
x^{2} \cos y \cdot \frac{d y}{d x} & =-2 x \sin y \\
\frac{d y}{d x} & =\frac{-2 x \sin y}{x^{2} \cos y} \\
\frac{d y}{d x} & =\frac{-2}{x} \tan y
\end{aligned}$$
(iii) $y=a+x e^{y}$

Differentiate w.r.t x
$$\begin{aligned}
\frac{d y}{d x} & =0+x e^{y} \cdot \frac{d y}{d x}+e^{y} \\
\frac{d y}{d x}-x e^{y} \frac{d y}{d x} & =e^{y} \\
\frac{d y}{d x}\left(1-x e^{y}\right) & =e^{y} \\
\frac{d y}{d x} & =\frac{e^{y}}{1-x e^{y}}
\end{aligned}$$
2. Find $\frac{d y}{d x}$ if
(i) $x^{3}+y^{3}=3 a x y$
(ii) $x^{2}+y^{2}-4 x+6 y-5=0$
(iii) $x^{2}+y^{2}=x y$
(iv) $a x^{2}+2 h x y+b y^{2}+2 g x+2 f y+c=0$
(i) $\mathrm{x}^{3}+\mathrm{y}^{3}=3 a x y$

Differentiate w.r.t x
$$3 x^{2}+3 y^{2} \frac{d y}{d x}=3 a\left[x \frac{d y}{d x}+y(1)\right]$$

Divide by 3
(using product rule)
$$\begin{aligned}
x^{2}+y^{2} \frac{d y}{d x} & =a\left[x \frac{d y}{d x}+y\right] \\
y^{2} \frac{d y}{d x}-a x \frac{d y}{d x} & =a y-x^{2} \\
\left(y^{2}-a x\right) \frac{d y}{d x} & =a y-x^{2} \\
\frac{d y}{d x} & =\frac{a y-x^{2}}{y^{2}-a x}
\end{aligned}$$
(ii) $x^{2}+y^{2}-4 x+6 y-5=0$

Differentiating w.r.t x
$$\begin{aligned}
2 x+2 y \frac{d y}{d x}-4+6 \frac{d y}{d x} & =0 \\
2 y \frac{d y}{d x}+6 \frac{d y}{d x} & =-2 x+4 \\
\frac{d y}{d x}(2 y+6) & =-2 x+4 \\
\frac{d y}{d x} & =\frac{-2 x+4}{2 y+6}=\frac{2(-x+2)}{2(y+3)} \\
& =\frac{-x+2}{y+3}
\end{aligned}$$
(iii) $x^{2}+y^{2}=x y$
uv rule
Differentiating w.r.t x ,
$$\begin{aligned}
2 x+2 y \frac{d y}{d x} & =x \frac{d y}{d x}+y(1) \\
2 y \frac{d y}{d x}-x \frac{d y}{d x} & =y-2 x \\
\frac{d y}{d x}(2 y-x) & =y-2 x \\
\frac{d y}{d x} & =\frac{y-2 x}{2 y-x}
\end{aligned}$$
(iv) $a x^{2}+2 h x y+b y^{2}+2 g x+2 f y+c=0$

Differentiate w.r.t x
$$2 a x+2 h\left[x \cdot \frac{d y}{d x}+y(1)\right]+b(2 y) \cdot \frac{d y}{d x}+2 g(1)+2 f \cdot \frac{d y}{d x}+0=0$$

Divide by 2
$$\begin{aligned}
& a x+h x \frac{d y}{d x}+h y+b y \frac{d y}{d x}+g+f \frac{d y}{d x}=0 \\
& \frac{d y}{d x}(h x+b y+f)=-a x-h y-g \\
& \frac{d y}{d x}=\frac{-a x-h y-g}{h x+b y+f}
\end{aligned}$$

\subsection*{5.2.1 SUCCESSIVE DIFFERENTIATION}

If $y=f(x)$ then $\frac{d y}{d x}=f^{\prime}(x)$ is a function of $x$ or constant which can be differentiated once again. $\frac{d y}{d x}=f^{\prime}(x)$ is the first order derivative of $y$ w.r.t $x$.
$\frac{d^{2} y}{d x^{2}}=\frac{d}{d x}\left(\frac{d y}{d x}\right)$ is the second order derivative of y w.r.t x
i.e the derivate of $\frac{d y}{d x}$ w.r.t $x$.
$\frac{d^{3} y}{d x^{3}}=\frac{d}{d x}\left(\frac{d^{2} y}{d x^{2}}\right)$ is the third order derivative of $y$ w.r.t $x$ and so on.
Notations of successive derivatives
$\frac{d y}{d x}=y_{1}=y^{\prime}=f^{\prime}(x)=D(y)$
$\frac{d^{2} y}{d x^{2}}=y_{2}=y^{\prime \prime}=f^{\prime \prime}(x)=D^{2}(y)$
$\frac{d^{n} y}{d x^{n}}=y_{n}=y^{(n)}=f^{(n)}(x)=D^{n}(y)$

\section*{WORKED EXAMPLES \\ PART - A}
1. If $y=e^{3 x}$ find $\frac{d^{2} y}{d x^{2}}$.

Solution:
$$\begin{aligned}
\frac{d y}{d x} & =3 e^{3 x} \\
\frac{d^{2} y}{{d x^{2}}^{2}} & =3\left(3 e^{3 x}\right) \\
& =9 e^{3 x}
\end{aligned}$$
2. If $y=\sin 3 x$ find $\frac{d^{2} y}{d x^{2}}$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
\frac{\mathrm{dy}}{\mathrm{dx}} & =3 \cos 3 \mathrm{x} \\
\frac{\mathrm{~d}^{2} \mathrm{y}}{\mathrm{dx}^{2}} & =3(-3 \sin 3 \mathrm{x}) \\
& =-9 \sin 3 \mathrm{x}
\end{aligned}$$

\section*{PART -B}
1. If $\mathrm{y}=\mathrm{a} \cos \mathrm{nx}+\mathrm{b} \sin \mathrm{nx}$ find $\mathrm{y}_{2}$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
y_{1} & =a(-n \sin n x)+b(n \cos n x) \\
& =n(-a \sin n x+b \cos n x) \\
y_{2} & =n[-a(+n \cos n x)+b(-n \sin n x)] \\
& =n^{2}(a \cos n x+b \sin n x) \\
& =-n^{2} y
\end{aligned}$$
2. If $y=\mathrm{Ae}^{3 x}+\mathrm{Be}^{-3 x}$ find $\frac{\mathrm{d}^{2} y}{\mathrm{dx}^{2}}$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
\frac{d y}{d x} & =A\left(3 e^{3 x}\right)+B\left(-3 e^{-3 x}\right) \\
& =3\left(A \cdot e^{3 x}-B e^{-3 x}\right) \\
\frac{d^{2} y}{d^{2} x^{2}} & =3\left[A\left(3 e^{3 x}\right)-B\left(-3 e^{-3 x}\right)\right] \\
& =3\left[3 A e^{3 x}+3 B e^{-3 x}\right] \\
& =9\left[\mathrm{Ae}^{3 x}+B e^{-3 x}\right] \\
& =9 y
\end{aligned}$$
3. If $\mathrm{y}=\tan \mathrm{x}$ find $\mathrm{y}_{2}$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
\frac{d y}{d x} & =\sec ^{2} x \\
\frac{d^{2} y}{d^{2} x^{2}} & =2(\sec x) \times \sec x \tan x \\
& =2 \sec ^{2} x \tan x
\end{aligned}$$

\section*{PART - C}
1. If $\mathrm{y}=\mathrm{x}^{2} \cos \mathrm{x}$ prove that $\mathrm{x}^{2} \mathrm{y}_{2}-4 \mathrm{x} \mathrm{y}_{1}+\left(\mathrm{x}^{2}+6\right) \mathrm{y}=0$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
& y=x^{2} \cos x \\
& y_{1}=x^{2}(-\sin x)+\cos x(2 x) \quad \quad \text { (using product rule) } \\
&=-x^{2} \sin x+2 x \cos x \\
& y_{2}=-x^{2}(\cos x)+\sin x(-2 x)+2 x(-\sin x)+\cos x(2) \\
&=-x^{2} \cos x-2 x \sin x-2 x \sin x+2 \cos x \\
&=-x^{2} \cos x-4 x \sin x+2 \cos x \\
& x^{2} y_{2}- 4 x y_{1}+\left(x^{2}+6\right) y=x^{2}\left[-x^{2} \cos x-4 x \sin x+2 \cos x\right] \\
& \quad-4 x\left[-x^{2} \sin x+2 x \cos x\right]+\left(x^{2}+6\right)\left(x^{2} \cos x\right) \\
&=-x^{4} \cos x-4 x^{3} \sin x+2 x^{2} \cos x+4 x^{3} \sin x-8 x^{2} \cos x+x^{4} \cos x+6 x^{2} \cos x \\
&=0
\end{aligned}$$
2. If $\mathrm{y}=\mathrm{e}^{\mathrm{x}} \sin \mathrm{x}$, prove that $\mathrm{y}_{2}-2 \mathrm{y}_{1}+2 \mathrm{y}=0$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
y & =e^{x} \sin x \\
y_{1} & =e^{x}(\cos x)+\sin x\left(e^{x}\right) \\
y_{1} & =e^{x} \cos x+y
\end{aligned} \quad \text { (using product rule) }$$

Differentiating w.r.t x
$$\begin{aligned}
y_{2} & =e^{x}(-\sin x)+\cos x e^{x}+y_{1} \\
y_{2} & =-y+\left(y_{1}-y\right)+y_{1} \text { from (1) } \\
y_{2} & =-y+y_{1}-y+y_{1} \\
& =-2 y+2 y_{1} \\
y_{2} & -2 y_{1}+2 y=0
\end{aligned}$$
3. If $y=a \cos (\log x)+b \sin (\log x)$ prove that $x^{2} y_{2}+x y_{1}+y=0$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$y=a \cos (\log x)+b \sin (\log x)$$

Differentiating w.r.t x
$$\begin{aligned}
y_{1} & =a\left[-\sin (\log x) \cdot \frac{1}{x}\right]+b\left[\cos (\log x) \cdot \frac{1}{x}\right] \\
y_{1} & =\frac{1}{x}[-a \sin (\log x)+b \cos (\log x)] \\
x_{1} & =-a \sin (\log x)+b \cos (\log x)
\end{aligned}$$

Differentiating w.r.t x
$$\begin{aligned}
x y_{2}+y_{1}(1) & =-a \cos (\log x) \cdot \frac{1}{x}+b\left(-\sin (\log x) \cdot \frac{1}{x}\right) \\
x y_{2}+y_{1} & =\frac{-1}{x}[a \cos (\log x)+b \sin (\log x)] \\
x\left[x y_{2}+y_{1}\right] & =-y \\
x^{2} y_{2}+x y_{1}+y & =0
\end{aligned}$$

\subsection*{5.2.2 DIFFERENTIAL EQUATION}

Definition: An equation containg differential co-efficients is called differential equation.

\section*{Examples:}
1. $\frac{d y}{d x}+y=x$
2. $\mathrm{x} \frac{\mathrm{d}^{2} \mathrm{y}}{\mathrm{dx}^{2}}+1=0$
3. $a \frac{d^{2} y}{d x^{2}}+b \frac{d y}{d x}+c y=d$

\section*{Order of the differential equation:}

The order of the highest derivative in the differential equation is called order of the differential equation.

\section*{Degree of the differential equation:}

The power of the highest derivative in the differential equation is called degree of the differential equation.

\section*{Example:}
(i) $7\left(\frac{d^{2} y}{d x^{2}}\right)^{2}+5\left(\frac{d y}{d x}\right)^{5}+7 y=\sin x$

Order-2, degree -2

\section*{Formation of Differential Equation:}

A differential equation is obtained by differentiating the function $f(x, y)=0$ as many times as the number of arbitrary constants, followed by elimination of arbitrary constants.

\section*{PART -A}
1. Find the order and degree of the following differential equations.
(i) $\left(\frac{d^{3} y}{d x^{3}}\right)^{4}+\frac{d^{2} y}{d x^{2}}+2 \frac{d y}{d x}+7 y=0$
(ii) $\left(\frac{d y}{d x}\right)^{2}+x \frac{d y}{d x}=k$
(iii) $\sqrt{1+\frac{\mathrm{dy}}{\mathrm{dx}}}=\frac{\mathrm{d}^{2} \mathrm{y}}{\mathrm{dx}^{2}}$

\section*{Solution}
(i) order $=3$, degree $=4$
(ii) order $=1$, degree $=2$
(iii) $\sqrt{1+\frac{\mathrm{dy}}{\mathrm{dx}}}=\frac{\mathrm{d}^{2} \mathrm{y}}{\mathrm{dx}^{2}}$

Squaring on both sides
$$\left(1+\frac{d y}{d x}\right)=\left(\frac{d^{2} y}{d^{2}}\right)^{2}$$

Order -2 , degree -2 .
2. From the differential equation by eliminating the constant.
(i) $x y=c$
(ii) $\sqrt{x}+\sqrt{y}=\sqrt{a}$

\section*{Solution:}
(i) $x y=c$
$\mathrm{x} \cdot \frac{\mathrm{dy}}{\mathrm{dx}}+\mathrm{y} \cdot 1=0 \quad$ (using product rule)
$$x \frac{d y}{d x}+y=0$$
(ii) $\sqrt{x}+\sqrt{y}=\sqrt{a}$
$\frac{1}{2 \sqrt{x}}+\frac{1}{2 \sqrt{y}} \cdot \frac{d y}{d x}=0$
Multiply by 2
$\frac{1}{\sqrt{x}}+\frac{1}{\sqrt{y}} \frac{d y}{d x}=0$

\section*{PART -B}

From the different equation by eliminating the constants.
(i) $y=a x+b^{2}$
(ii) $y=m e^{5 x}$
(iii) $\frac{\mathrm{x}}{\mathrm{a}}+\frac{\mathrm{y}}{\mathrm{b}}=1$
(iv) $y^{2}=4 a x$

\section*{Solution:}
(i) $y=a x+b^{2}$
$$\begin{aligned}
& \frac{d y}{d x}=a(1)+0 \\
& \frac{d^{2} y}{d x^{2}}=0
\end{aligned}$$
(ii) $\mathrm{y}=\mathrm{m} \mathrm{e}^{5 \mathrm{x}}$
$\frac{d y}{d x}=m .\left(5 e^{5 x}\right)$
$\frac{d y}{d x}=5 m\left(e^{5 x}\right) \quad$ from (1) $m e^{m x}=y$
$\frac{d y}{d x}=5 y$
(iii) $\frac{\mathrm{x}}{\mathrm{a}}+\frac{\mathrm{y}}{\mathrm{b}}=1$

Differentiating w.r.t x
$$\begin{aligned}
\frac{1}{a}+\frac{1}{b} \quad \frac{d y}{d x} & =0 \\
0+\frac{1}{b} \frac{d^{2} y}{d x^{2}} & =0 \\
\therefore \frac{d^{2} y}{d x^{2}} & =0
\end{aligned}$$
(iv) $y^{2}=4 a x$
$2 y \cdot \frac{d y}{d x}=4 a(0)$
$2 y \cdot \frac{d y}{d x}=4\left(\frac{y^{2}}{4 x}\right) \quad\left(\because y^{2}=4 a x, \frac{y^{2}}{4 x}=a\right)$
$2 y \frac{d y}{d x}=\frac{y^{2}}{x}$

\subsection*{5.3 PARTIAL DIFFERENTIATION}

\section*{Functions of two or more variables:}

In many applications, we come across function involving more than one independent variable. For example, Area of the rectangle depends on its length and breadth, volume of cuboid depends on its length, breadth and height.

Hence one variable $u$ depends on more than one variable.
i.e. $u=f(x, y) \quad v=\varphi(x, y, z)$

\section*{Definition of partial differentiation:}

Let $\mathrm{u}=\mathrm{f}(\mathrm{x}, \mathrm{y})$ then partial differentiation of u w.r.t x is defined as differentiation of u w.r.t x treating y as constant and is denoted by $\frac{\partial \mathrm{u}}{\partial \mathrm{x}}$.
$$\therefore \frac{\partial \mathrm{u}}{\partial \mathrm{x}}=\lim _{\Delta \mathrm{x} \rightarrow 0} \frac{\mathrm{f}(\mathrm{x}+\Delta \mathrm{x}, \mathrm{y})-\mathrm{f}(\mathrm{x}, \mathrm{y})}{\Delta \mathrm{x}}$$

Similarly partial differentiation of $u$ w.r.t $y$ is defined as differentiation of $u$ w.r.t $y$ treating $x$ as constant and is denoted by $\frac{\partial u}{\partial y}$.
$$\therefore \frac{\partial \mathrm{u}}{\partial \mathrm{y}}=\lim _{\Delta \mathrm{y} \rightarrow 0} \frac{\mathrm{f}(\mathrm{x}, \mathrm{y}+\Delta \mathrm{y})-\mathrm{f}(\mathrm{x}, \mathrm{y})}{\Delta \mathrm{y}}$$

\section*{Second order partial derivatives:}

In General, $\frac{\partial \mathrm{u}}{\partial \mathrm{x}}$ and $\frac{\partial \mathrm{u}}{\partial \mathrm{y}}$ are function of x and y . They can be further dfferentiated partially w.r.t x and y as follows.
(i) $\frac{\partial}{\partial \mathrm{x}}\left(\frac{\partial \mathrm{u}}{\partial \mathrm{x}}\right)=\left(\frac{\partial^{2} \mathrm{u}}{\partial \mathrm{x}^{2}}\right)$
(ii) $\frac{\partial}{\partial x}\left(\frac{\partial u}{\partial y}\right)=\left(\frac{\partial^{2} u}{\partial x \partial y}\right)$
(iii) $\frac{\partial}{\partial y}\left(\frac{\partial u}{\partial x}\right)=\left(\frac{\partial^{2} u}{\partial y \partial x}\right)$
(iv) $\frac{\partial}{\partial y}\left(\frac{\partial u}{\partial y}\right)=\left(\frac{\partial^{2} u}{\partial y^{2}}\right)$

For all ordinary functions $\left(\frac{\partial^{2} u}{\partial x \partial y}\right)=\left(\frac{\partial^{2} u}{\partial y \partial x}\right)$.

\section*{WORKED EXAMPLES}

\section*{PART - A}
1. Find $\frac{\partial \mathrm{u}}{\partial \mathrm{x}}$ and $\frac{\partial \mathrm{u}}{\partial \mathrm{y}}$ for the following:
(i) $u=x+y$
(ii) $u=x^{3}+y^{3}$
(iii) $\mathrm{u}=\mathrm{e}^{\mathrm{x}+\mathrm{y}}$
(iv) $u=e^{2 x+3 y}$

\section*{Solution:}
i) $u=x+y$
$$\begin{aligned}
& \frac{\partial u}{\partial x}=1 \\
& \frac{\partial u}{\partial y}=1
\end{aligned}$$
ii) $u=x^{3}+y^{3}$
$$\begin{aligned}
& \frac{\partial u}{\partial x}=3 x^{2} \\
& \frac{\partial u}{\partial y}=3 y^{2}
\end{aligned}$$
(iii) $u=e^{x+y}$
$$\begin{aligned}
& \frac{\partial u}{\partial x}=e^{x+y}(1)=e^{x+y} \\
& \frac{\partial u}{\partial y}=e^{x+y}(1)=e^{x+y}
\end{aligned}$$
(iv) $u=e^{2 x+3 y}$
$$\begin{aligned}
& \frac{\partial u}{\partial x}=e^{2 x+3 y}(2)=2 e^{2 x+3 y} \\
& \frac{\partial u}{\partial y}=e^{2 x+3 y}(3)=3 e^{2 x+3 y}
\end{aligned}$$

\section*{PART - B}
(i) Find $\frac{\partial u}{\partial x}$ and $\frac{\partial u}{\partial y}$ for the following:
(i) $u=x^{3}+4 x^{2} y+5 x y^{2}+y^{3}$
(ii) $u=5 \sin x+4 \tan y$
(iii) $u=y^{2} \sec x$
(iv) $u=\sin 4 x \cos 2 y$

\section*{Solution:}
(i) $u=x^{3}+4 x^{2} y+5 x y^{2}+y^{3}$
$\frac{\partial u}{\partial x}=3 x^{2}+8 x y+5 y^{2}+0$
$\frac{\partial u}{\partial y}=0+4 x^{2}+10 x y+3 y^{2}$
(ii) $u=5 \sin x+4 \tan y$
$$\begin{aligned}
& \frac{\partial u}{\partial x}=5 \cos x+0 \\
& \frac{\partial u}{\partial y}=0+4 \sec ^{2} y
\end{aligned}$$
(iii) $u=y^{2} \sec x$
$$\begin{aligned}
& \frac{\partial u}{\partial x}=y^{2} \sec x \tan x \\
& \frac{\partial u}{\partial y}=\sec x \cdot 2 y
\end{aligned}$$
(iv) $u=\sin 4 x \cos 2 y$
$$\begin{aligned}
& \frac{\partial u}{\partial x}=4 \cos 4 x \cdot \cos 2 y \\
& \frac{\partial u}{\partial y}=2 \sin 4 x \sin 2 y
\end{aligned}$$
2. Find $\frac{\partial^{2} u}{\partial x^{2}}$ and $\frac{\partial^{2} u}{\partial y^{2}}$ for the following:
(i) $u=x^{3}+y^{3}$
(ii) $u=x^{3} \tan y$

\section*{Solution:}
(i) $u=x^{3}+y^{3}$
$$\begin{aligned}
\frac{\partial u}{\partial x} & =3 x^{2}+0 \\
\frac{\partial^{2} u}{\partial x^{2}} & =6 x \\
\frac{\partial u}{\partial y} & =0+3 y^{2} \\
\frac{\partial^{2} u}{\partial y^{2}} & =6 y
\end{aligned}$$
(ii) $u=x^{3} \tan y$
$$\begin{aligned}
\frac{\partial u}{\partial x} & =3 x^{2} \tan y \\
\frac{\partial^{2} u}{\partial x^{2}} & =6 x \tan y \\
\frac{\partial u}{\partial y} & =x^{3} \sec ^{2} y \\
\frac{\partial^{2} u}{\partial y^{2}} & =x^{3}(2 \sec y \cdot \sec y \tan y) \\
& =2 x^{3} \sec ^{2} y \cdot \tan y
\end{aligned}$$
3. Find $\frac{\partial^{2} u}{\partial x \partial y}$ and $\frac{\partial^{2} u}{\partial y \partial x}$ for $u=x^{2} e^{5 y}$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
u & =x^{2} e^{5 y} \\
\frac{\partial u}{\partial x} & =2 x e^{5 y} \\
\frac{\partial^{2} u}{\partial y \partial x} & =\frac{\partial}{\partial y}\left(\frac{\partial u}{\partial x}\right)=2 x \cdot\left(5 e^{5 y}\right)=10 x^{5 y} \\
\frac{\partial u}{\partial y} & =5 x^{2} e^{5 y} \\
\frac{\partial^{2} u}{\partial x \partial y} & =\frac{\partial}{\partial x}\left(\frac{\partial u}{\partial y}\right)=10 x e^{5 y}
\end{aligned}$$

\section*{PART - C}
1. If $u=\log \left(x^{3}+y^{3}\right)$ find $\frac{\partial^{2} u}{\partial x^{2}}$.

\section*{Solution:}
$u=\log \left(x^{3}+y^{3}\right)$
$$\begin{aligned}
\frac{\partial u}{\partial x} & =\frac{1}{x^{3}+y 3}\left(3 x^{2}\right) \\
\frac{\partial^{2} u}{\partial x^{2}} & =\frac{\left(x^{3}+y^{3}\right)(6 x)-\left(3 x^{2}\right)\left(3 x^{2}+0\right)}{\left(x^{3}+y^{3}\right)^{2}} \\
& =\frac{6 x y^{3}-3 x^{4}}{\left(x^{3}+y^{3}\right)^{2}}
\end{aligned}$$
(using quotient rule)
2. If $u=\frac{x}{y^{2}}-\frac{y}{x^{2}}$ find $\frac{\partial^{2} u}{\partial x \partial y}$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
& u=\frac{x}{y^{2}}-\frac{y}{x^{2}} \\
& \frac{\partial u}{\partial y}=x \cdot\left(\frac{-2}{y^{3}}\right)-\frac{1}{x^{2}} \\
& \frac{\partial^{2} u}{\partial x \partial y}=\left(\frac{-2}{y^{3}}\right)-\left(\frac{-2}{x^{3}}\right) \\
&=\frac{2}{x^{3}}-\frac{2}{y^{3}}
\end{aligned}$$
3. If $u=x^{3}+3 x^{2} y+3 x y^{2}+y^{3}$, prove that $x \frac{\partial u}{\partial x}+y \frac{\partial u}{\partial y}=3 u$.

\section*{Solution:}
$$\begin{aligned}
u & =x^{3}+3 x^{2} y+3 x y^{2}+y^{3} \\
\frac{\partial u}{\partial x} & =3 x^{2}+6 x y+3 y^{2}+0 \\
x \frac{\partial u}{\partial x} & =x\left(3 x^{2}+6 x y+3 y^{2}\right) \\
x \frac{\partial u}{\partial x} & =3 x^{3}+6 x^{2} y+3 x y^{2} \\
u & =x^{3}+3 x^{2} y+3 x y^{2}+y^{3} \\
\frac{\partial u}{\partial y} & =0+3 x^{2}+3 x(2 y)+3 y^{2} \\
& =3 x^{2}+6 x y+3 y^{2} \\
y \frac{\partial u}{\partial y} & =y\left(3 x^{2}+6 x y+3 y^{2}\right) \\
& =3 x^{2} y+6 x y^{2}+3 y^{3} \\
(1)+(2) & \Rightarrow \\
x \frac{\partial u}{\partial x}+y \frac{\partial u}{\partial y} & =3 x^{3}+6 x^{2} y+3 x y^{2}+3 x^{2} y+6 x y^{2}+3 y^{3} \\
& =3 x^{3}+9 x^{2} y+9 x y^{2}+3 y^{3} \\
& =3\left(x^{3}+3 x^{2} y+3 x y^{2}+y^{3}\right) \\
& =3 u u s \operatorname{sing}(A)
\end{aligned}$$

\section*{EXERCISE}

(i) $y=(2 x+5)^{3}$
(ii) $y=\sqrt{a x+b}$
(iii) $y=\sin 2 x$
(iv) $y=\cos ^{3} x$
(v) $y=\sin ^{2} 5 x$
(vi) $y=\tan \sqrt{x}$
(vii) $y=\sin (\cos x)$
(viii) $y=\cos (\log x)$
(ix) $y=\log (2 x+3)$
(x) $y=e^{x^{2}}$
2. Find $\frac{d y}{d x}$ if
(i) $y=\sin ^{-1}(2 x)$
(ii) $y=\cos ^{-1}\left(x^{2}\right)$
(iii) $y=\tan ^{-1}(\sqrt{x})$
(iv) $\mathrm{y}=\cos ^{-1}\left(\mathrm{e}^{\mathrm{x}}\right)$

(i) $y^{2}=4 a x$
(ii) $2 \mathrm{x}^{2}-\mathrm{y}^{2}-9=0$
(iii) $\mathrm{x}^{3}+\mathrm{xy}=0$ (iv) $\mathrm{x} \sin \mathrm{y}=\mathrm{c}$

(ii) $\mathrm{y}=\sin ^{3} \mathrm{x}$

(i) $y=a x+b$
(ii) $\mathrm{y}^{2}=4 \mathrm{ax}$
(iii) $y=m x$
(iv) $\mathrm{y}=\mathrm{mx}+\frac{1}{\mathrm{~m}}$

(vi) $y=c x+c^{3}$

\section*{PART - B}
1. Find $\frac{d y}{d x}$ if
(i) $y=\operatorname{cosec}^{3}(5 x+1)$
(ii) $y=\tan \left(x^{2} \log x\right)$
(iii) $y=\cos \left[\frac{\log x}{x}\right]$
(iv) $y=e^{\cos ^{3} x}$
2. Find $\frac{d y}{d x}$ if
(i) $\mathrm{y}=\sqrt{\mathrm{x}} \tan ^{-1} \mathrm{x}$
(ii) $y=x^{3}+\tan ^{-1}\left(x^{2}\right)$
(iii) $\mathrm{y}=\left(\sin ^{-1} \mathrm{x}\right)^{2}$
(iv) $y=\cos ^{-1}\left(4 x^{3}-3 x\right)$
3. If $x^{2}-y^{2}=5 y-3 x$ find $\frac{d y}{d x}$.
4. If $y^{2}=x \sin y$ find $\frac{d y}{d x}$.
5. If $\sin y=x \sin (a+y)$ find $\frac{d y}{d x}$.
6. If $y=a e^{x}+b e^{-x}$ that $x \quad \frac{d^{2} y}{d x^{2}}+2 \frac{d y}{d x}=x y$.
7. If $y=\frac{\cos x}{x}$ prove that $x y_{2}+2 y_{1}+x y=0$.
8. If $u=x^{3}-2 x^{2} y+3 x y^{2}+y^{3}$ find $\frac{\partial^{2} u}{\partial x^{2}}$ and $\frac{\partial^{2} u}{\partial y^{2}}$.
9. If $u=x^{y}$ find $\frac{\partial u}{\partial x}, \frac{\partial^{2} u}{\partial x^{2}}$.
10. If $u=\sqrt{x^{2}+y^{2}}$ show that $x \frac{\partial u}{\partial x}+y \frac{\partial u}{\partial y}=u$.

\section*{PART - C}
1. Find $\frac{d y}{d x}$ if
(i) $\mathrm{y}=\mathrm{e}^{3 \mathrm{x}} \log \mathrm{x} \sin 2 \mathrm{x}$
(ii) $\mathrm{y}=\frac{1+\sin 2 \mathrm{x}}{1-\sin 2 \mathrm{x}}$
(iii) $y=\frac{\sin (\log x)}{x}$
(iv) $\left(3 \mathrm{x}^{2}-2\right)^{2} \cot \mathrm{x} \cdot \log \sin \mathrm{x}$.
2. Find $\frac{d y}{d x}$ if
(i) $y=\cos ^{-1}\left(\frac{1-x^{2}}{1+x^{2}}\right)$
(ii) $\mathrm{y}=\mathrm{x} \sin ^{-1}(\tan \mathrm{x})$
(iii) $y=\frac{\sin ^{-1} x}{\sqrt{1-x^{2}}}$
3. If $\mathrm{y}=\mathrm{x}^{2} \sin \mathrm{x}$ prove that $\mathrm{x}^{2} \mathrm{y}_{2}-4 \mathrm{x} \mathrm{y}_{1}+\left(x^{2}+6\right) \mathrm{y}=0$.
4. Verify that $\frac{\partial^{2} u}{\partial x \partial y}=\frac{\partial^{2} u}{\partial y \partial x}$ for the following functions:
(i) $u=\frac{x}{y^{2}}-\frac{y}{x^{2}}$
(ii) $u=x \sin y+y \sin x$
(iii) $u=\log \left(\frac{x^{2}+y^{2}}{x y}\right)$
5. If $u=x^{4}+4 x^{3} y+3 x^{2} y^{2}+y^{4}$ find $x^{2} \frac{\partial^{2} u}{\partial x^{2}}+y^{2} \frac{\partial^{2} u}{\partial y^{2}}$.
6. If $u=\log \left(x^{2}+y^{3}\right)$ show that $x \frac{\partial u}{\partial x}+y \frac{\partial u}{\partial y}=2$.

\section*{ANSWERS}

\section*{PART - A}
1.
(i) $6(2 x+5)^{2}$
(ii) $\frac{a}{\sqrt[2]{a x+b}}$
(iii) $2 \cos 2 x$
(iv) $-3 \cos ^{2} \mathrm{x} \sin \mathrm{x}$
(v) $10 \sin 5 \mathrm{x} \cos 5 \mathrm{x}$
(vi) $\frac{1}{2 \sqrt{\mathrm{x}}} \sec ^{2} \sqrt{\mathrm{x}}$
(vii) $-[\cos (\operatorname{cois} x)] \sin x$
(viii) $-\frac{1}{\mathrm{x}} \sin (\log \mathrm{x})$
(ix) $\frac{2}{2 x+3}$
(x) $2 x e^{x^{2}}$
2.
(i) $\frac{2}{\sqrt{1-4 x^{2}}}$
(ii) $-\frac{2 x}{\sqrt{1-4^{2}}}$
(iii) $\frac{1}{2 \sqrt{x}(1+x)}$
(iv) $\frac{-\mathrm{e}^{\mathrm{x}}}{\sqrt{1-\mathrm{e}^{2 \mathrm{x}}}}$
3.
(i) $\frac{d y}{d x}=\frac{2 a}{y}$
(ii) $\frac{d y}{d x}=\frac{2 x}{y}$
(iii) $\frac{-\left(3 x^{2}+y\right)}{x}$
(iv) $\frac{-\tan y}{x}$
4.
(i) $40 x^{3}-8$
(ii) $3 \sin \mathrm{x}\left[2 \cos ^{2} \mathrm{x}-\sin ^{2} \mathrm{x}\right]$
(iii) $-\cos x$
5.
(i) $\frac{d^{2} y}{d x^{2}}=0$
(ii) $y^{2}=2 x y \frac{d y}{d x}$
(iii) $y=x \frac{d y}{d x}$
(iv) $y=x \frac{d y}{d x}+\frac{d x}{d y}$
(v) $x+y \frac{d y}{d x}=0$
(vi) $y=x \frac{d y}{d x}+\left(\frac{d y}{d x}\right)^{3}$
6. $3 x^{2}+10 x y, 5 x^{2}+3 y^{2}$
8. $2 x \mathrm{e}^{x^{2}+y^{2}}, 2 \mathrm{y}^{\mathrm{x}^{2}+y^{2}}$
9. $a \sec ^{2}(a x+b y)$

\section*{PART - B}
1.
(i) $15 \operatorname{cosec}^{3}(5 x+1) \cot (5 x+1)$
(ii) $x(1+2 \log x) \sec ^{2}\left(x^{2} \log x\right)$
(iii) $\frac{-(1+\log x)}{x^{2}} \sin \left(\frac{\log x}{x}\right)$
(iv) $-3 \cos ^{2} x \sin x e^{\cos ^{3} x}$
2.
(i) $\frac{1}{2 \sqrt{\mathrm{x}}} \tan ^{-1} \mathrm{x}+\frac{\sqrt{\mathrm{x}}}{1+\mathrm{x}^{2}}$
(ii) $3 \mathrm{x}^{2}+\frac{2 \mathrm{x}}{1+\mathrm{x}^{4}}$
(iii) $\frac{2 \sin ^{-1} \mathrm{x}}{\sqrt{1-\mathrm{x}^{2}}}$
(iv) $\frac{-3\left(4 x^{2}-1\right)}{\sqrt{1-\left(4 x^{3}-3 x\right)^{2}}}$
3. $\frac{2 x+3}{2 y+5}$
4. $\frac{\sin y}{2 y-x \cos y}$
5. $\frac{\sin (a+y)}{\cos y-x \cos (a+y)}$
8. $6 x-4 y, 6 x+6 y$
9. $y x^{y-1}, y(y-1) x^{y-2}$

\section*{PART - C}
1. (i) $e^{3 x}\left[2 \log x \cos 2 x+3 \log x \sin 2 x+\frac{\sin 2 x}{x}\right]$
(ii) $\frac{4 \cos 2 x}{(1-\sin 2 x)^{2}}$
(iii) $\frac{\cos (\log x)-\sin (\log x)}{x^{2}}$
(iv) $12 x\left(3 x^{2}-2\right) \cot x \log (\sin x)+\left(3 x^{2}-2\right)^{2} \cot ^{2} x-\left(3 x^{2}-2\right) \log (\sin x) \operatorname{cosec}^{2} x$
2.
(i) $\frac{2}{1+x^{2}}$
(ii) $\frac{x \sec ^{2} x}{\sqrt{1-\tan ^{2} x}}$
(iii) $\frac{\sqrt{1-x^{2}}-x \sin ^{-1} x}{\left(1-x^{2}\right)^{3 / 2}}$
10. $6\left(2 x^{4}+4 x^{3} y+2 x^{2} y^{2}-x y^{3}+2 y^{4}\right)$
